1 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Heck Van Tran v. State


No. W1998-00175-SC-R11-PD


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT JACKSON


6 S.W.3d 257; 1999 Tenn. LEXIS 602



November 23, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied April 24, 2000, Reported at: 2000 U.S. LEXIS 2938.



DISPOSITION:  [**1] AFFIRMED AS MODIFIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals (Tennessee), holding that a proceeding for post-conviction relief was not the appropriate avenue for litigating the issue of competency to be executed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed from a judgment holding that a proceeding for post-conviction relief was not the appropriate avenue for litigating the issue of competency to be executed. The court agreed and determined that that there currently was no Tennessee statute that contained a procedure for litigating the issue of present competency. The court proceeded to exercise its inherent supervisory authority and herein adopted and set forth the procedure that a prisoner sentenced to death must follow in order to assert his or her common law and constitutional rights to challenge competency to be executed. The court further held that under this procedure defendant's claim that he was incompetent to be executed was not ripe for resolution.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed. Defendant's claim that he was incompetent to be executed was not ripe for resolution.

 

2 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Momon v. State


No. E1996-00007-SC-R11-PC


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, EASTERN SECTION, AT KNOXVILLE


18 S.W.3d 152; 1999 Tenn. LEXIS 581



November 15, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Granted March 30, 2000, Reported at: 2000 Tenn. LEXIS 153.


PRIOR HISTORY: HAMILTON CRIMINAL. HON. STEPHEN M. BEVIL, JUDGE. (Post Conviction).



DISPOSITION: TRIAL COURT AND COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS REVERSED, CASE REMANDED TO TRIAL COURT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant requested permission to appeal a Court of Criminal Appeals (Tennessee) decision upholding his conviction despite defendant's claim that he was denied effective assistance of counsel when his trial counsel failed to allow him to testify at his own trial.


OVERVIEW: At the trial, defendant's counsel failed to allow defendant to testify and unilaterally waived his right. Defendant's post-conviction relief petition claiming ineffective assistance of counsel was dismissed. After the intermediate court's affirmance, defendant appealed. The court held that a criminal defendant's right to testify was a fundamental constitution right guaranteed both by Tenn. Const. art. I, § 9 and U.S. Const. amend. V and XIV, and could only be personally waived. The court determined that defendant was denied his right to testify and remanded the case to the trial court for a hearing to determine whether the error was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt. If the State failed to meet its burden on remand, the trial court was directed to vacate the conviction.


OUTCOME: After holding that defendant was denied his fundamental right to testify when trial counsel unilaterally waived his right, the court remanded the case to the trial court for a hearing at which the State bore the burden of demonstrating that the error was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt.

 

3 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Tennessee Baptist Children's Homes, Inc. v. Swanson (In re Swanson)


Supreme Court No. 02S01-9810-CV-00103


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT JACKSON


2 S.W.3d 180; 1999 Tenn. LEXIS 475



October 4, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] CIRCUIT COURT. TIPTON COUNTY. Hon. Joe H. Walker, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father challenged decision of the Tennessee Court of Appeals granting appellee children's home's petition for termination of appellant's parental rights over his biological child in custody of appellee for willfully failing to support her or willfully failing to make reasonable payments towards her support pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-1-102(1)(D) (1996 & Supp. 1998).


OVERVIEW: Appellant father's child was placed in the legal custody of the Tennessee Department of Human Services (DHS) after a dependency and neglect determination was made, whereby the child resided in foster care through placement by appellee children's home. The DHS received no support for the child from her appellant and was told by her mother that appellant was deceased. Appellee filed a petition for legal custody of the child. The county juvenile court terminated appellant's parental rights. The county circuit court denied the petition to terminate appellant's parental rights on appeal, which decision was reversed by the appellate court pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-1-102(1)(D) (1996 & Supp. 1998). Appellant sought review of the termination of parental rights. The court reversed the judgment and remanded the case for preparation and implementation of a plan returning the child to appellant. Appellant's constitutional right to care and custody of his child was violated by unconstitutional statutory definitions creating an irrebuttable presumption that his failure to support the child constituted abandonment, irrespective of whether that failure was intentional.


OUTCOME: Judgment was reversed and case remanded for reinstatement of appellant's parental rights. Unconstitutional definitions in the applicable statute created irrebuttable presumption that appellant's failure to provide monetary support for four months preceding petition to terminate parental rights constituted abandonment, irrespective of whether failure was intentional, violating appellant's constitutional right to care and custody of his child.

 

4 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Hathaway v. First Family Fin. Servs.


NO. 01S01-9811-FD-00203


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1 S.W.3d 634; 1999 Tenn. LEXIS 408



August 30, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Certified Questions of Law from the United States District Court for the Middle District of Tennessee. (John T. Nixon, Judge).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court accepted two certified questions of law from the United States District Court for the Middle District of Tennessee with regard to industrial loan and thrift company charges assessed against plaintiff borrowers, and remedies for defendant lender's violation of limitations on loan charges and interest rates imposed by the Industrial Loan and Thrift Company Act, § 45-5-101 et seq.


OVERVIEW: The court accepted certification of two questions from a federal district court concerning the amount of a service charge that defendant industrial loan and thrift company could lawfully impose and, with respect to a violation thereof, whether plaintiff borrowers' remedies were limited to the general statute pertaining to interest and other charges by lenders. As to the first question, the court opined that the amount that could be charged was that portion of the refinancing loan that was used to pay all or any part of the initial loan. As to the second question, the court held that plaintiff borrowers' remedies for a violation of the limitations on loan charges and interest rates imposed by the Industrial Loan and Thrift Company Act, Tenn. Code Ann. § 45-5-101 et seq., were limited to the remedies prescribed by the general statutes pertaining to interest and other charges by lenders.


OUTCOME: The certified questions from the federal district court were answered in the affirmative: defendant lender's permissible charges were limited to the amount of money it took to pay all or part of the initial loan and, in the event of a violation, plaintiff borrowers' remedy was limited.

 

5 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


McIlvain v. Russell Stover Candies


NO. 01-S-01-9709-CH-00208


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


996 S.W.2d 179; 1999 Tenn. LEXIS 365



July 19, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 19, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: CHANCERY COURT. PUTNAM COUNTY. HON. VERNON NEAL, CHANCELLOR.



DISPOSITION: WORKERS' COMPENSATION SPECIAL APPEALS PANEL AFFIRMED, AS MODIFIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant employer appealed a judgment from the Workers' Compensation Special Appeals Panel (Tennessee), which affirmed a finding of permanent partial disability for plaintiff employee, and held that an award to a worker over age 60 based on injury to scheduled members was subject to a cap of 260 weeks of benefits under Tenn. Code Ann. § 50-6-207(4)(A)(i) (1991 & Supp. 1998).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff employee, who was over 60, obtained an award of 160 weeks benefits for carpal tunnel syndrome that caused permanent partial disability of 40 percent to scheduled members. The Worker's Compensation Special Appeals Panel affirmed the award, but held that the age-based classification of Tenn. Code Ann. § 50-6-207(4)(A)(i) (1991 & Supp. 1998) placed a 260 week cap on an award to an over-60 worker who suffered injury to a scheduled member. Holding that the weight of the evidence did not preponderate against the award, and that § 50-6-207(4)(A)(i) was applicable only to injuries to the body as a whole, the court affirmed the judgment as modified. The court held that the testimony of plaintiff, her husband, and three experts preponderated against the testimony of an expert who found no disability yet advised plaintiff to seek non-repetitive work. The court also held a surveillance tape of plaintiff unpersuasive, since it did not show her engaging in repetitive work. The court held that § 50-6-207(4)(A)(i) did not reduce an award based on injury to a scheduled member, though it did note that this meant that the law reduced awards to the arguably more seriously injured only.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment for plaintiff employee, as the evidence did not preponderate against the award, but the court modified that portion of the lower court's opinion that held an age-based classification was applicable to over-60 workers who suffered injury to a scheduled member, and instead held that such classification was only applicable to injury to the body as a whole.

 

6 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Ramsey v. Town of Oliver Springs


NO. 03-S-01-9807-CH-00073


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, EASTERN SECTION, AT KNOXVILLE


998 S.W.2d 207; 1999 Tenn. LEXIS 366



July 19, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 19, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: CHANCERY COURT. ROANE COUNTY. HON. FRANK V. WILLIAMS, III,. CHANCELLOR.



DISPOSITION: COURT OF APPEALS AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of the decision of the Chancery Court, Roane County (Tennessee), which held that appellants could not adjudicate a criminal case where the offense was committed in a county for which appellee was the district attorney general.


OVERVIEW: Appellee district attorney general for county brought a declaratory judgment action against appellants town for a determination that appellants' policy and practice of prosecuting appellee's county's cases in appellants town was illegal. Portions of appellants town were located in three different counties, including appellee's county, but the city court was not located in appellee's town. The court affirmed lower court's finding that that appellants' application of Tenn. Priv. Acts, ch. 137, § 1 (1994), impeded appellee's duty to prosecute crimes committed in his county. While Tenn. Priv. Acts, ch. 137, § 1 (1994) granted appellants concurrent jurisdiction with courts of general sessions for violations of criminal laws, the court found that only appellee as district attorney general had the power to decide whether to proceed with a prosecution for an offense committed within his district. Because appellants' policy of prosecuting those who had committed crimes in appellee's district impeded appellee's constitutional and statutory obligation under Tenn. Const. art. VI, § 5, to discharge the duties of his office, the court affirmed the lower court's judgment in favor of appellee.


OUTCOME: Judgment of lower court that appellants' attempts to prosecute crimes occurring in different county improperly impeded appellee's duties of determining whether or not to prosecute those crimes occurring within his jurisdiction was affirmed.

 

7 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


State v. Middlebrooks


NO. 01S01-9802-CR-00017


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


995 S.W.2d 550; 1999 Tenn. LEXIS 351



July 6, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] CRIMINAL COURT. DAVIDSON COUNTY. HON. ANN LACY JOHNS, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a decision of the Court of Criminal Appeals (Tennessee), which affirmed the death sentence imposed by a lower court for first degree murder, based upon aggravating circumstances under Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-2-203(i) (1982) (codified in Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-204(i), 1997 & Supp. 1998), in an action by appellee State of Tennessee.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, his girlfriend, and an associate tortured and brutalized a young boy prior to killing him. Appellant was convicted of felony murder and sentenced to death based upon the jury's finding of aggravating circumstances under Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-2-203(i) (1982) (codified in Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-204(i), 1997 & Supp. 1998), namely, that the murder was especially heinous, atrocious, or cruel in that it involved torture or depravity of mind and that the murder was perpetrated during the commission of a felony. At a resentencing hearing, appellant was again sentenced to death, and the appellate court affirmed the decision of the resentencing court. On automatic appeal to the state supreme court, the appellate court's decision was affirmed. The court reasoned that although the prosecutor improperly made a statement concerning the victim's family and improperly used biblical references during his closing, the errors did not require reversal. The court noted that the cumulative effect of the improper conduct was far outweighed by the strength of the evidence that supported the jury's finding that the aggravating circumstance outweighed proof of any mitigating factors.


OUTCOME: The decision that affirmed the imposition of the death penalty against appellant was affirmed. The court found that after reviewing the record, the appellate court's decision, the issues raised, and the applicable law, none of the alleged errors affected the sentence imposed by the jury. Moreover, the evidence supported the jury's sentence of death, and the sentence was not disproportionate or arbitrary as applied to appellant.

 

8 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Strouth v. State


No. 03S01-9707-CC-00079


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, EASTERN SECTION, AT KNOXVILLE


999 S.W.2d 759; 1999 Tenn. LEXIS 346



June 28, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Strouth v. State, 2002 Tenn. LEXIS 480 (Tenn. October 28, 2002).
Certiorari Denied March 20, 2000, Reported at: 2000 U.S. LEXIS 2036
. Petition for Rehearing Denied September 7, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Tenn. LEXIS 423.
Rehearing denied by Strouth v. State, 1999 Tenn. LEXIS 423 (Tenn., Sept. 7, 1999)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Strouth v. Bell, 2008 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 109144 (M.D. Tenn., Feb. 4, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] CRIMINAL COURT. SULLIVAN COUNTY. Hon. Frank L. Slaughter, Judge.
Strouth v. State, 1997 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 210 (Tenn. Crim. App., Mar. 4, 1997)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals (Tennessee), which affirmed the dismissal of defendant's petition for post-conviction relief. Defendant argued his death sentence should have been thrown out because the jury considered an invalid felony murder aggravating circumstance when it sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's first-degree felony murder conviction and death sentence were affirmed on direct appeal. Defendant filed a post-conviction petition, arguing that his death sentence should be set aside because the jury relied on an invalid felony murder aggravating circumstance when it sentenced defendant to death. The court of appeals affirmed the trial court's dismissal of defendant's petition. The court affirmed. The error was harmless because the court was convinced beyond a reasonable doubt that the sentence would have been the same had the jury not considered the invalid aggravating circumstance. The prosecutor did not emphasize the invalid aggravating circumstance in his closing argument. The remaining aggravating circumstance, that the murder was especially heinous because it involved depravity of mind, was supported by an abundance of proof that was qualitatively persuasive. The evidence in the record that defendant slashed his victim's throat from ear to ear and almost decapitated him when the victim was already unconscious overwhelmingly established the applicability of this aggravating circumstance. Defendant also presented very little mitigating evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of defendant's post-conviction petition. Even though a jury relied on an invalid felony murder aggravating circumstance when it sentenced defendant to death, this error was harmless because the court found that beyond a reasonable doubt the sentence would have been the same had the jury not considered the invalid aggravating circumstance.

 

9 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Taylor v. State


Supreme Court No. 02S01-9806-CR-00054


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT JACKSON (HEARD AT SAVANNAH)


995 S.W.2d 78; 1999 Tenn. LEXIS 324



June 21, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Certiorari Denied October 4, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 6457.


PRIOR HISTORY: SHELBY COUNTY. Hon. Chris B. Craft, Judge. Hon. Joe B. Brown, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS AFFIRMED AS TO TAYLOR; REVERSED AS TO GWIN; POST-CONVICTION PETITIONS DISMISSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated appeal, petitioners sought review of judgments of the Court of Criminal Appeals (Tennessee) on the grounds that sentences imposed under a statute that was subsequently declared unconstitutional constituted an illegal sentence that was void and, thus, could be challenged without regard to post-conviction statute of limitations.


OVERVIEW: Following convictions for first degree murder in the perpetration of felonies, petitioners sought review on the grounds that their sentences, which were imposed under a statute that was subsequently declared unconstitutional, constituted an illegal sentence that was void and could be challenged and corrected without regard to post conviction statute of limitations. In a consolidated appeal, the court affirmed the sentences, holding that the sentences were voidable, rather than void. The court explained that a sentence was void and illegal only if it was in direct contravention of the statute that was in existence at the time the sentence was imposed. Petitioners' sentences, however, were in accordance with the statute and, thus were voidable only if timely challenged in a post-conviction proceeding. Since the petitions were filed beyond the applicable three-year post conviction statute of limitations, the trial courts properly dismissed the petitions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments of conviction and sentences imposed against petitioner criminal defendants, holding that sentences imposed in accordance with a statute in effect at the time of its imposition was not void merely because the statute was later declared unconstitutional.

 

10 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


State v. Smith


Supreme Court No. 03-S-01-9710-CC-00129


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, EASTERN SECTION, AT KNOXVILLE


993 S.W.2d 6; 1999 Tenn. LEXIS 269



May 17, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Certiorari Denied November 29, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 7841.
Writ of certiorari denied Smith v. Tennessee, 528 U.S. 1023, 120 S. Ct. 536, 145 L. Ed. 2d 415, 1999 U.S. LEXIS 7841 (1999)
Application denied by Smith v. State, 2003 Tenn. LEXIS 496 (Tenn., May 27, 2003)
Post-conviction relief denied at, in part, Post-conviction proceeding at, Remanded by Smith v. State, 2010 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 793 (Tenn. Crim. App., Sept. 21, 2010)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Dismissed by, Certificate of appealability denied Smith v. Westbrooks, 2016 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 135626 (E.D. Tenn., Sept. 30, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY: Hamblen County. Hon. Lynn W. Brown, Judge.
State v. Smith, 1997 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 996 (Tenn. Crim. App., Oct. 3, 1997)



DISPOSITION: TRIAL COURT AND COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Tennessee Court of Criminal Appeals, which affirmed his death sentence for a conviction of first-degree felony murder. The defendant challenged the trial court's decision to allow the defendant to control the presentation of mitigating evidence. Defendant also alleged error in the admission of victim impact testimony and asserted that the sentence of death was arbitrary and disproportionate.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of two counts of first-degree felony murder in separate trials after he participated in two convenience store robberies that resulted in the death of two store clerks. The defendant received a life sentence in one case and was sentenced to death in the other case. Defendant's appeal was automatic under Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-206(a)(1). The defendant alleged that the trial court erred in permitting the defendant to control the presentation of mitigating evidence; that the trial court erred in admitting victim impact testimony; and that the sentencing was disproportionate. The appellate court held that ultimately, the defense belonged to the defendant and the defendant could choose what evidence to present. The court found that the victim impact testimony was not unfairly prejudicial to the defendant. The court also found that the defendant's death sentence was not disproportionate to other cases with similar circumstances, even though the defendant received a life sentence for the other murder for which he was convicted. The court therefore affirmed the defendant's sentence.


OUTCOME: The court found no merit to any of the defendant's arguments and affirmed his sentence. The court found that the defendant had the authority to control the presentation of evidence in his defense; that the admittance of victim impact testimony was not unfairly prejudicial; and that the sentence was not disproportionate compared to other similar cases.

 

11 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Foster v. Carolina Freight Carriers Corp.


No. 02S01-9802-CV-00013


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, SPECIAL WORKERS' COMPENSATION APPEALS PANEL, AT JACKSON


1999 Tenn. LEXIS 257



April 23, 1999, Filed


NOTICE: CONSULT THE TENNESSEE SUPREME COURT RULES FOR CITATION OF UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Judgment Order of April 23, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Tenn. LEXIS 254.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Shelby Circuit. Honorable Robert A. Lanier, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review from the Shelby Circuit Court (Tennessee), which found that appellee sustained a permanent partial disability in the amount of 30 percent to the body as a whole as a result of appellee's second accident superimposed upon the disability from appellee's first accident.


OVERVIEW: Appellee reached a workers' compensation settlement with appellant after his first injury. Settlement was based on a 36 percent permanent partial disability (PPD) to the body as a whole. Appellee suffered a second injury. The trial court based its award on the mistaken belief that in appellee's first injury he suffered a 17 percent PPD. The trial court concluded that appellee suffered a 30 percent PPD between both injuries. The court reversed and remanded. Appellant's position that it was entitled to a credit against the first disability award under Tenn. Code Ann. § 50-6-207(3)(F) was erroneous based on Tennessee Supreme Court precedent. The trial court erred by awarding appellee benefits based upon appellee's total disability from both injuries. According to a recent Tennessee Supreme Court case, Tenn. Code Ann. § 50-6-207(3)(F) authorized compensation for the degree of permanent disability that resulted from the second injury only. The evidence supported a conclusion that appellee suffered a residual disability from the second injury. The court remanded for a determination of appellee's PPD rating as to the second accident.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the trial court's decision, finding that the trial court erred when it awarded appellee a recovery for his second injury based on appellee's total disability from both injuries because Tennessee Supreme Court analysis of the applicable statutory provision made clear that compensation should have been paid only for the degree of permanent disability from the second injury.

 

12 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Helms v. Tennessee Dep't of Safety


01S01-9709-CH-00185


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


987 S.W.2d 545; 1999 Tenn. LEXIS 229



April 12, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 987 S.W.2d 545 at 549. Released for Publication April 12, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: DAVIDSON COUNTY. CHANCERY COURT.

Original Opinion of January 25, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Tenn. LEXIS 42.



DISPOSITION: Petition to rehear respectfully overruled.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought a rehearing of his appeal of a judgment from the Davidson County Chancery Court (Tennessee) holding that the Tennessee statutes governing the forfeiture of personal property were constitutional. Appellant reargued that the personal property forfeiture statutes violated the constitution because they omitted the right to a jury trial.


OVERVIEW: The court overruled a petition to rehear appellant's case in which he argued that the state statutes governing the forfeiture of personal property were unconstitutional because they omitted the right to a jury trial. The acts of the general assembly were presumed to be constitutional, and defendant failed to overcome the heavy burden of overcoming that presumption. Review of the common law right to a jury trial required looking to the English common law of North Carolina, adopted by Tennessee in 1796. Nevertheless, appellant's proof of a colonial North Carolina statute which established jury trial proceedings in slave forfeiture cases was unpersuasive because statutory law was separate from common law. Accordingly, the court respectfully overruled appellant's petition to rehear.


OUTCOME: The court denied the petition to rehear appellant's case in which he contended that the personal property forfeiture statutes were unconstitutional by omitting the right to a jury trial. The North Carolina colonial statute cited by appellant failed to convince the court because statutory law was separate from common law, and defendant's claim was based on a common law right to a jury trial.

 

13 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


State v. Harris


Supreme Court No. 02-S01-9806-CC-00053


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT JACKSON


989 S.W.2d 307; 1999 Tenn. LEXIS 230



April 12, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] The Name of this Case has been Corrected by the Court April 19, 1999, Released for Publication April 12, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: HENRY COUNTY. Hon. Julian P. Guinn, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order from the Henry County Court of Criminal Appeals (Tennessee), in which the court affirmed defendant's sentence of life imprisonment without the possibility of parole following her conviction for felony murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sentenced to life imprisonment without the possibility of parole following her conviction for felony murder. Defendant appealed, asserting that the jury's incomplete verdict as to one of the mitigating factors of the death penalty statute contained in Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-204(i)(5) constituted constitutional error. The appellate court rejected defendant's assertion, holding that the error was not constitutional error and that the error was harmless. According to the supreme court, the constitutional error standard was inapplicable in defendant's case because defendant was actually sentenced to life imprisonment and not death. The supreme court affirmed, holding that the constitutional error standard did not apply outside the death penalty context. The applicable standard was whether the jury grossly abused its discretion by arbitrarily imposing sentence. The court held that this standard was applicable where the sentence was based in part on at least one valid aggravating factor. The court concluded that the jury's reliance on an invalid aggravating factor was harmless error because one valid aggravating circumstance remained to support defendant's sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's sentence of life imprisonment without the possibility of parole because the jury's incomplete verdict regarding the aggravating factors of the death penalty statute was not constitutional error where another valid aggravating circumstance supported the sentence. Thus, the jury did not abuse its discretion in imposing sentence.

 

14 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Helms v. Tennessee Dep't of Safety


No. 01S01-9709-CH-00185


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


987 S.W.2d 545; 1999 Tenn. LEXIS 42



January 25, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Chancery Court. Davidson County. Hon. Irvin H. Kilcrease, Jr., Chancellor. (Civil Forfeiture).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed from the Court of Appeals (Tennessee) which affirmed the trial court's decision that plaintiff was not entitled to a jury trial regarding his property that was forfeited.


OVERVIEW: The police seized cocaine and other drug paraphernalia from plaintiff's residence. The court issued an ex parte order of seizure, requiring a bank to freeze money in plaintiff's bank accounts. The trial court found probable cause to believe the money was traceable to plaintiff's alleged illegal drug trade and found the money was subject to forfeiture under Tenn. Code Ann. § 53-11-451 (1992). The court directed the bank to surrender the money to the police, which the bank did. Plaintiff did not file a timely claim for the money, and it was forfeited without an administrative hearing. Plaintiff requested the Commissioner of Safety to reconsider the forfeiture order and to provide a hearing on the merits. The request was denied, and plaintiff filed a petition for review, arguing he was denied the right to a jury trial in violation of the Tennessee Constitution. In a bench trial, the chancery court upheld the forfeiture, and the court of appeals affirmed. On appeal, the court affirmed the holding that plaintiff was not entitled to a jury trial, finding in Tennessee that there was no right to a jury trial in statutory proceedings involving the forfeiture of personal property.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court and court of appeals, finding that plaintiff was not entitled to a jury trial because Tennessee did not provide a right to a jury trial in statutory proceedings involving the forfeiture of personal property.

 

15 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


DeLaney v. Thompson


S. Ct. No. 01S01-9808-CH-00144


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


982 S.W.2d 857; 1998 Tenn. LEXIS 748



December 21, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Chancery Court. Davidson County. Hon. Ellen Hobbs Lyle, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of Court of Appeals and Trial Court Reversed; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff judicial candidate sued defendant, the Tennessee State Coordinator of Elections, to enjoin him from placing the names of incumbent judges on the ballot on a retention election basis. The trial court granted the injunction, but the Tennessee Court of Appeal reversed. The candidate sought further review.


OVERVIEW: The appellate judge advised the judicial evaluation commission that he would not run for reelection. Before the commission issued its report about retention of incumbents, the candidate asked the coordinator for a nominating petition to run for the court of appeals. The coordinator declined to issue a petition until he learned if the commission did not recommend retaining one or more of the incumbents. At that time, such positions would be considered contested offices, and the coordinator would issue petitions to any interested persons. The candidate sued before the commission issued its report, which did not recommend retaining the incumbent. The trial court granted the candidate an injunction on grounds that the Tennessee Plan, Tenn. Code Ann. tit. 17, ch. 4, was unconstitutional. The court of appeals reversed, ruling that the plan was constitutional. The instant court held that the lower courts erred in considering the plan's constitutionality, as by its terms it was inapplicable to the controversy. The plan was applicable only when an incumbent judge whose retention was recommended by the commission failed to file a declaration of candidacy or withdrew as a candidate.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded.

 

16 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


City of White House v. Whitley


Supreme Court No. 01S01-9711-CH-00259


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE, (HEARD AT SHELBYVILLE)


979 S.W.2d 262; 1998 Tenn. LEXIS 573



October 12, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Chancery Court. Sumner County. Hon. Tom E. Gray, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: COURT OF APPEALS AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Court of Appeals (Tennessee) reversed the trial court's judgment that neither the state constitution nor its statutes required municipal judges to be licensed to practice law in an action by appellant city against appellee district attorneys general. The city challenged the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The city passed an ordinance establishing a municipal court, but did not require the municipal judge to be licensed to practice law in the state. The district attorneys general argued that non-attorney judges could not preside over hearings where the defendants faced the possibility of incarceration. The court affirmed the judgment that municipal judges must be licensed to practice law if they presided over trials for defendants who might be incarcerated. A criminal defendant had a constitutional right to representation by a legally qualified attorney. To require a lesser standard of a judge presiding over the trial of a criminal offense punishable by incarceration would defeat the constitutional purpose of the right to counsel. The failure to provide a judge qualified to comprehend and utilize counsel's legal arguments was a denial of due process. The due process protections of Tenn. Const. art. I, § 8 guaranteed to a criminal defendant on trial for an offense punishable by incarceration the right to be tried before an attorney judge.


OUTCOME: The judgment that municipal judges who presided over a trial for an offense punishable by incarceration must be required to be licensed to practice law was affirmed.

OVERVIEW: Defendants sought review of the appellate court's reversal of the trial court's grant of defendants' motion to suppress evidence obtained in an initial investigative automobile stop and subsequently by search warrant. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's judgment which reversed the trial court's grant of defendants' motion to suppress, and remanded the matter to the trial court for further proceedings.

State v. Vann


Supreme Court No. 03-S01-9706-CR-00068


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, EASTERN SECTION, AT KNOXVILLE


976 S.W.2d 93; 1998 Tenn. LEXIS 513



September 21, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied April 19, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 2664. Petition for Rehearing Denied October 19, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Tenn. LEXIS 580.
Rehearing denied by State v. Vann, 1998 Tenn. LEXIS 580 (Tenn., Oct. 19, 1998)
Writ of certiorari denied Vann v. Tennessee, 526 U.S. 1071, 119 S. Ct. 1467, 143 L. Ed. 2d 551, 1999 U.S. LEXIS 2664 (1999)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Criminal Court. McMinn County. Hon. R. Steven Bebb, Judge.
State v. Vann, 1997 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 551 (Tenn. Crim. App., June 10, 1997)



DISPOSITION: TRIAL COURT AND COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment form the Court of Criminal Appeals (Tennessee) affirming the conviction and sentence of the trial court. Appellant was convicted of first degree felony murder in the perpetration of aggravated rape and two counts of incest; appellant was sentenced to death by electroexecution.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of first degree felony murder in the perpetration of aggravated rape and two counts of incest. The jury found three aggravating circumstances, that the murder was committed against a person younger than twelve, appellant was previously convicted for a crime involving the use of violence on a person, and the murder was especially heinous, atrocious, or cruel in that it involved torture or serious physical abuse beyond that necessary to produce death. Appellant was sentenced to death. The lower appellate court affirmed. On further appeal, the court affirmed the convictions and sentence of the trial court. The court rejected eleven claims of error and held jury instructions were proper and other crimes evidence was admissible under Tenn. R. Evid. 404(b). The court ruled evidence was not obtained from an illegal search of appellant's home and was admissible, the element of mens rea for the incest charges could logically have been inferred in the indictment, and that the jury's finding of aggravating circumstances outweighed mitigating circumstances beyond a reasonable doubt. The court also held that the sentence was not disproportionate to the crimes committed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower appellate court. Jury instructions were proper, evidence of other crimes was admissible, a search of appellant's home was not unconstitutional, aggravating circumstances outweighed other circumstances, the indictment was not insufficient for failure to allege requisite mental state, and the punishment was not disproportionate.

976 S.W.2d 121; 1998 Tenn. LEXIS 514

Writ of certiorari denied Hall v. Tennessee, 526 U.S. 1089, 119 S. Ct. 1501, 143 L. Ed. 2d 654, 1999 U.S. LEXIS 2893 (1999)
Post-conviction relief denied at, Decision reached on appeal by Quintero v. State, 2008 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 597 (Tenn. Crim. App., July 7, 2008)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Motion granted by, in part, Motion denied by, in part Quintero v. Bell, 2012 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 175992 (M.D. Tenn., Dec. 12, 2012)
Post-conviction relief denied at State v. Hall, 2013 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 920 (Tenn. Crim. App., Oct. 22, 2013)

State v. Hall, 1997 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 206 (Tenn. Crim. App., Mar. 5, 1997)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were convicted for two counts of murder during the perpetration of first degree burglary, three counts of grand larceny, one count of petit larceny and three counts of first degree burglary and sentenced to death for one of the murders. The Court of Criminal Appeals (Tennessee) affirmed but determined that two aggravating circumstances were inapplicable, but the application was harmless. The death sentence was automatically reviewed.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were convicted for two counts of murder during the perpetration of first degree burglary, three counts of grand larceny, one count of petit larceny and three counts of first degree burglary and sentenced to death for one of the murders. The court of criminal appeals affirmed the judgment after merging the petit larceny convictions with the grand larceny convictions but determined that two aggravating circumstances were inapplicable, but in light of the other aggravating circumstances the error in application was harmless. The court affirmed the convictions and the sentence of death. The court did reverse the determination that Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-2-203(i)(6) (1982) was inapplicable because the court determined that the ability to identify a murderer was not a requirement for the aggravating circumstance. The court determined that because the murders were committed during the process of an escape, Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-2-203 (i)(8) (1982) was properly applied. The court determined from a proportionality review that the penalty imposed by the jury in this case was not disproportionate to the penalty imposed for similar crimes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment upholding defendants' convictions and sentences of death by electrocution because the court determined that there were adequate aggravating circumstances to support the death penalty and the imposition was proportional to other crimes of similar nature. The court modified the judgment to restore the aggravating factor that related to murder to avoid identification.

Memphis Publ'g Co. v. Tennessee Petroleum Underground Storage Tank Bd.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


975 S.W.2d 303; 1998 Tenn. LEXIS 465



August 31, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Chancery Court. Davidson County. Hon. Irvin H. Kilcrease, Jr., Chancellor. NO. 01S01-9710-CH-00232.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, state petroleum underground storage tank board and commissioner of the state department of environment and conservation (board), appealed an judgment of the Court of Appeals (Tennessee), which affirmed a lower court's finding that the law of the cases doctrine bar them from reasserting that plaintiff publishing company had no right to reimbursement under the Tennessee Petroleum Underground Storage Tank Act of 1988 (Act).


OVERVIEW: The publishing company sought reimbursement for costs associated with a leak from an underground tank pursuant to the Act, which became effective on July 1, 1988. The spill took place prior to July 1, 1988. The chancery court affirmed the board's decision that a 1990 amendment to the Act, which made the Act not applicable to spills that took place prior to July 1988, barred the action. The court of appeals reversed, concluding that prior to the amendment the Act provide reimbursement for all releases regardless of date. The highest court denied the application for permission to appeal from the judgment of the court of appeals, concurring in results only. Upon remand the board attempted to assert again that the Act barred reimbursement. The publishing company asserted that the court of appeals opinion established the law of the case on remand. The chancery court agreed. The board's appealed was rejected. The instant court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court finding that law of the case doctrine applied on remand to issues implicitly decided by the appellate court as the instant court denied permission to appeal from that decision, but concurred in the results.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the chancellor and the court of appeals was affirmed in favor of the publishing company, and against the board, in an action seeking reimbursement pursuant to the Act.

 

21 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


State v. King


NO. 02-S-01-9703-CR-00021


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT JACKSON


973 S.W.2d 586; 1998 Tenn. LEXIS 424



July 6, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] SHELBY COUNTY. HON. JOSEPH B. DAILEY, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was indicted for aggravated burglary in Shelby County (Tennessee). The State filed a notice of intent to seek enhanced punishment because defendant was a persistent offender. The trial court granted the motion and defendant's motion to instruct on the range of punishment for aggravated burglary and all lesser included offenses, but denied his request that it refrain from instructing on parole eligibility. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-35-201(b)(2) violated two constitutional principles: separation of powers and due process. Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-35-201(b)(1) providing for a range of punishment instruction when requested, which the State requested, was a proper exercise of the legislative function. The addition of information on the shortest length of time defendant might serve was merely a refinement on it. The statute constituted an overlap of legislative and judiciary powers. However, the jury still was to decide guilt or innocence, and the trial court was still to decide the ultimate sentence. Therefore, the appellate court concluded Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-35-201(b)(2) did not violate the Separation of Powers Clauses of the Constitution, and Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-35-201(b)(2) sufficiently overcame any allegation of vagueness. The jurors were properly instructed that the State had to prove each element of the offense beyond a reasonable doubt, they were not to attempt to fix punishment, the sentencing information was for their information only. No due process violation had occurred.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State ex rel. Earhart v. City of Bristol


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


970 S.W.2d 948; 1998 Tenn. LEXIS 366



June 22, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 27, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Chancery Court. Sullivan County. Hon. Thomas J. Seeley, Jr., Judge (Sitting by Interchange). S. Ct. No. 03S01-9709-CH-00116



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF COURT OF APPEALS AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED IN PART; CASE REMANDED TO TRIAL COURT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, owners of annexed land, challenged the judgment from the Court of Appeals (Tennessee), which found that defendant city's municipal annexation ordinances were subject to review under the declaratory judgment statute and that the trial court did not err in declining to issue a declaratory judgment concerning defendant city's annexation of their property.


OVERVIEW: The city adopted 24 annexation ordinances in which it sought to annex 24 separate parcels of property that were adjacent to a highway. Plaintiffs were owners of 15 of the 24 parcels, and they filed a quo warranto and declaratory judgment action contesting the annexations. The complaint, which originally charged that the ordinances were unreasonable within the meaning of Tenn. Code Ann. § 6-51-103(a)(1)(A) (1992), was amended to charge that 16 of the ordinances, the 14 ordinances previously named as well as two additional ordinances, were invalid on the grounds that one of the 1989 highway right-of-way annexations, to which these later annexations were attached, was "null and void" under Tenn. Code Ann. § 6-51-102 (1992), because it did not annex people, private property or commercial activities. Under the Declaratory Judgment Act, the trial court held that the annexation was illegal and void. The court held that the appellate court correctly permitted plaintiffs to challenge the 1989 annexation ordinance outside of the quo warranto procedures of Tenn. Code Ann. § 6-51-103. The trial court erred in declining to consider whether to issue a declaratory judgment concerning annexation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded for further proceedings.

 

23 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


State v. Henning


No. 02S01-9707-CC-00065


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


975 S.W.2d 290; 1998 Tenn. LEXIS 370



June 22, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Henning v. State, 2004 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 90 (Tenn. Crim. App., Jan. 30, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Criminal Court. Madison County. Hon. Whit LaFon, Judge.
State v. Henning, 1997 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 5 (Tenn. Crim. App., Jan. 9, 1997)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of possession of cocaine with intent to sell, possession of cocaine with intent to deliver, and possession of drug paraphernalia. Defendant appealed the judgment of the Tennessee Criminal Court of Appeals, which affirmed the trial court's denial of defendant's motion to suppress the evidence seized in a search of his property and affirmed his convictions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the search warrant affidavit did not establish probable cause. The court disagreed, finding that the affidavit contained specific allegations regarding the location and defendant's actions, showing the basis of knowledge. Although there was no specific allegation in the affidavit that established the informant's credibility, the independent police corroboration of the informant's tip, explained in the affidavit, was sufficient to establish the informant's credibility. The affidavit was sufficient to support a finding of probable cause justifying issuance of the search warrant. Defendant next contended that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress because the officers executing the warrant failed to comply with the knock and announce requirement before entering defendant's home. The court held that a court should consider the entire record when reviewing a motion to suppress. Based upon the record, which included police testimony that defendant was likely to flee and that it would have been difficult to ascertain where the drugs were going to be if they got in the house, the court found that the police were justified in using a no-knock entry.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's judgment upholding the trial court's denial of defendant's motion to suppress and the judgment of conviction. The court remanded the cause to the trial court for resentencing.

State v. Blanton

975 S.W.2d 269; 1998 Tenn. LEXIS 352



June 15, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected June 16, 1998. Rehearing Denied September 8, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Tenn. LEXIS 478.

Rehearing denied by State v. Blanton, 1998 Tenn. LEXIS 478 (Tenn., Sept. 8, 1998)
Writ of certiorari denied Blanton v. Tennessee, 525 U.S. 1180, 119 S. Ct. 1118, 143 L. Ed. 2d 113, 1999 U.S. LEXIS 1585 (1999)

DISPOSITION: COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision of the Court of Criminal Appeals (Tennessee), which affirmed his convictions on two counts of first degree premeditated murder, four counts of grand larceny, and three counts of first degree burglary, and sentenced him to death on both counts of first degree murder.


OVERVIEW: Within days of his escape from prison, defendant murdered an elderly couple in their home. The husband was shot to death and the wife suffered gunshot wounds as well as stab wounds. A jury sentenced defendant to death on both counts of first degree murder based on three aggravating circumstances. The jury found that the wife's murder was especially heinous, atrocious and cruel in that it involved torture or depravity of mind. The jury found that no mitigating circumstances sufficiently outweighed the aggravating circumstances. Although an instruction charging all felonies without regard to whether they were supported by the evidence was error, it was harmless.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court upholding defendant's murder convictions and sentencing him to death by electrocution.

Finister v. Humboldt Gen. Hosp.


Supreme Court No. 02S01-9704-CH-00038


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


970 S.W.2d 435; 1998 Tenn. LEXIS 291



May 26, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Chancery Court. Gibson County. Hon. George R. Ellis, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant hospital appealed an order of Gibson County Chancery Court (Tennessee), which denied it summary judgment in connection with plaintiff employee's action for workers' compensation benefits.


OVERVIEW: The employee sought workers' compensation benefits for a work-related injury while employed by the hospital. The hospital, a public benefit, non-profit corporation filed a motion for summary judgment, claiming an exemption applicable to municipal corporations from the Tennessee Workers' Compensation Act pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 50-6-106(5) (1997). The court reversed the denial of summary judgment, holding that as a subsidiary of an exempt hospital district, the hospital was exempt from the workers' compensation laws unless the quasi-municipal corporation elected to accept the provisions of the Workers' Compensation Act by filing written notice with the Commissioner of Labor. The hospital district was a municipal corporation under the exemption provision because it was created for the benefit of two cities, the members of the hospital district's governing board received no compensation and were selected by government officials, and city funds were used to finance the hospital district. Under its charter, the hospital was a subsidiary of the hospital district, an exempt, quasi-municipal corporation, and thus the hospital was also exempt from the workers' compensation laws.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the denial of summary judgment for the hospital in connection with the employee's claim for workers' compensation benefits, and the court entered summary judgment in favor of the hospital.

State ex rel. Earhart v. City of Bristol


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


1998 Tenn. LEXIS 254



April 27, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Chancery Court. Sullivan County. Hon. Thomas J. Seeley, Jr., Judge (Sitting by Interchange). S. CT. NO. 03S01-9709-CH-00116.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF COURT OF APPEALS AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED IN PART; CASE REMANDED TO TRIAL COURT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review from a decision of the Court of Appeals (Tennessee), which confirmed the trial court's verdict, in favor of appellee homeowners, as to each ordinance and held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in declining to issue a declaratory judgment regarding the validity of the 1989 ordinances.


OVERVIEW: The issue involved the validity of municipal ordinances concerning the annexation of certain streets and highways. The first issue on appeal was whether the homeowners should have been allowed to collaterally challenge the 1989 annexation ordinance outside of the quo warranto procedures set out in Tenn. Code Ann. § 6-51-103. The court affirmed the trial court and held that they could since they did own property in the territory that was being annexed in reliance on the 1989 ordinance. The second issue was whether the trial court abused its discretion in declining to issue a declaratory judgment concerning the 1989 annexation. At issue was whether the city's annexation scheme was consistent with the purpose sought to be accomplished by the statutes authorizing municipalities to determine their own boundaries. The court noted that a declaratory judgment would have terminated this controversy and that the case involved an important issue of law which affected the growth of cities throughout the state and which needed to be resolved. The court reversed and held that the trial court should have granted declaratory judgment for such an important issue.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision that the homeowners could bring the collateral challenge to the annexation ordinance. The court reversed the trial court's decision and held that the application for declaratory relief should have been granted.

SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


967 S.W.2d 773; 1998 Tenn. LEXIS 207



April 13, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied Cribbs v. Tennessee, 525 U.S. 932, 119 S. Ct. 343, 142 L. Ed. 2d 283, 1998 U.S. LEXIS 6525 (1998)

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of a Court of Criminal Appeals (Tennessee), which affirmed his conviction for the offense of first degree murder during the perpetration of an aggravated burglary and his sentence of death by electrocution.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the jury instructions concerning eyewitness identification was inadequate, that prosecutorial argument during the penalty phase was improper, and that the sentence was erroneous because the jury found aggravating circumstances and sentenced defendant to death under each of the three murder counts when only one person was murdered. Evans v. Steelman


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


970 S.W.2d 431; 1998 Tenn. LEXIS 179



March 30, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 30, 1998. Petitions for Rehearing Denied June 22, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Tenn. LEXIS 371.


PRIOR HISTORY: JUVENILE COURT. DAVIDSON COUNTY. HON. ANDREW J. SHOOKHOFF, JUDGE. NO. 01S01-9701-JV-00019.

CIRCUIT COURT. DAVIDSON COUNTY. HON. THOMAS W. BROTHERS, JUDGE. NO. 01S01-9703-CV-00046.



DISPOSITION: COURT OF APPEALS AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Juvenile Court, Davidson County (Tennessee) dismissed a legitimation petition filed by petitioner biological father one against respondent mother one on the basis of no standing. Petitioner biological father two's legitimation petition against respondents, mother two and husband, was maintained in the Circuit Court, Davidson County (Tennessee), which found that Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-2-202 was not facially unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The lower court, on appeal, dismissed the legitimation petitions of biological father one and biological father two. The court granted the applications for permission to appeal and consolidate the petitions. Both contended that they were the biological fathers of the children in question, which were born while mother one and mother two were married to their respective spouses. The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court. Biological father one and biological father two lacked standing pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-2-202. The phrase, child born out of lawful wedlock, found in § 36-2-202, meant a child born to an unmarried woman. The denial of standing did not violate their procedural and substantive due process rights by denying biological father one and biological father two fair hearings and opportunities to establish legal relationships with the children. Section 36-2-202 created a right for putative fathers; it did not take those rights away. Therefore, no protected interests were implicated. There was no equal protection violation because the classification created by § 36-2-202 did not treat similarly situated persons differently.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court, which dismissed the legitimation petitions of biological father one against mother one and biological father two against mother two and the husband.

Stuart v. State Department of Safety


NO. 01-S-01-9612-CH-00239


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


963 S.W.2d 28; 1998 Tenn. LEXIS 96



March 2, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DAVIDSON COUNTY. HON. IRVIN H. KILCREASE, JR., CHANCELLOR.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant claimant, who had pled guilty to controlled substances offenses, sought review of a judgment of the Court of Appeals (Tennessee), which affirmed the chancery court's decision upholding an administrative forfeiture of the claimant's property by appellee Tennessee Department of Safety. The claimant alleged that the forfeiture violated the double jeopardy and excessive fine clauses of the United States and Tennessee constitutions.


OVERVIEW: The Commissioner of the Tennessee Department of Safety (department) under Tenn. Code Ann. § 53-11-201 et seq. had ordered the forfeiture of the claimant's truck, other personal property, and over $ 840,000 in currency on the ground that the property was used in the conduct of an illegal drug enterprise. On appeal, the court affirmed the appellate court's judgment in favor of the department. The court held that the forfeiture as a civil in rem proceeding did not impose punishment for purposes of the constitutional double jeopardy clauses. The court found that forfeiture served important nonpunitive goals, such as encouraging property owners to ensure that their property was not used for illegal purposes, and preventing persons from profiting from their illegal acts. The court further held that the forfeiture of the claimant's property did not violate the constitutional excessive fines clauses. The court found that the claimant was never legally entitled to the proceeds of illegal drug transaction; and the forfeiture of the claimant's truck was justified in view of the seriousness of the drug conspiracy offense, and because the truck was used to facilitate a drug transaction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's judgment in upholding the department's administrative forfeiture of the claimant's property.

 

31 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


State v. Boyd


No. 02-S-01-9611-CR-00102


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


959 S.W.2d 557; 1998 Tenn. LEXIS 2



January 5, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] CRIMINAL COURT. SHELBY COUNTY. HON. JOSEPH B. McCARTIE, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals (Tennessee), which affirmed the denial of a petition for post-conviction relief that alleged numerous constitutional violations in the trial that resulted in his conviction of felony murder and the death sentence. The lower appellate court held that the jury's reliance on an invalid aggravating circumstance violated Tenn. Const. art. I, § 16, but was harmless error.


OVERVIEW: The prosecution offered three aggravating circumstances to the jury at sentencing: (1) that defendant had a prior conviction for a violent felony, (2) that defendant knowingly created a risk of death to two or more persons other than the victim, and (3) that the killing occurred in the perpetration of a felony. On appeal, the court held that the felony murder factor could not be used in a felony murder case because it duplicated the elements of the offense and did not narrow the class of death eligible murderers, as required by Tenn. Const. art. I, § 16 and the Eighth Amendment. The court used a harmless error analysis and looked at the number and strength of remaining aggravating circumstances, the prosecutor's argument at sentencing, the evidence admitted to establish the invalid aggravator, and the nature, quality, and strength of mitigating evidence. The court found that defendant's prior homicide conviction outweighed the other factors, the prosecution did not emphasize the factor, and there was little mitigation evidence. The court concluded beyond a reasonable doubt that the verdict would have been the same had the jury given no weight to the invalid factor.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower appellate court judgment that affirmed the denial of post-conviction relief and upheld the sentence of death.

 

32 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lewis


No. 01-S-01-9611-CR-00227


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


958 S.W.2d 736; 1997 Tenn. LEXIS 631



December 29, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] SUMNER COUNTY. HON. FRED A. KELLY, III, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Court of Criminal Appeals (Tennessee), which affirmed defendant's conviction for five counts of aggravated arson in violation of Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-14-302(a) (1991).


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the double jeopardy clauses of the United States and Tennessee constitutions barred multiple convictions for aggravated arson of a single structure containing several apartment units. The court found that the word "structure" as used in Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-14-301 (1991) meant the entire structure and because defendant burned a portion of a single structure in the course of one act, only one count of aggravated arson could have successfully withstood double jeopardy scrutiny. The judgment of conviction on four of the counts was reversed and the sentences imposed on those four counts were vacated. The sentence imposed on the remaining count was vacated and the cause was remanded for a new sentencing hearing. The court held that defendant could not have received multiple punishments for the same offense. The legislature did not intend to punish for the arson of each apartment in a multi-apartment structure.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of conviction imposed on four arson counts and the sentences imposed upon those four counts were vacated. The remaining arson count was affirmed but the sentence imposed on that count was vacated and the matter for remanded for a new sentencing hearing.

 

33 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


State v. Winningham


NO. 01-S-01-9701-CC-00008


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


958 S.W.2d 740; 1997 Tenn. LEXIS 632



December 29, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] PICKETT COUNTY. HON. LEON BURNS, JR., JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED; INDICTMENT REINSTATED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state challenged the order of the Court of Criminal Appeals (Tennessee), which affirmed the trial court's decision that the defendant's conviction of criminal contempt barred, on grounds of double jeopardy, a subsequent indictment for arson that was based on the same facts and occurrence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant set fire to his estranged wife's home. He was convicted of criminal and civil contempt for violating a protection order. The state then indicted him on arson charges. The trial court found that double jeopardy barred the indictment, and the appellate court affirmed. The court reversed and reinstated the indictment because double jeopardy was not violated. The court held that arson and contempt were, in the context presented, significantly different offenses under double jeopardy analyses. The court held that the underlying criminal offense was not viewed as a lesser-included offense of contempt because it was not necessarily included within the statutory elements of contempt. The court held that the two charges had no common elements. The court held that the court was the victim of contempt, while the public or the property owner were the victims of arson; the fact that different victims were involved suggested that separate prosecutions would not violate double jeopardy principles. The fact that the two statutes served vastly different purposes suggested that separate prosecutions would not violate double jeopardy principles.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and reinstated the indictment.

State v. Hall

DISPOSITION: TRIAL COURT AND COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The trial court (Tennessee) entered judgment, upon a jury verdict, convicting defendant of premeditated first degree murder and aggravated arson. Finding that the aggravating circumstances outweighed mitigating circumstances beyond a reasonable doubt, the jury sentenced defendant to death by electrocution. On review, the Court of Criminal Appeals affirmed. Automatic review followed.


OVERVIEW: In a capital case, defendant was convicted of premeditated first degree murder and aggravated arson. In the sentencing hearing, the jury found two aggravating circumstances that outweighed mitigating circumstances beyond a reasonable doubt and sentenced defendant to death by electrocution. Defendant appealed from the decision. Defendant first argued he was entitled to a new trial because during the guilt phase of the trial, the trial court refused to admit the expert proof regarding his mental state at the time the offense was committed. The reviewing court found the testimony was properly excluded because defendant's proffer failed to inform the trial court that the testimony was being offered to negate intent. The reviewing court also found the jury's findings supported the aggravating circumstances and were constitutionally applied. Finally the reviewing court found the evidence was sufficient to show defendant acted with premeditation and deliberation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for first degree murder and sentence of death.

 

35 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Tennessee Mun. League v. Thompson


Supreme Court No. 01S01-9711-CH-00242


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


958 S.W.2d 333; 1997 Tenn. LEXIS 613



December 10, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Chancery Court. Davidson County. Hon. Irvin H. Kilcrease, Jr., Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, cities and municipal league, sought review of a declaratory judgment of the Chancery Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) in favor of appellees, state and county election officials, holding that 1997 Tenn. Pub. Acts 98 (Act), which changed requirements for municipal incorporation, was constitutional under Tenn. Const. art. II, § 17.


OVERVIEW: The Act, which amended the municipal annexation provisions in Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 6-1-201, et seq., was passed by the general assembly and signed into law by the governor. The cities and municipal league brought an action seeking a declaratory judgment that certain sections of the Act were unconstitutional under the Tennessee Constitution. The chancery court found the Act to be constitutional and entered judgment in favor of the state and county election officials. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment. The court held that the Act violated Tenn. Const. art. II, § 17 and was void because the restrictive title of the Act, which referred specifically to tax collections after the incorporation of new municipalities and the timing of elections to incorporate new municipalities, did not directly or indirectly relate to the broader provisions set forth in the Act. The court held that where the title of an amendatory act recited the title of the act to be amended and also specified the amendments to be made, the legislature was limited to the amendments specified, and anything outside of those amendments was void.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the chancery court's judgment and held that an act amending Tennessee's requirements for municipal incorporation violated the Tennessee Constitution and was void.

State v. Mann


Supreme Court No. 02-S01-9609-CC-00077


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


959 S.W.2d 503; 1997 Tenn. LEXIS 608



December 8, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied February 17, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Tenn. LEXIS 53. Certiorari Denied June 26, 1998, Reported at: 1998 U.S. LEXIS 4345.
Rehearing denied by State v. Mann, 1998 Tenn. LEXIS 53 (Tenn., Feb. 17, 1998)
Writ of certiorari denied Mann v. Tennessee, 524 U.S. 956, 118 S. Ct. 2376, 141 L. Ed. 2d 743, 1998 U.S. LEXIS 4345 (1998)
Post-conviction relief denied at Mann v. State, 2003 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 858 (Tenn. Crim. App., Oct. 9, 2003)
Writ denied by State v. Mann, 2007 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 619 (Tenn. Crim. App., Aug. 6, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: CRIMINAL COURT. DYER COUNTY. Hon. Joe G. Riley, Judge.
State v. Mann, 1996 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 508 (Tenn. Crim. App., Aug. 16, 1996)



DISPOSITION: TRIAL COURT AND COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of premeditated first degree murder, aggravated rape, and aggravated burglary. A jury found certain aggravating factors under Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 39-13-204(i)(5) and (7) (1991) outweighed any mitigating circumstances beyond a reasonable doubt and sentenced defendant to death by electrocution. The Court of Criminal Appeals (Tennessee) affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant confessed to raping and stabbing a hearing impaired woman to death, but claimed that he did not intend to kill her. The court held that (1) defendant's constitutional rights were not violated by the State's decision to seek the death penalty after defendant rejected the State's offer of life imprisonment in exchange for a guilty plea because, once defendant rejected the offer, the State was entitled to prosecute defendant to the fullest extent possible and to seek the most severe punishment; (2) the evidence, including the fact that the victim was conscious while the wounds were inflicted, was sufficient to establish the aggravating factor of serious physical abuse beyond that necessary to produce death; (3) the evidence, including defendant's admission that he forced open the victim's door with the intent to steal her television, was sufficient to establish the aggravating factor of a murder committed during a burglary; and (4) the aggravating circumstances outweighed any mitigating circumstances beyond a reasonable doubt. Thus, the court held that the death penalty was not disproportionate, given the nature of the crime, even though defendant was only 22 years old.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence of death by electrocution.

State v. Bland

SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


958 S.W.2d 651; 1997 Tenn. LEXIS 587



December 1, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Certiorari Denied April 20, 1998, Reported at: 1998 U.S. LEXIS 2690.
Writ of certiorari denied Bland v. Tennessee, 523 U.S. 1083, 118 S. Ct. 1536, 140 L. Ed. 2d 686, 1998 U.S. LEXIS 2690 (Apr. 20, 1998)
Post-conviction relief denied at Bland v. State, 2009 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 283 (Tenn. Crim. App., Apr. 3, 2009)
Application denied by Bland v. State, 2017 Tenn. LEXIS 42 (Tenn., Jan. 20, 2017)

DISPOSITION: TRIAL COURT AND COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a Court of Criminal Appeals (Tennessee) judgment affirming his conviction and death sentence for first-degree murder pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-204(1)(5), arguing various errors and challenging the sufficiency of the evidence and the proportionality of the sentence imposed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of premeditated first-degree murder, attempted aggravated robbery, especially aggravated robbery, and attempted first-degree murder. After a death sentence was imposed on him pursuant to Tenn. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and sentence.

State v. Yeargan


No. 01S01-9604-CC-00080


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE (HEARD AT COOKEVILLE)


958 S.W.2d 626; 1997 Tenn. LEXIS 574



November 24, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Criminal Court. Coffee County. Hon. Gerald L. Ewell, Sr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Court of Criminal Appeals (Tennessee), which affirmed the denial of a motion to suppress evidence of defendant's intoxication obtained during a stop by a city police officer.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped by a police officer while defendant was operating a truck. Six months earlier, the officer arrested defendant for driving under the influence. The officer was also present in court when defendant's driver's license was revoked for one year. The trial court denied defendant's motion to suppress the evidence of defendant's intoxication obtained during the stop. The lower court affirmed the trial court's decision. The court affirmed the lower court's decision because considering the totality of the circumstances, the officer's decision to initiate the investigatory stop was based upon reasonable suspicion, supported by specific and articulable facts, that defendant was driving on a revoked license. The officer had previously arrested defendant. Further, the officer had personal knowledge that defendant's driver's license was revoked for one year, but that only six months had passed since the revocation. Moreover, the officer had no constitutional obligation to verify the status of defendant's license before making the stop because the availability of less intrusive investigatory techniques did not vitiate the validity of a stop supported by reasonable suspicion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the lower court that affirmed the denial of defendant's motion to suppress.

Arnold v. Tennessee Bd. of Paroles


NO. 01-S-01-9610-CH-00210


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


956 S.W.2d 478; 1997 Tenn. LEXIS 533



November 10, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY: DAVIDSON COUNTY. HON. C. ALLEN HIGH, Chancellor and HON. ELLEN HOBBS LYLE, Chancellor.

DAVIDSON COUNTY. HON. ELLEN HOBBS LYLE, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: AS TO ARNOLD: AFFIRMED. AS TO EVANS: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmates sought review of the judgment of the Court of Appeals (Tennessee), which affirmed the trial court's dismissal of their petitions for the common law writ of certiorari challenging the decision of respondent Tennessee Board of Paroles (Board). The Board had denied them parole. The inmates urged, inter alia, that the Board violated the Open Meetings Act, Tenn. Code Ann. § 8-44-101 et seq. (1993).


OVERVIEW: Two inmates asserted in their petitions for common law writ of certiorari that the process used by the Tennessee Board of Paroles, by which they were denied parole, violated the Open Meetings Act (Act), Tenn. Code Ann. § 8-44-101 et seq. (1993). Under the Board's procedure, each Board member separately and independently reviewed the cases before the Board. Each case file was circulated to each of the Board members. A member formulated his or her decision without conferring with any other member, relying solely on the record compiled by the hearing officer. The trial court denied the petitions for writ of certiorari. The appellate court affirmed. The state supreme court held that the Board was exempt from the Act because, although the Board was a "governing body" within the meaning of the Act, nothing in the Board's enabling statute, Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-28-105(b), (d) (1990), required it to meet in order to deliberate or make parole decisions. The court further concluded that, while parole was properly denied on substantive grounds in both cases, one inmate stated a U.S. Const. amend. I claim upon which relief could be granted, and thus his case was remanded to the trial court.


OUTCOME: The Court of Appeals judgment, affirming the trial court's dismissal of the inmates' petitions for common law writ of certiorari that were filed after the Tennessee Board of Paroles denied parol, was affirmed as to one inmate. The judgment was reversed in part as to the other inmate's claim for injunctive relief, as he stated a First Amendment claim upon which relief could be granted, and his case was remanded to the trial court.
