State v. Sheline


No. 03-S-01-9701-CR-00002


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


955 S.W.2d 42; 1997 Tenn. LEXIS 496



October 20, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied March 9, 1998, Reported at: 1998 U.S. LEXIS 1735.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] CRIMINAL COURT. HAMILTON COUNTY. HON. DOUGLAS A. MEYER, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS REVERSED; JUDGMENT OF TRIAL COURT REINSTATED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state challenged a decision from the Court of Criminal Appeals of Tennessee, which reversed defendant's rape conviction on the grounds that the trial court had erred in excluding evidence of the victim's sexual encounter with witness one and the events on the evening in question as described by witness two. The question presented to the court was whether the trial court had property applied the Tennessee "rape shield" rule.


OVERVIEW: The victim and defendant were college students. They met at a bar. The victim asked defendant if he wanted to stay the night at her apartment. The victim alleged she was raped, while defendant argued the intercourse was consensual. Defendant attempted to introduce witness one's testimony that he had met the victim in a bar, that they drank heavily, and then engaged in oral sex and sexual intercourse. He testified that they had also had sex on another occasion. Defendant also attempted to introduce witness two's testimony that the same evening defendant and the victim met in the bar, the victim had kissed him and asked him to go home with her. The court reversed, holding that: (1) the evidence of the victim's sexual behavior with persons other than defendant did not establish a pattern of sexual behavior so distinctive and so closely resembling defendant's version of the encounter with the victim that it tended to prove the victim consented to the act charged and it, therefore, was not admissible under Tenn. R. Evid. 412(c)(4)(iii); and (2) the trial court's application of Rule 412 did not deny defendant's rights under the Tennessee or United States Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's judgment and reinstated defendant's rape conviction. The court held the costs of the appeal were taxed to defendant.

Carter v. State

Bean v. McWherter


No. 01S01-9607-CH-00132


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


953 S.W.2d 197; 1997 Tenn. LEXIS 436



September 8, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied October 27, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Tenn. LEXIS 509.
Rehearing denied by Bean v. McWherter, 1997 Tenn. LEXIS 509 (Tenn., Oct. 27, 1997)
Appeal after remand at Bean v. McWherter, 24 S.W.3d 325, 1999 Tenn. App. LEXIS 801 (Tenn. Ct. App., 1999)


PRIOR HISTORY: Chancery Court. Davidson County. Hon. Irvin H. Kilcrease, Jr., Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: COURT OF APPEALS REVERSED; CASE REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the Tennessee Wildlife Resources Commission (TWRC) and the Director of the Tennessee Wildlife Resources Agency, sought review of a decision from the Court of Appeals (Tennessee), which upheld a chancery court ruling that Tenn. Code Ann. § 70-4-403(1), (3) was unconstitutional. Plaintiffs, owners, dealers, and licensed propagators of various wildlife species, had filed a declaratory judgment action.


OVERVIEW: The court of appeals held that the general assembly could not constitutionally delegate power to the TWRC to add or delete animals from the dangerous species list. The court reversed, holding that the legislature could delegate power to add and delete items from a statutory schedule absent explicit guidance standards, so long as the legislature provided a basic standard accompanied by a general policy when delegating in areas concerning public health, safety, and general welfare. The test for determining whether a statute was an unlawful delegation of authority was whether the statute contained sufficient standards or guidelines to enable both the agency and the courts to determine if the agency was carrying out the legislature's intent. The court ruled that governing standards need not be expressed provided such standards could be reasonably ascertained from the statutory scheme as a whole. Section 70-4-403(1), (3) outlined a general scheme designed to protect the public from dangerous animals. The mere adding or deleting of animals from a nonexclusive list or moving an animal from one classification to another did not alter the legislative policy of providing public protection.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the chancery court and the court of appeals. The court ruled that the legislature had the power to delegate to the TWRC the authority to add or delete animals from the dangerous species act.

Fletcher v. State


Supreme Court No. 02-S01-9606-CR-00056


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


951 S.W.2d 378; 1997 Tenn. LEXIS 407



August 25, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Fletcher v. State, 1999 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 654 (Tenn. Crim. App., July 7, 1999)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Hon. L. T. Lafferty, Judge. SHELBY COUNTY.
Fletcher v. State, 1995 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 588 (Tenn. Crim. App., July 19, 1995)



DISPOSITION: COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of a decision of the Court of Criminal Appeals (Tennessee),which affirmed the trial court's denial of his motion to reopen his first petition for post-conviction relief under Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-30-217 (1996 Supp.).


OVERVIEW: The inmate's petition for post-conviction relief was denied and the decision was affirmed on appeal. He filed a motion to reopen his petition. The trial court denied the motion and the appellate court upheld the denial. On appeal, the court affirmed, finding that the trial court did not abuse its discretion by denying the inmate's motion to reopen because the allegations did not establish a valid statutory basis for granting it under § 40-30-217. The court rejected the State's claim that the inmate had no right to seek the court's review, ruling that the failure of the procedures outlined in § 40-30-217(c) to include supreme court review did not preclude an application for permission to appeal the denial of a motion to reopen. The court found that the statute's silence did not support the implication that the legislature intended to divest the court of its discretionary jurisdiction over such motions under Tenn. R. App. P. 11. The court concluded that § 40-30-217(c) was merely intended to simplify and expedite the appellate court's review by setting short timelines and removing it from the strictures of the appellate rules, but left further review to proceed under the rules.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's decision upholding the trial court's denial of the inmate's motion to reopen his petition for post-conviction relief.

State v. Bush

SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


942 S.W.2d 489; 1997 Tenn. LEXIS 171



April 7, 1997, FILED

PRIOR HISTORY: CUMBERLAND COUNTY. Hon. Leon Burns, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: TRIAL COURT AND COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a capital case, defendant was convicted of premeditated first degree murder and first degree burglary and the Court of Criminal Appeals (Tennessee) affirmed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murdering an elderly woman by repeatedly stabbing her. On appeal, the defendant first argued that his statements to the police should have been suppressed because he was not advised of his Miranda warnings, even though he was in custody when he gave the first tape-recorded statement. Considering the totality of the circumstances, the court found that the evidence in the record did not preponderate against the lower courts' finding that defendant was not in custody when he was initially interviewed by law enforcement officials. Defendant initiated the contact, and he showed no signs of delusions or mental illness at the time that would warrant intervention of a psychiatrist, had he been in custody. The court also found that a waiver of defendant's Miranda rights was voluntary because there was no showing of mental illness before the interrogation and once defendant did ask for counsel, it was provided. The court held that aggravating circumstances had been appropriately considered by the trial court, and the death penalty was proportionate with the crime.


OUTCOME: The conviction and sentence were affirmed.

 

45 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


State v. Martin


NO. 01-S-01-9605-CR-00091


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


940 S.W.2d 567; 1997 Tenn. LEXIS 131



March 17, 1997, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DAVIDSON COUNTY. HON. ANN LACY JOHNS, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted on four counts of possession and sale of cocaine in various amounts pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-17-417 (1991). The trial judge sentenced defendant to consecutive 10-year sentences and imposed a fine. Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals (Tennessee), which affirmed the convictions, modified the sentences, and remanded the cause to the trial court for determination of the fine.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the admission of tape-recorded statements of an informant at trial violated his state and federal constitutional rights, that the admission of evidence of a prior drug offense was erroneous under Tenn. R. Evid. 404(b), and that he was entitled to a new trial because the trial judge imposed fines in excess of $ 50 in violation of Tenn. Const. art. VI, § 14. On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's convictions and remanded the cause to the trial court for a determination, by a new jury, of the fines to be imposed. The court held that defendant waived his right to appeal the admission of the informant's statements and the admission of the prior drug offense. The court found that Tenn. Const. art. VI, § 14 did not require the same jury that determined guilt to fix the fine. The trial judge lacked the authority to fix the fines imposed in the various counts of the case. Nothing in the record pointed to a waiver by defendant of his right to have the fine fixed by the jury. Also, the trial judge exercised some measure of discretion because Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-17-428(b)(7-9) (1991) prescribed only a minimum fine.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and remanded the cause to the trial court, directing that a new jury was to have been empaneled for the purpose of fixing the amount of the fines to be imposed.

 

46 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Lea Indus. v. Hixon


NO. 03S01-9606-CH-00067


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, SPECIAL WORKERS' COMPENSATION APPEALS PANEL, AT KNOXVILLE


1997 Tenn. LEXIS 133



March 17, 1997, FILED


NOTICE: CONSULT THE TENNESSEE SUPREME COURT RULES FOR CITATION OF UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Judgment Order of March 17, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Tenn. LEXIS 137.


PRIOR HISTORY: GRAINGER COUNTY. HON. CHESTER S. RAINWATER, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: MODIFIED AND AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant employee appealed a decision from a Tennessee trial court, which found that he was entitled to permanent disability benefits of 17.5 percent to the body as a whole based on its determination that the award was limited to two and one-half times the medical impairment rating of seven percent, pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 50-6-241(a)(1).


OVERVIEW: The employee argued that the chancellor erred in not applying § 50-6-241(b), which fixed the limit of the award at six times the medical impairment rating. The chancellor had applied § 50-6-241(a)(1) based on its finding that the employee voluntarily left his employment. The court held that which section applied had to be determined by whether there was a meaningful return to work. The employee was a 49 year old man who had completed the 9th grade. He hurt his back when bending down to pick up some lumber. He returned to work about 10 days after being released from the hospital. He continued to work with pain and under restrictions for eight months. The chancellor made no finding as to whether or not the return to work had been meaningful. On appeal, the court found the employee returned to his employment in an injured condition. His leaving employment was obviously because of his physical condition due to the work-related injury. His return to work was not meaningful in the sense of the statute. Thus, he was entitled to an award which did not exceed the cap of six times the medical impairment rating under subsection (b).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the amount of disability, but determined that the employee was entitled to an award of six times the medical impairment rating. It modified the award to 42 percent permanent disability benefits to the body as a whole, and as modified, the judgment was affirmed.

 

47 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Riggs v. Burson


No. 03-S-01-9603-CV-00032


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


941 S.W.2d 44; 1997 Tenn. LEXIS 126



March 10, 1997, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied April 7, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Tenn. LEXIS 174.


PRIOR HISTORY: CIRCUIT COURT. SEVIER COUNTY. HON. WILLIAM R. HOLT, JR., JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: COURT OF APPEALS REVERSED; TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT REINSTATED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, attorney general and transportation commissioner, appealed an order of the Court of Appeals (Tennessee), which remanded the dismissal of a declaratory action. Plaintiffs, heliport company and owner, argued that Tenn. Code Ann. § 42-8-101 et seq. was preempted by the Federal Aviation Act, 49 U.S.C.S. § 40101-41901, and violative of U.S. Const. amend. XIV, Tenn. Const. art. I, § 8 and Tenn. Const. art. XI, § 8.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, heliport company and owner, filed a declaratory action to challenge the constitutionality of Tenn. Code Ann. § 42-8-101 et seq. on the grounds that it was preempted by the Federal Aviation Act (Act), 49 U.S.C.S. § 40101-41901, and violative of U.S. Const. amend. XIV, Tenn. Const. art. I, § 8, and Tenn. Const. art. XI, § 8. Plaintiffs' action was dismissed pursuant to a motion filed by defendants, attorney general and transportation commissioner, and plaintiffs appealed. The lower court remanded the dismissal and defendants appealed. The court reversed the lower court's order and reinstated the dismissal. The court held that the statute was not preempted by the Act because proper analysis revealed that the statute regulated the use of land and not the flight of aircraft or the use of airspace as regulated by the Act. The court held that the statute did not violate due process or equal protection rights under U.S. Const. amend. XIV, Tenn. Const. art. I, § 8, or Tenn. Const. art. XI, § 8 because it restricted the location of heliports within nine miles of a national park in an effort to achieve a legitimate interest related to the public's safety, health, and welfare.


OUTCOME: An order remanding the dismissal of a declaratory action brought by plaintiffs, heliport company and owner, to challenge the constitutionality of a state statute as preempted by federal law and contrary to due process and equal protection rights was reversed on the grounds that the statute regulated the use of land and the statutory restrictions were reasonably related to the legitimate interest of securing public safety.

City of Tullahoma v. Bedford County


Appeal No. 01S01-9511-CH-00208


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE

DISPOSITION: COURT OF APPEALS REVERSED; SUMMARY JUDGMENT ENTERED FOR PLAINTIFFS.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant cities challenged the decision of the Court of Appeals (Tennessee), which, in an action for declaratory judgment, affirmed the summary judgment issued by the trial court in favor of appellees, county, board, and clerk.


OVERVIEW: The cities sought a declaratory judgment against the appellees that a private act authorizing the county to impose a tax on the privilege of disposing of solid waste at landfills in the county did not violate the equal protection provisions of the state constitution. The cities claimed, on appeal, that the private act was in conflict with the Tennessee Solid Waste Disposal Act, Tenn. State v. Smoky Mt. Secrets


No. 02S01-9509-CH-00084


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


937 S.W.2d 905; 1996 Tenn. LEXIS 695



October 28, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Chancery Court. Shelby County. Hon. D. J. Alissandratos, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF COURT OF APPEALS AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED IN PART; CASE REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State of Tennessee sought review of the judgment of the Court of Appeals (Tennessee), which held that certain provisions of the Tennessee Charitable Solicitations Act, Tenn. Code Ann. § 48-3-501 et seq. (1989), regulating professional solicitors violated the equal protection provisions of the federal and state constitutions and that other provisions violated constitutional guarantees of freedom of speech.


OVERVIEW: Appellant State of Tennessee filed an action for declaratory and injunctive relief against appellee professional solicitation company pursuant to the Tennessee Charitable Solicitations Act (Act), Tenn. Code Ann. § 48-3-501 et seq. (1989). The trial court granted summary judgment to appellee, holding that certain of the Act's provisions were unconstitutional. Appellant sought interlocutory review. The court reversed the grant of summary judgment as to those provisions that imposed requirements on professional solicitors not imposed on charitable organizations, holding that these did not violate constitutional principles of equal protection or freedom of speech because professional and charitable organizations were not similarly situated and the provisions applicable to professional organizations were narrowly tailored to serve a compelling state interest in protecting the public against fraud. The court affirmed the denial of appellee's request for summary judgment on the constitutionality of the fee and bond provisions, finding that there was a genuine issue of fact as to whether these fees had a reasonable relationship to the costs of administering and enforcing the Act.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the summary judgment granted to appellee professional solicitation company, finding that the provisions of the Tennessee Charitable Solicitation Act that imposed requirements on professional solicitors not imposed on charitable organizations did not violate constitutional guarantees of free speech or equal protection because professional solicitors and charitable organizations were not similarly situated.

 

50 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Wimley v. Rudolph


No. 01S01-9507-CH-00108


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


931 S.W.2d 513; 1996 Tenn. LEXIS 616



October 7, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Davidson County. Hon. C. Allen High, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Tennessee Department of Human Services (DHS) challenged the decision of the Tennessee Court of Appeals that upheld an award of attorney fees under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988 in plaintiff claimant's administrative appeal of the termination of her benefits under the Aid for Dependent Children (AFDC) program.


OVERVIEW: Claimant was a recipient of AFDC benefits when she received an inheritance. She was told by DHS that there would not be a change in her benefits. Instead, DHS terminated her benefits. The claimant exhausted her administrative remedies and filed an action in court, also requesting attorney fees under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988. The trial court found in the claimant's favor and awarded fees. When DHS appealed, the appellate court upheld the trial court's decision. The court affirmed. The court rejected DHS's argument that the lower courts' actions violated the election of remedies doctrine. The election of remedies doctrine prohibited a litigant from seeking inconsistent remedies once a clear choice had been made to pursue a specific remedy, in order to prevent double recoveries. The court held that the claimant did not pursue inconsistent remedies by seeking attorney fees in her administrative appeal. Rather, she was entitled to attorney fees under § 1988 when she showed that the AFDC benefits were wrongfully terminated.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the award of attorney fees.

 

51 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Vogel v. Wells Fargo Guard Servs.


No. 03S01-9601-CV-00005


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


937 S.W.2d 856; 1996 Tenn. LEXIS 618



October 7, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Cumberland County. Hon. John Turnbull, Judge. NJ-2206.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, employer and state, sought review of a judgment by the trial court for Cumberland County (Tennessee) that held Tenn. Code Ann. § 50-6-207(4)(A)(i) (1995 Supp.) of the Workers' Compensation Reform Act of 1992 (Act), was unconstitutional under the Equal Protection Cause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV, because it unfairly discriminated between workers based on age. The trial court then awarded the appellee employee lifetime benefits.


OVERVIEW: Under Tenn. Code Ann. § 50-6-207(4)(A)(i) (1995 Supp.) of the Act, the employee who was 73 years of age when injured was entitled to only 260 weeks of compensation for his permanent and total disability. The employee claimed it was age discriminatory to award up to 400 weeks of benefits for those under age 65. With respect to the employee's equal protection claim, the court applied the rational basis level of scrutiny because his age was not a suspect class, and workers' compensation benefits were not fundamental rights that triggered a higher level of review. The court then held that § 50-6-207(4)(A)(i) was not unconstitutional because it was rationally related to the governmental purpose of paying workers' compensation benefits for lost wages only until the recipient reached the age upon which he was entitled to old-age Social Security benefits. The court also held that there was no violation of 29 U.S.C.S. § 623(a) of the Age Discrimination in Employment Act because age was not a factor in the disparity between terminations of benefits, but rather termination was based upon degree of disability, and while irrational there was no constitutional violation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that awarded the employee lifetime benefits under the Tennessee Worker's Compensation Act because it neither violated the equal protection clause nor the Age Discrimination in Employment Act when the term for payment of benefits was rationally related to the legitimate government purpose of providing benefits until the recipient became entitled to old-age Social Security benefits.

 

52 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Hooker v. Thompson


No. 01S01-9605-CH-00106


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


249 S.W.3d 331; 1996 Tenn. LEXIS 839



October 2, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Hooker v. Anderson, 12 Fed. Appx. 323, 2001 U.S. App. LEXIS 13818 (6th Cir. Tenn., 2001)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] EQUITY COURT. DAVIDSON COUNTY. Hon. Walter C. Kurtz, Chancellor by Interchange. Hon. Irvin H. Kilcrease, Jr., Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: TRIAL COURTS AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART AND MODIFIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant candidates sought review after appellee state refused to furnish the candidates with nominating petitions for a judgeship in an action that arose under Tenn. Code Ann. § 17-4-101, et seq. and the Tennessee Constitution. The Supreme Court assumed jurisdiction under Tenn. Code Ann. § 16-3-201(d). The case involved the right to hold or retain public office, was of unusual public importance, and required an expedited decision.


OVERVIEW: Both candidates sought to obtain a nominating petition from the state before the filing deadline, which the state refused to furnish. The candidates challenged the constitutionality of the Tennessee Plan: sitting judges ran unopposed and the public voted "yes" or "no" as to whether the judge should be retained. The court consolidated the appeals and held that the Tennessee Plan was constitutional, but that the statute had been violated in this case. Under Tenn. Code Ann. § 17-4-114(c), unless the judicial evaluation commission recommended retention of a judge running to fill an unexpired term of that judge's predecessor, the provisions of the Tennessee Plan for a yes/no retention vote did not apply, opening the race to the regular election laws. The judicial evaluation commission had not recommended retention of the sitting judge. No one had qualified under the general election laws to run for the unexpired term. The court exercised its equitable powers to extend the deadline. A vacancy in one of the "at large" positions for an unexpired term had to be filled by a resident of the grand division in which the vacancy occurred, which was that in which the "at large" judge resided.


OUTCOME: The court held that the Tennessee Plan was constitutional and that the "at large" vacancy created by the resignation of the judge whose seat had been filled by an interim appointment had to be filled by a resident of the grand division in which the vacancy originally occurred. The court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of one candidate's petition, an attorney whose license to practice had been suspended.

City of Tullahoma v. Bedford County


Appeal No. 01S01-9511-CH-00208


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


1996 Tenn. LEXIS 604



September 30, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Chancery Court. Bedford County. Hon. Cornelia A. Clark, Judge.



DISPOSITION: COURT OF APPEALS REVERSED; SUMMARY JUDGMENT ENTERED FOR PLAINTIFFS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant cities brought a declaratory judgment action against appellee county for a declaration that a private act authorizing the County Commission to impose a tax on the privilege of disposing of solid waste at landfills in the county violated the equal protection provisions of the Tennessee Constitution. The Court of Appeals (Tennessee) affirmed the trial court's order granting summary judgment in favor of the county. The cities appealed.


OVERVIEW: All landfills in the county were privately owned. The county alleged that the fee was imposed to reimburse the county for the additional costs of maintaining and repairing county roads, the employment of inspectors, and the purchase of equipment and test services to monitor the solid waste disposal. The cities alleged that 1991 Tenn. Priv. Acts, ch. 52 authorizing the County Commission to impose a tax on the privilege of disposing of solid waste in county landfills was in conflict with the Tennessee Solid Waste Management Act and other statutes regulating the disposal of solid waste. The court held that the fee imposed by the county violated the equal protection provisions of Tenn. Const. art. I, § 8, and U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1 because it imposed an obligation on the county citizens that was not imposed on citizens in other counties in the state. The court declared 1991 Tenn. Priv. Acts, ch. 52 invalid because it was inconsistent with general Tennessee laws that mandated a comprehensive plan for the control of solid waste in Tennessee. Because the county did not own and operate a landfill, it was not authorized by the general law to impose a landfill use fee.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the lower courts and entered summary judgment for the cities.

State v. Huddleston

SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON

State v. Huddleston, 1994 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 392 (Tenn. Crim. App., June 29, 1994)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Gibson County Circuit Court (Tennessee) upholding his conviction for aggravated robbery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his conviction for aggravated robbery. The court reversed the order of conviction and remanded the case for a new trial. The court found that defendant's rights under both Tenn. R. Crim. P. 5(a) and the Fourth Amendment to the United States Constitution were violated by the state's failure to seek prompt judicial determination of probable cause after defendant was arrested. The court further found that the violation of Rule 5(a) did not require that defendant's confession be suppressed because it was voluntarily given under the totality of circumstances. However, the court determined that suppression was required as a result of the Fourth Amendment violation. Finally, the court found that defendant's constitutional right to counsel was not violated.


OUTCOME: The order upholding defendant's conviction for aggravated robbery was reversed and the case was remanded for a new trial.

State v. Odom


No. 02-S-01-9502-CR-00014


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


928 S.W.2d 18; 1996 Tenn. LEXIS 360



June 3, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Rehearing Denied September 9, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Tenn. LEXIS 571 and 1996 Tenn. LEXIS 570.
Rehearing denied by State v. Odom, 1996 Tenn. LEXIS 570 (Tenn., Sept. 9, 1996)
Motion denied by State v. Odom, 1996 Tenn. LEXIS 571 (Tenn., Sept. 9, 1996)
Appeal after remand at State v. Odom, 2002 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 871 (Tenn. Crim. App., Oct. 15, 2002)


PRIOR HISTORY: Criminal Court. Shelby County. Hon. Joseph B. McCartie, Judge.
State v. Odom, 1994 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 689 (Tenn. Crim. App., Oct. 19, 1994)



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED; SENTENCE VACATED; REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Criminal Court of Shelby County (Tennessee), which convicted him of first-degree murder committed in the perpetration of rape and sentenced him to death by electrocution.


OVERVIEW: At defendant's sentencing hearing, the jury found three aggravating circumstances beyond a reasonable doubt that outweighed the mitigating circumstances to support his death sentence. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction, but vacated the death sentence and remanded for a new sentencing hearing. The court ruled that the standard for appellate review of trial court rulings on suppression issues was the "preponderance of the evidence" standard. The court determined that the "heinous, atrocious, or cruel" aggravating circumstance, Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-204(i)(5), was constitutional, but that the record did not support the jury's finding of this aggravating circumstance. The court held that the evidence did not support the jury's finding that defendant committed the murder during an escape from lawful custody. Further, the court found that the trial court's refusal to permit defendant to present mitigating evidence in the form of a psychologist's testimony constituted reversible error. The court concluded that the "no distinction" language in Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-204(e) required the trial court to specifically charge the jury on nonstatutory mitigating factors.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for first-degree murder committed in the perpetration of rape. The court vacated defendant's sentence of death by electrocution. The court remanded the cause for a new sentencing hearing to be conducted in a manner consistent with its opinion.

State v. Wood


No. 01-S-01-9501-CC-00015


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


924 S.W.2d 342; 1996 Tenn. LEXIS 303



May 6, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Circuit Court. Williamson County. Donald P. Harris, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court Williamson County (Tennessee), which convicted him of murder after a thirteen year delay between the issuance of a sealed presentment and the prosecution of the case.


OVERVIEW: A grand jury returned a sealed presentment that charged defendant with murder. A capias was not executed because defendant was in the custody of Alabama authorities on a different murder charge. Four years later the cause was placed on the "retired docket." Thereafter, a detainer was lodged against defendant. Although aware of the detainer, defendant did not assert his motion for speedy trial until 11 years after the presentment was returned. Subsequently, the case was prosecuted, over thirteen years after the return of the presentment. On appeal, the court held that the return of a sealed presentment engaged the right to speedy trial because it was a formal accusation that involved similar issues as the return of an unsealed indictment. The court applied the Barker analysis to determine whether defendant's rights were violated. The court found that the length and reason of the delay were not justified and weighed in defendant's favor. The court concluded, however, that defendant's right to speedy trial was not violated because his failure to assert his right and the lack of presumption of prejudice because of this failure overweighed the first two factors.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the preceding court.

McClellan v. Board of Regents of the State Univ.

Douglas v. State


No. 01S01-9508-CH-00138


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


921 S.W.2d 180; 1996 Tenn. LEXIS 253



April 22, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] CHANCERY COURT. DAVIDSON COUNTY. Hon. Irving Kilcrease, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: COURT OF APPEALS REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Tennessee State Board of Dentistry (board) appealed from a judgment of the Court of Appeals (Tennessee), which vacated the public reprimand issued by the board to appellee dentist for violation of the board's advertising rules and affirmed by the chancery court.


OVERVIEW: The board filed a notice of charges against the dentist, alleging that he had violated Tennessee State Board of Dentistry Rule 0460-2-.10(5)(b) by failing to state on his business cards and doorway that the orthodontic services he advertised were "being provided by a general dentist." After a hearing, the board found the dentist to be in violation of the rule. The dentist appealed the board's decision to the chancery court, and the chancery court affirmed. The dentist then sought review from the court of appeals, and the court of appeals reversed the judgment of the board and the chancery court and found the board's rule unconstitutional. On appeal, the court reversed the court of appeals' decision and affirmed the decision of the chancery court. The court concluded that the board rule passed constitutional muster, because the disclaimer at issue was scarcely burdensome at all. General dentists were merely required to include a one-sentence explanation in their advertisements of specialty branches, and the court held that this was not a sufficient burden to warrant the drastic action of striking a duly enacted administrative rule.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the court of appeals, which vacated the chancery court's public reprimand of the dentist, and the court affirmed the judgment of the chancery court.

 

59 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hines


No. 01-S-01-9303-CC-00052


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


1996 Tenn. LEXIS 149



March 11, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Criminal Court. Cheatham County.
State v. Hines, 919 S.W.2d 573, 1995 Tenn. LEXIS 503 (Tenn., 1995)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant had brought a petition for rehearing with the court to reconsider the affirmance of his murder conviction and death sentence relating to the trial court's instruction to the jury regarding the aggravating circumstance in Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-2-203(i) was unconstitutional and that the trial court committed constitutional error in its definition of the term "depravity."


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the instructions given regarding "depravity" were constitutionally insufficient. The trial court had instructed the jury that "depravity" meant moral corruption, wicked, or perverse act. The court continued to abide by its original holding that this aggravating circumstance had been constitutionally applied under the circumstances of the case. Although the instructions given by the trial judge were unconstitutionally vague, the failure to give a constitutionally proper instruction on depravity was harmless error beyond a reasonable doubt. The court found that the facts of the case fully satisfied the definitions of "torture" and "depravity." If there was constitutional error in the instruction on depravity, the result would have been the same had the aggravating circumstance been properly instructed. Any unconstitutional vagueness in the instruction given concerning "depravity' was harmless because the record established was sufficiently proved by evidence of torture independent of depravity. The court found that evidence of the stab wound to the vagina was sufficient to support a finding that the wounds were intentionally inflicted.


OUTCOME: The court found without merit the challenge presented in defendant's petition for rehearing regarding the constitutionally of the application of aggravating circumstances, and denied the petition for rehearing. Thus, the sentence of death, having been stayed, would be carried out as provided by law.

State v. Gray


NO. 01-S-01-9411-CR-00138


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


917 S.W.2d 668; 1996 Tenn. LEXIS 120



February 26, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] WILSON COUNTY. HON. JAMES O. BOND, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS REVERSED; JUDGMENT OF THE TRIAL COURT REINSTATED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Court of Criminal Appeals (Tennessee), which reversed the trial court's order, which dismissed the State's indictment charging defendant with the offense of carnal knowledge of a female under the age of 12.


OVERVIEW: Over 40 years after the incident occurred, defendant's niece claimed that he sexually assaulted her when she was 8 years old. Based on the accusations, defendant was charged with the offense of carnal knowledge of a female under the age of 12, but the trial court granted his motion to dismiss. The appellate court reversed the trial court, but the court disagreed with the appellate court and reinstated the trial court's order of dismissal. The court held that defendant's prosecution violated his due process rights. The court further held that the appellate court incorrectly decided the case based on its conclusion that the State was not the cause of the delay in charging defendant with the crime. The court then held that because defendant was charged under a savings clause, no statute of limitations applied to protect him from the stale prosecution. The court also held that the constitutional issue was dispositive of the case and that the unreasonable delay and the resultant prejudice to defendant required the dismissal of the indictment. Finally, the court held that prosecution of defendant would violate the concepts of fundamental fairness and substantial justice.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's order and reinstated the trial court's order, which dismissed the indictment against defendant.

Caldwell v. State


No. 02S01-9505-CC-00044


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


917 S.W.2d 662; 1996 Tenn. LEXIS 98



February 20, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected February 22, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: CRIMINAL COURT. MADISON COUNTY. Honorable Whit Lafon, Judge.



DISPOSITION: COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of the order of the Court of Criminal Appeals (Tennessee), which reversed the trial court's decision dismissing defendant's petition for post-conviction relief and remanded the case for an evidentiary hearing.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder. Both his conviction and his death sentence were affirmed on direct appeal. Thereafter, defendant admittedly filed his post-conviction relief petition well beyond the three year period of Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-30-102. He claimed that his confession should have been suppressed on the grounds that certain radio logs established that his arrest for public drunkenness was pretextual. The radio logs were not previously available. The trial court dismissed defendant's petition. The criminal appeals court reversed the trial court's decision and remanded the case for an evidentiary hearing. On appeal, the court reversed the order of the criminal appeals court. The court held that due process did not require the suspension of the § 40-30-102 limitations period because after balancing the legitimate State interests of precluding stale claims and limiting excessive costs against defendant's Fourth Amendment rights under the exclusionary rule, the State's interests were weightier. Further, the strict enforcement of § 40-30-102 did not deprive defendant of a reasonable opportunity to litigate his claim. Thus, the post-conviction relief petition was dismissed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the criminal appeals court that overturned the trial court's decision dismissing defendant's petition for post-conviction relief and ordered an evidentiary hearing. The court dismissed defendant's petition for post-conviction relief.

 

62 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Richardson v. Board of Dentistry


No. 01S01-9502-CH-00027


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE AT NASHVILLE


913 S.W.2d 446; 1995 Tenn. LEXIS 788



December 28, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Chancery Court, Davidson County, Hon. C. Allen High, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF COURT OF APPEALS REVERSED & CASE REMANDED TO TENNESSEE BOARD OF DENTISTRY


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state board of dentistry challenged the decision of the Court of Appeals (Tennessee), which declared Tenn. Code Ann. § 63-1-134 unconstitutional to the extent it authorized the assessment of civil penalties for acts otherwise declared to be criminal offenses, and dismissed charges brought by appellant and affirmed by the trial court against appellee dentist for practicing dentistry without a license.


OVERVIEW: Appellant state board of dentistry sought review of the appellate court's decision that declared Tenn. Code Ann. § 63-1-134 unconstitutional to the extent it authorized the assessment of civil penalties for acts otherwise declared to be criminal offenses, and dismissed charges against appellee dentist for practicing dentistry without a license in violation of Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 63-5-107, 121(2). The court found that the doctrine of collateral estoppel barred appellee's constitutional challenges because in a prior chancery proceeding deciding the same issues, appellee had failed to appeal pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 4-5-323. The court rejected appellee's claim of privilege against self-incrimination under U.S. Const. amend. V and Tenn. Const. art. I, § 9, because the criminal statute of limitations had run under Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-2-102. The court reversed the appellate court and remanded to appellee state board of dentistry for assessment of civil penalties.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court and remanded to appellee state board of dentistry because appellee dentist was barred by the doctrine of collateral estoppel from raising a constitutional challenge, and the Fifth Amendment privilege against self-incrimination was inapplicable in the proceedings because the statute of limitations had run on the alleged criminal offense arising from the matter.

 

63 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Brown v. Campbell County Bd. of Educ.


No. 03S01-9412-CH-00121, No. 03S01-9501-CH-00004


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


915 S.W.2d 407; 1995 Tenn. LEXIS 781



December 28, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended. Certiorari Denied May 28, 1996, Reported at: 1996 U.S. LEXIS 3465.


PRIOR HISTORY: Chancery Court. Campbell County. Chancellor Billy Joe White.

Chancery Court. Scott County. Chancellor Billy Joe White.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF TRIAL COURT REVERSED IN PART, AFFIRMED IN PART, AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, employers and the State, challenged the decisions of the Chancery Court of Campbell County and the Chancery Court of Scott County (Tennessee), which found that plaintiff employees were disabled. In both cases, the chancery courts found Tenn. Code Ann. § 50-6-241(a)(1) and (c) was unconstitutional because it violated the Equal Protection Clauses if both the Tennessee and Federal Constitutions.


OVERVIEW: Employees were allegedly disabled due to work related activities causing injuries. The trial court found that Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 50-6-241 and 50-6-242, which established the maximum disability awards for employees, were unconstitutional. Employers and the State appealed. The court held the proper standard of review was the rational basis test. The court found that the reasonable and legitimate state interests applicable to the multipliers - uniformity, fairness and predictability, were equally applicable to the use of the American Medical Association's Guides to the Evaluation of Permanent Impairment (Guides). The statutes fulfilled legitimate state interests and did not discriminate against those whose disabilities had to be rated by a method other than the Guides. The different treatment of workers who satisfied the criteria was based upon a reasonable difference. Thus, there was a rational basis for the distinction. Further the court found no basis for workers' claim that § 241 was in conflict the federal statutes. However, one of the worker's cases was remanded for further proof because it was obvious she had sustained substantial mental impairment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed in part; affirmed in part, and remanded the judgment of the trial court.

Estate of Jenkins v. Guyton


No. 01S01-9503-PB-00044


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


912 S.W.2d 134; 1995 Tenn. LEXIS 766



December 18, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] PROBATE COURT. DAVIDSON COUNTY. Hon. James Everett, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: COURT OF APPEALS AND TRIAL COURT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant estate sought review of a judgment from the Court of Appeals (Tennessee), which upheld a decision that refused to find appellee claimant's claim untimely, pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 30-2-306(c) (1989). The court of appeals held that § 30-2-306(c)'s six-month time period had been extended by Tenn. Code Ann. § 30-2-307(a)(1) (1989) because the claimant had not received actual notice under Tenn. Code Ann. § 30-2-306(e) (1989).


OVERVIEW: An order entered in the claimant's action against the decedent awarded the claimant damages and provided for a stay of execution upon the decedent's monthly payments. When the decedent died, the executor notified the claimant's attorney of the death and continued to make the payments. However, when the six-month period under Tenn. Code Ann. § 30-2-306(c) (1989) expired, the executor discontinued the payments, alleging the claimant had failed to file a timely claim against the estate. Thereafter, the claimant filed a claim against the estate, and when the trial court and the court of appeals rejected the untimeliness claim, the estate sought review. In affirming, the court held the estate had failed to give the claimant "actual notice" as required by Tenn. Code Ann. § 30-2-306(e) (1989) because the notification given to the attorney had not included information regarding: 1) the commencement of the probate proceedings; and 2) the time period for filing claims with the probate court. As such, the court held the period within which to file a claim had automatically been extended to one year from the decedent's death, pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 30-2-307(a)(1) (1989).


OUTCOME: In affirming a judgment which upheld a decision that refused to find the claimant's claim against the estate untimely, the court held the six-month time period had been extended because the claimant had not received actual notice.

 

65 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Newsom v. Biggers


No. 02-S-01-9408-CC-00054


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


911 S.W.2d 715; 1995 Tenn. LEXIS 704



November 20, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected December 4, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Criminal Court. Madison County. Franklin Murchison, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the sentence imposed by the Criminal Court of Madison County (Tennessee), which ordered a workhouse sentence of 11 months and 29 days and assessed a $ 100 fine. Appellant challenged the validity of his sentence on the ground that a judge who was not authorized by law to do so imposed it.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pled guilty to shoplifting and the trial court imposed a workhouse sentence of 11 months and 29 days and assessed a $ 100 fine. Appellant challenged the sentence on the ground that it was imposed by a judge who was not authorized by law to do so. The court affirmed the sentence and held that the judge had, at a minimum, de facto authority to render the judgment in appellant's case. The court held that the judge, because he was elected to a term of less than eight years, was not in compliance with Tenn. Const. art. IV, § 4; however, he was a de facto judge because the only irregularity in his appointment to the bench was the length of the term to which he was elected. It would have subverted the ends of justice to invalidate the acts of a judge who presided over the case with the consent of the parties. The court held that his judicial acts were valid and were not subject to collateral attack.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial judge, who imposed sentence on appellant, because the judge was a de facto judge.

 

66 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Davis v. State


NO. 02-S-01-9407-CR-00043


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


912 S.W.2d 689; 1995 Tenn. LEXIS 691



November 15, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] CRIMINAL COURT. SHELBY COUNTY. HON. ARTHUR R. BENNETT, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted, in separate trials, of rape and homicide. The trial court denied his petitions for post conviction relief. On direct appeal, the Court of Criminal Appeals (Tennessee) affirmed his convictions. Defendant sought review.


OVERVIEW: One of defendant's petitions for post-conviction relief concerned his convictions for aggravated kidnapping, rape, and robbery. The other petition concerned his conviction for homicide. The trial court denied the petitions. On direct appeal, his convictions were affirmed. On further review, the court affirmed the appellate court's judgment. The court determined that defendant's motion for expert assistance at the post-conviction level was properly denied because the state was not required to provide expert assistance to indigent non-capital post-conviction petitioners. The court rejected defendant's various contentions that he was denied effective assistance of counsel because he failed to show that there was a "reasonable probability" that but for counsel's deficient performance the result of the proceedings would have been different. Regarding the rape case the court noted that defense counsel's failure to pursue testing was a reasonable strategy, even if testing was requested. Therefore, counsel's performance was not deficient. Even if counsel did not act properly, defendant did not established that he was prejudiced by the error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's judgment that affirmed defendant's convictions for rape and homicide. The court also determined that defendant's petitions for post-conviction relief were properly denied by the trial court. The court remanded to the trial court for the implementation of its judgment and any further necessary proceedings.

 

67 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


State v. Barnett


No. 03-S-01-9410-CR-00094


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


909 S.W.2d 423; 1995 Tenn. LEXIS 672



November 13, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] CRIMINAL COURT. CLAIBORNE COUNTY. HON. W. LEE ASBURY, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision from the Court of Criminal Appeals (Tennessee), which affirmed the trial court's denial of defendant's request for appointment of a state-funded psychiatric expert to assist the defense. Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder and sentenced to life in prison. He relied on the defense of insanity and voluntary intoxication. Defendant had a history of mental and emotional disturbance.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court concluded that a United States Supreme Court decision providing for appointment of a psychiatrist under certain circumstances was limited to capital cases and that there was no Tennessee authority for appointment in non-capital cases. On appeal, defendant argued that the denial of his motion for appointment of a psychiatric expert deprived him of his right to a fair trial guaranteed by the Due Process Clause of both the Tennessee and United States Constitutions. The court held that when a defendant in a non-capital case demonstrates to the trial court in an ex parte proceeding that his sanity at the time of the offense is to be a significant factor at trial, the federal constitution, at a minimum, requires the state to provide defendant access to a competent, independent psychiatrist who will conduct an appropriate examination and assist in evaluation, preparation, and presentation of the defense. The court affirmed where defendant failed to make the required threshold showing of particularized need for the psychiatric expert he sought. The court held that in the context of a request for a psychiatric expert, an ex parte hearing is required.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's affirmation of the trial court's denial of defendant's request for appointment of a state-funded psychiatric expert to assist the defense.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The prosecution appealed a judgment from the Tennessee Court of Criminal Appeals, which, in a drunk driving case, reversed the trial court's order dismissing defendant's petition for post-conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: After three convictions for driving under the influence (DUI), defendant's license to drive was revoked. DISPOSITION: COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS REVERSED; TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT REINSTATED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state challenged a judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals (Tennessee), which reversed a denial of petitioner's second application for post-conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Subsequent to his conviction and denial of post-conviction relief in his first application, petitioner filed a second application. Petitioner argued that issues raised in the second application were not barred because he did not receive a full and fair hearing in the first proceeding. On review, the court reversed the judgment of the lower appellate court. In reaching its conclusion, the court held that petitioner had received a full and fair hearing in the original proceeding because an evidentiary hearing was held, and petitioner was afforded every opportunity to present evidence. The court noted that petitioner had no constitutional right to counsel during the post-conviction proceeding. The court then held that petitioner was not entitled to an evidentiary hearing to rebut the presumption of waiver of a ground for relief because his petition did not establish a legal excuse for not having raised the issue on direct appeal or in the original post-conviction proceeding.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower appellate court's judgment and reinstated the denial of petitioner's second application for post-conviction relief.

In re Burson


No. 01-S-01-9209-OT-00103


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


909 S.W.2d 768; 1995 Tenn. LEXIS 509



September 11, 1995, FILED



DISPOSITION:  [**1] REPORT OF SPECIAL MASTER AFFIRMED AS MODIFIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner attorney general and state board of equalization requested a determination of whether Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-5-1514 (1994), which provided that taxpayers contesting tax assessments could be represented by non-attorney agents, was constitutional in light of constitutional separation of powers principles regarding authority to regulate the practice of law.


OVERVIEW: Local and state board of equalization procedures allowed non-attorney agents to represent taxpayers who contested real and personal property tax assessments. The attorney general and the state board of equalization filed a petition for a determination of whether Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-5-1514 (1994) violated separation of powers provisions of the Tennessee Constitution. The special master assigned to the case held an evidentiary hearing, reviewed the briefs submitted, and recommended that the services performed by non-attorney agents did not constitute the practice of law and that the legislature was acting within its constitutional authority when it adopted § 1514. The court agreed that § 1514 did not authorize the practice of law by non-attorneys and that the legislature was within its constitutional power by enacting the statute. However, the court also ruled that it possessed not only the inherent supervisory power to regulate the practice of law, but also the corollary power to prevent the unauthorized practice of law. Whether a person was engaged in the practice of law depended upon whether the person was required to use the professional judgment of a lawyer.


OUTCOME: The court modified the special master's report and affirmed it as modified.

72 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


State v. Walker


02S01-9405-CC-00018


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


905 S.W.2d 554; 1995 Tenn. LEXIS 430



August 14, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Madison County. Hon. Franklin Murchison. (Lower Court No. C-92-215). Appeal Nos. 02-C-01-9304-CC-00066, 02-C-01-9304-CC-00067.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND DISMISSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of a judgment from the Court of Criminal Appeals (Tennessee), which affirmed the trial court's holding that their sentences did not begin to run until they were actually taken into custody.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were convicted of driving under the influence and each sentenced to 11 months and 20 days imprisonment with all but the 20 days suspended. The day after their sentences were imposed, they reported to the sheriff's office to begin serving their time. The sheriff turned them away because there was no space available and informed them that they would be notified when to report. One defendant was told to report two years later, the other defendant was told to report a year later. The lower court found that the mere expiration of time without confinement was not an execution of a criminal judgment. Upon review, the court reversed. Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-23-103 required the sheriff to commit a defendant to jail as soon as possible. Under Tenn. Code Ann. § 41-4-121, the sheriff was to commit them to the nearest sufficient jail. There was no proof in the record of the sheriff's attempt to find the nearest sufficient jail. The court held that when a defendant presented himself to the appropriate authorities for incarceration and was turned away, his sentence began to run when the judgment of conviction became final or when he was actually incarcerated, whichever was earlier.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the finding that defendants' sentences did not begin to run until they were actually taken into custody. The court dismissed the sentences imposed against them.

 

73 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Watkins v. State


No. 02S01-9405-CR-00016


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


903 S.W.2d 302; 1995 Tenn. LEXIS 340



July 3, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Criminal Court. Shelby County. Hon. H. T. Lockard, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS AFFIRMED; CASE REMANDED TO TRIAL COURT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent State appealed from the Criminal Court of Shelby County (Tennessee), which found that the statutory three-year limitation for filing a petition for post-conviction relief was suspended while petitioner prisoner was mentally incompetent.


OVERVIEW: The court found that the petition for relief was facially sufficient and if it was not barred by the statute of limitations, the prisoner was entitled to the appointment of counsel and a hearing on the petition. However, the petition was time-barred unless the limitation of the action was suspended by the prisoner's mental incompetence. The trial court found that the petition was suspended by the prisoner's mental incompetence. The court on appeal found that decision was supported by statute, Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-30-102, and by principles of due process. Where the prisoner was mentally incompetent and therefore legally incapable, he would be denied any opportunity to assert his constitutional rights in a post-conviction petition unless the period of limitations was suspended during his mental incompetence. Due process required that some reasonable opportunity to assert those rights be afforded.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and remanded to the trial court for further proceedings on the petition for post-conviction relief.

State v. Shepherd


No. 03S01-9201-CR-00002


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


902 S.W.2d 895; 1995 Tenn. LEXIS 269



May 30, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] CRIMINAL COURT. BRADLEY COUNTY. Hon. Mayo Mashburn, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction from the Criminal Court, Bradley County (Tennessee), in which he was found guilty on one count of felony murder in the commission of rape and one count of aggravated assault. Defendant was sentenced to death on the first count and 2-5 years imprisonment on the second.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of felony murder in the commission of rape and aggravated assault and was sentenced to death on the first count and 2-5 years imprisonment on the second. Defendant appealed his convictions and the court affirmed, holding that: 1) as the evidence showed that the victim was healthy at the time of her death, an expert's testimony that asphyxiation was the most likely cause of her death was supported by defendant's own statement that she may have been alive when he buried her; 2) although the expert's testimony indicated any evidence of sperm could have degenerated while the body was buried, there was adequate evidence of attempted rape in that defendant tried to force the victim to have sex with him; 3) defendant's aggressive behavior and confrontation of police officers with a loaded shotgun supported the aggravated assault conviction; and 4) defendant's statements to police were admissible as they were freely and voluntarily given after he was advised of his Miranda rights. The court found that the trial court committed error in employing the felony murder aggravating circumstance at sentencing, and thus the court remanded the case for resentencing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, with costs to defendant, defendant's convictions for felony murder in the commission of rape and aggravated assault, but remanded the case for resentencing without the use of the felony murder aggravating circumstance.

Simmons v. Simmons


No. 03S01-9406-CV-00052


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


900 S.W.2d 682; 1995 Tenn. LEXIS 271



May 30, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Law Court. Hawkins County. Hon. Ben K. Wexler, Judge.



DISPOSITION: COURT OF APPEALS AND TRIAL COURT REVERSED; PETITION TO TERMINATE APPELLEES' VISITATION GRANTED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent grandparents appealed a decision of the Tennessee Court of Appeals, which, finding no change in circumstances, refused to terminate grandparents' court authorized visitation privileges upon the application of appellant mother and her husband, the minor child's adoptive father.


OVERVIEW: The court held that Tenn. Const. art. I, § 8 protected the privacy interest of parents in their child-rearing decisions as long as their decisions did not substantially endanger the welfare of their children. The court found that the trial court had based its decision on the finding that the mother had failed to prove a change of circumstances on which to terminate grandparents' visitation privileges. The court reiterated that change of circumstances was not the standard for determining the parents' right to refuse visitation to a non-parent, but that the issue was whether the child was in danger of substantial harm. Therefore, without evidence that the child was in danger of substantial harm, the mother and adoptive father were entitled to constitutional protection of their parental rights. The court reversed the appellate court's decision and granted mother's petition to terminate grandparents' visitation privileges.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the denial of mother's petition to terminate grandparents' visitation privileges and granted the petition.

Tennessee Small Sch. Sys. v. McWherter


Appeal No. 01S01-9404-CH-00040


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


894 S.W.2d 734; 1995 Tenn. LEXIS 45



February 16, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at, Remanded by Tenn. Small Sch. Sys. v. McWherter, 91 S.W.3d 232, 2002 Tenn. LEXIS 425 (Tenn., 2002)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Chancery Court. Davidson County. Hon. C. Allen High, Chancellor.
Tennessee Small Sch. Sys. v. McWherter, 851 S.W.2d 139, 1993 Tenn. LEXIS 114 (Tenn., 1993)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF CHANCERY COURT MODIFIED; CASE REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In previous litigation, the court made rulings regarding the public education system. In the instant case, appellant small school systems sought review of an order of the Chancery Court of Davidson County, Tennessee, which, in the small school systems suit against defendants, governor and others (collectively state), denied the small school systems' demand that funding for all local school systems be equalized immediately.


OVERVIEW: In a prior case, the court held that the Tennessee Constitution guaranteed to the school children of Tennessee the right to a free public education and imposed upon the General Assembly the obligation to maintain and support a system of free public schools that afforded substantially equal educational opportunities to all students. While that case was pending, the Basic Education Program (BEP) was implemented by the state. The small school systems were displeased with the BEP and filed suit. On appeal, the small school systems argued that the statutory funding scheme violated equal protection because complete equalization was accomplished over a period of years rather than immediately and because the plan contained no provision for equalizing teachers' salaries. The court held that the an incremental equalization of funding under the BEP was acceptable but found that exclusion of teachers' salary increases from the equalization formula substantially impaired the objectives of the plan. Consequently, the court modified the plan to include equalization of teachers' salaries according to the BEP formula. The plan, as modified, was approved for the purposes of the proceeding.


OUTCOME: The court modified the judgment of the trial court and remanded the case for further proceedings.

 

77 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


State v. Walker


No. 03S01-9311-CR-00071


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


893 S.W.2d 429; 1995 Tenn. LEXIS 26



January 30, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] CRIMINAL COURT. HAMILTON COUNTY. Hon. Joseph F. Di Riso, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Hamilton County Criminal Court (Tennessee) of a reckless killing committed in the perpetration of, or attempt to perpetrate, a robbery. Defendant was sentenced to life imprisonment. The single issue raised on appeal concerned the constitutionality of Tennessee's felony murder statute. Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-202.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and a co-defendant decided that they would rob a drug dealer. Defendant admitted shooting the victim during the robbery but alleged that the discharge of the murder weapon was inadvertent. Defendant argued that Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-202, as it related to the felony murder rule, was unconstitutional under U.S. Const. amends. IV and V, and Tenn. Const. art. I, § 8. The court disagreed holding that under Tennessee's statutory definition of felony murder the prosecution was not required to prove the elements of malice, deliberation, and premeditation, or that the defendant intended to kill the victim. The jury was afforded the opportunity to consider whether the acts committed by defendant conformed to the mutually exclusive statutory definitions of murder in the first degree, the second degree, or criminally negligent homicide. The trial court correctly charged the jury, explaining the requisite elements of each offense as well as the punishment prescribed. The jury returned a constitutionally sound verdict of murder in the first degree as the result of a reckless killing in the perpetration of a robbery. Accordingly, the judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed.

Shell v. State


No. 02S01-9401-BC-00085


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


893 S.W.2d 416; 1995 Tenn. LEXIS 14



January 17, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Rehearing Denied February 21, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Tenn. LEXIS 51.


PRIOR HISTORY: TENNESSEE CLAIMS COMMISSION. Hon. C.E. Murray Commissioner.



DISPOSITION: COURT OF APPEALS AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant citizens brought an action pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 9-8-307(a)(1)(N) against appellee State for negligent deprivation of their constitutional rights and professional malpractice in the form of prosecutorial misconduct in the investigation of reports of child sexual abuse in a day care center at which the citizens worked. A court of appeals (Tennessee) affirmed the dismissal of the citizens' action. The citizens sought review.


OVERVIEW: The State argued that the citizens' action was barred by the one-year statute of limitations for personal injury actions contained in Tenn. Code Ann. § 28-3-104 and alternatively, that amendments to Tenn. Code Ann. § 9-8-307(a)(1)(N), which eliminated a cause of action for negligent deprivation of a constitutional right, were to be applied retroactively to bar the citizens' action. The court found that statutes should be applied prospectively unless the legislative history clearly indicated a contrary content and that there was no such intent in this instance. Further, the court explained that remedial or procedural statutes could be applied retroactively, but that § 9-8-403(a)(1)(N) was neither remedial or procedural. The court held that although the citizens' action was based on the deprivation of constitutional rights, it was actually a negligence action and negligence law should govern when the cause of action accrued. The court concluded that the injuries alleged by the citizens occurred more than one year before they filed their complaint, and as a result, their complaint was barred by the statute of limitations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

79 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


State v. Smith


S.C. No. 02S01-9111-CR-00061


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


893 S.W.2d 908; 1994 Tenn. LEXIS 278



October 3, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition to Rehear Denied in part and Granted in part February 21, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Tenn. LEXIS 48.


PRIOR HISTORY: CRIMINAL Court. SHELBY County. Hon. Joseph B. McCartie, Judge. (Lower Court No. 90-10395)



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED; SENTENCE OF DEATH AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In accordance with the jury's verdict and recommendation, the Criminal Court of Shelby County (Tennessee) convicted defendant of first-degree felony murder and sentenced him to death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: After attending Sunday school and church, an elderly woman had her throat cut twice after she was raped and beaten. Drowning also played a role in the victim's death, as she was found lying in about two inches of bloody water in the bathtub. Upon being instructed in accordance with the law in effect at the time of the offense, the jury recommended the death penalty after it found defendant guilty of first-degree felony murder. The state supreme court affirmed, holding that the evidence was sufficient to support the finding of guilt and the finding of the heinous, atrocious, and cruel aggravating factor. The court held that the 1989 amendments to the capital sentencing statute did not apply to sentencing conducted after the effective date of the amendments for capital offenses committed before the effective date. Moreover, the sentencing jury's consideration of the invalid felony murder aggravating circumstance was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt where there were two remaining aggravating circumstances. Finally, although "mentally retarded" persons could not be sentenced to death, the record was inadequate to find that defendant suffered deficits in his adaptive behavior.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's first-degree felony murder conviction and death sentence.

State v. Bigbee

DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED; SENTENCE REVERSED; REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his felony murder conviction and death sentence, both imposed by the Criminal Court of Sumner County (Tennessee), raising numerous grounds for relief.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court upheld defendant's conviction but reversed his sentence, remanding the case for a resentencing hearing. As to defendant's conviction, the court held that there was sufficient evidence to convict defendant, that the jury instructions on accomplice testimony were correct, that an impartial jury was provided, that favorable evidence was not withheld, and that there were no prejudicial evidentiary errors at the guilt and innocence phase of the trial. Other sentencing issues were also reviewed.


OUTCOME: Defendant's felony murder conviction was affirmed. However, defendant's sentence was reversed and remanded.

 

81 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Barker v. Harmon


NO. 01-S-01-9311-CV-00154


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


882 S.W.2d 352; 1994 Tenn. LEXIS 233



August 1, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] LAW COURT. SEQUATCHIE COUNTY. HON. WILLIAM H. INMAN, JUDGE, BY DESIGNATION



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART; AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State challenged an order of the Court of Appeals (Tennessee), which affirmed the trial court's finding that 1983 Tenn. Priv. Acts ch. 79 violated Tenn. Const. art. VI, § 7 in that it was an unconstitutional increase in compensation during a judge's term of office but reversed the finding that the doctrine of elision could not be applied to save the constitutionality of the act in a mandamus action against appellee county executives.


OVERVIEW: A non-lawyer bus driver was elected to an eight-year term as a general sessions judge for the county. During his term, he and the county attorney drafted a proposed private act authorizing a monthly expense allowance for his position. The county commission ratified the act, the judge received monthly allowances and gave up his other job. The judge sought a writ of mandamus when the general assembly eliminated the allowance. The trial court found that the act was unconstitutional, the appellate court agreed but applied the doctrine of elision to save the act's validity, and ordered the judge to repay the allowance received. On appeal, the court affirmed the unconstitutionality and reversed the elision, finding that (1) the expense allowance was an illegal increase in the judge's compensation; (2) elision could not be applied because there was no severability clause, the general assembly enacted new legislation restructuring judges' salaries, and it was inconceivable that the private act would have been passed without an effective date; and (3) the judge was not required to repay allowances received because he reasonably relied on the validity of the act in giving up his other job.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the unconstitutionality of the private act, reversed the application of the doctrine of elision, and reversed the order requiring the judge to repay monthly allowances received under the private act.
