State v. Tester


NO. 03-S-01-9311-CR-00074


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


879 S.W.2d 823; 1994 Tenn. LEXIS 172



June 20, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] CRIMINAL COURT. WASHINGTON COUNTY. HON. ARDEN L. HILL, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART; AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed from the judgment of the Criminal Court, Washington County (Tennessee), which, pursuant to a work release statute, Tenn. Code Ann. § 41-2-128(c) (1990 & Supp. 1993), permitted defendant to serve his 50-day sentence for second offense driving under the influence of a drug or intoxicant (DUI) in a work release program rather than in jail.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty in Washington County of second offense DUI and was to be sentenced to 50 days in jail. At his sentencing hearing, defendant challenged the constitutionality of Tenn. Code Ann. § 41-2-128(c)(9) (1990 & Supp. 1993), which limited application of the work release statute to Davidson, Moore, and Shelby Counties. The trial court held that the statute was unconstitutional to the extent that its applicability was limited to three counties. The trial court elided the unconstitutional portion, held that the remainder of the statute was constitutional, and applied it to defendant, permitting him to serve his sentence in a work release program. On appeal, the court affirmed the holding that the limiting provision was unconstitutional, but reversed the holding that the remainder of the statute was constitutional and could be applied to defendant. The court held that there was no rational basis for distinguishing between three counties and all other state counties. Because the court was unable to conclude that the legislature would have enacted § 41-2-128(c) without the limiting provision, it held that the unconstitutional provision could not be elided.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the portion of the trial court's judgment holding that the limiting provision of the work release statute was unconstitutional, reversed the portion of the trial court's judgment eliding the unconstitutional limitation and applying the remainder of the statute to defendant, and remanded the matter to the trial court for resentencing.

 

83 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


State v. Turner


No. 02S01-9309-CC-00064


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


879 S.W.2d 819; 1994 Tenn. LEXIS 168



June 13, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] CRIMINAL COURT. BENTON COUNTY. Hon. C. Creed McGinley, Judge



DISPOSITION: TRIAL COURT AND COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the decision of the Court of Criminal Appeals (Tennessee), which affirmed his conviction on one count of incest and one count of sexual battery.


OVERVIEW: On appeal from his conviction, defendant contended that the trial court improperly barred him from striking female jurors from the venire and counsel admitted that he wanted a male jury. The appellate court affirmed the conviction, finding that defendant's counsel had admitted that he was trying to get a sympathetic jury, which the appellate court held was impermissible. On further review, the court affirmed, but disagreed with the appellate court's reasoning for the affirmance. The court held that the peremptory strike process contemplated that each party would exhibit blatant self-interest by choosing sympathetic jurors and that the ultimate impartiality of the jury would be the collective product of these clashing expressions of self-interest. Therefore, it was permissible to select a sympathetic jury. However, peremptory strikes based solely on the basis of gender violated the Equal Protection Clause because jurors had a right not to be excluded summarily based on stereotypes. Thus, the trial court properly barred defendant from striking female jurors.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for incest and sexual battery was affirmed.

In re Brown


S. Ct. No. 01S01-9306-0T-00087


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


879 S.W.2d 801; 1994 Tenn. LEXIS 170



June 13, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Court of the Judiciary



DISPOSITION: COURT OF THE JUDICIARY AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant judge sought review of a judgment from the Court of the Judiciary (Tennessee), which imposed a public reprimand after finding that the judge violated Tenn. Code of Judicial Conduct Canons 2A, 3A(3).


OVERVIEW: The judiciary court found that the judge violated the judicial conduct code (code) by making certain statements in open court and by failing to timely respond to the proceedings against him in the judiciary court. The court reversed the judgment insofar as it found that the judge's statements violated the code. Although the court questioned the wisdom of the judge's comments regarding the juvenile court, it found that they did not violate the code because the comments did not impair public confidence in the judiciary. While the judge's language was harsh, his statements were not directed at the juvenile court judge personally, except to the extent that the procedures under review were made necessary by the fact that the juvenile court judge was not a lawyer. Viewed in context, the court found that the comments directed at the perceived inadequacies in the structure and operation of the juvenile court system were appropriate subjects for criticism. The court affirmed the judgment insofar as it related to the judge's response. The court found that the judge's cavalier attitude toward the proceedings against him detracted from his avowed respect for the law and its processes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed that part of the judgment, which found that the judge's delay in responding to the complaint constituted a violation of the code and which imposed a public reprimand. The court reversed that part of the judgment, which found that the judge's statements regarding the juvenile court constituted a violation of the code.

State v. Keen


No. 02S01-9112-CR-00064


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Criminal Court, Shelby County (Tennessee), which convicted him on his guilty plea to murder in the first degree, perpetration of rape, and aggravated rape, and sentenced him to death for the murder and to a 20-year consecutive sentence for the aggravated rape.


OVERVIEW: The charges against defendant were based on his rape and murder of an eight-year-old girl. OUTCOME: The court remanded for defendant's resentencing.

State v. Stephenson


No. 03-S-01-9103-CR-00024


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


878 S.W.2d 530; 1994 Tenn. LEXIS 143



May 9, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Rehearing Denied June 20, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Tenn. LEXIS 203.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] CRIMINAL COURT. COCKE COUNTY. HON. J. KENNETH PORTER, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AFFIRMED; REVERSED AND REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Criminal Court of Cocke County (Tennessee) convicting him of first-degree premeditated murder and conspiracy to commit first-degree murder and, finding the existence of an aggravating circumstance, sentencing defendant to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first-degree premeditated murder and conspiracy to commit first-degree murder. The jury, after finding the aggravating circumstance that defendant had employed another to commit the murder for remuneration, sentenced defendant to death. On appeal, the court affirmed the convictions, but reversed the sentence of death and remanded for resentencing. The court noted that defendant was sentenced under an old statute and verdict form that imposed a lower standard of proof resulting in a facially void verdict and prejudicial error. The court held that the imposition of the death penalty required a jury finding that the state had proven beyond a reasonable doubt that the aggravating circumstance or circumstances outweighed any mitigating circumstances. In affirming the conviction, the court held that the right against self-incrimination set forth in Tenn. Const. art. I, § 9 did not require that law enforcement officials inform a suspect that an attorney was present and attempting to see him before the suspect could make a voluntary and knowing waiver of his state constitutional right to counsel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction, but reversed the sentence of death and remanded for resentencing, holding that defendant had not been sentenced under the current statute and verdict form that required a finding that the state had proven beyond a reasonable doubt that the aggravating circumstance or circumstances outweighed any mitigating circumstances.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant client and attorney general sought review of the decision of the Equity Court, Shelby County (Tennessee) that found appellant had no cause of action against appellee attorney because the state's statute that limited the percentage contingency fee appellee could charge was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant client and appellee attorney entered into a contingency fee agreement wherein appellee would represent appellant and would receive 50 percent of any recovery. Eventually the underlying case was completed and appellee received his fee but appellant filed suit against him based on Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-26-120 which limits the contingency amount to 331/3 percent of any recovery. The court first found that the statute was a reflection of the state's public policy, that the contingency fee between the parties violated the statute, and that appellant's suit to avoid the contract was cognizable and proper. The court then found that the statute did not violate the equal protection provision of the U.S. Const. amend. XIV and the state constitution. The court applied the rational basis analysis and determined the Tenn. Code Ann. §29-26-120 did not violate equal protection or due process.


OUTCOME: Lower court decision that found appellant client had no cause of action against appellee attorney because the state's statute that limited the percentage contingency fee appellee could charge was unconstitutional was reversed and remanded.

State v. Nichols


No. 03-S-01-9105-CR-00047


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


877 S.W.2d 722; 1994 Tenn. LEXIS 135



May 2, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Counsel Corrected May 9, 1994. Petition for Rehearing Denied June 20, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Tenn. LEXIS 202.
Rehearing denied by State v. Nichols, 1994 Tenn. LEXIS 202 (Tenn., June 20, 1994)
Writ of certiorari denied Nichols v. Tennessee, 513 U.S. 1114, 115 S. Ct. 909, 130 L. Ed. 2d 791, 1995 U.S. LEXIS 589 (1995)
Related proceeding at State v. Nichols, 1995 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 998 (Tenn. Crim. App., Dec. 19, 1995)
Post-conviction relief denied at Nichols v. State, 2001 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 47 (Tenn. Crim. App., Jan. 19, 2001)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] HAMILTON COUNTY. HON. DOUGLAS A. MEYER, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: DEATH SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The trial court (Tennessee) sentenced defendant to death following his pleas of guilty to first-degree felony murder and other charges. On appeal, defendant alleged errors in the sentencing phase, which included: changing venue for jury selection, permitting discovery of an expert's interview notes, and using felony murder as an aggravating circumstance.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to first-degree felony murder and was sentenced to death. He sought review, asserting numerous errors in the sentencing phase, including a change of venue for the limited purpose of jury selection, Tenn. Const. art. I, § 9; permitting discovery of a psychologist's interview notes, Tenn. R. Crim. P. 16(b)(1)(B); and using the aggravating circumstance that the murder occurred during a rape, Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-204(i)(2). The court affirmed. It examined the record of the sentencing hearing and concluded that any trial errors committed during the sentencing phase were harmless error beyond a reasonable doubt and had not affected the jury's verdict of death. Although the use of the aggravating circumstance of the felony murder violated Tenn. Const. art. I, § 16, U.S. Const. amend. VIII, the sentencing jury's consideration of the invalid circumstance was harmless error beyond a reasonable doubt. Defendant's change of venue motion constituted a waiver of his Tenn. Const. art. I, § 9, rights. In the absence of any other records of an expert's evaluation of defendant, records of his interview with defendant and others were discoverable under Rule 16(b)(1)(B).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the jury's sentence of death imposed after defendant pleaded guilty to first-degree murder. The unconstitutional use of the felony-murder aggravating circumstance was harmless error because it did not affect the sentence imposed. Defendant waived objections to the change of venue. A psychologist's interview records were properly discoverable as reports that formed the basis for his expert opinion.

State v. Superior Oil


No. 01-S-01-9311-CR-00164


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


875 S.W.2d 658; 1994 Tenn. LEXIS 110



April 11, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DAVIDSON County. CRIMINAL Court. HON. THOMAS H. SHRIVER, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State of Tennessee appealed a decision of the Davidson County Criminal Court (Tennessee), which upheld the constitutionality of the Water Quality Control Act of 1977, Tenn. Code Ann. § 69-3-101, et seq., in the State's action against defendant alleging violations of the Act.


OVERVIEW: The grand jury indicted defendants for violations of the Act, and defendants sought dismissal of the indictments because the State had not obtained permission to prosecute as required by Tenn. Code Ann. § 69-3-115(d). The trial court granted defendants' motion to dismiss, holding the Act constitutional. The State appealed, contending that the Act was unconstitutional because it impermissibly interfered with the prosecutorial discretion inherent in the constitutional office of district attorney general, and because it infringed upon the independent investigative authority of the grand jury. The court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded, holding that because § 69-3-115(d) required that the district attorney general or the grand jury obtain authorization from the Commissioner of the Department of Health and Environment or the Water Quality Control Board before instituting criminal proceedings, it impermissibly interfered with the district attorney's discretion and responsibility and the grand jury's power and function and, therefore, violated Tenn. Const. art. VI, § 5; art. I, § 14. The court applied the doctrine of elision and upheld the remainder of the Act.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment dismissing the indictments against defendants and upholding the constitutionality of the Act, and remanded for further proceedings consistent with the court's determination that the Act was unconstitutional.

Nale v. Robertson


No. 01S01-9308-CV-00126


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


871 S.W.2d 674; 1994 Tenn. LEXIS 36



February 18, 1994, Decided  
February 18, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Law Court. Davidson County. Hon. Harry S. Lester Judge



DISPOSITION: PETITION FOR LEGITIMATION GRANTED; PETITION FOR ADOPTION DISMISSED; CASE REMANDED TO TRIAL COURT WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, foster parents and adoption service, filed for the parents' adoption of a baby boy. Respondent natural father opposed the adoption and filed a petition for legitimation after the service filed a motion to terminate his parental rights. The Court of Appeals (Tennessee) reversed the trial court's judgment that granted the parents' petition, dismissed the father's petition, and remanded for further proceedings on the legitimation issue.


OVERVIEW: The father filed a notice of intent to claim paternity of the child. The services filed a termination of parental rights petition in juvenile court and the father responded by filing a petition to legitimate the child. The parents then filed this adoption petition. Initially, the parents claimed that the father abandoned the child, but they amended their petition to assert that the adoption was in the child's best interests. The trial court granted the parents' petition notwithstanding the father's pending legitimation proceeding. The court held that this was error. The state and federal constitutions required that the father's parental rights be determined prior to the adoption petition being considered. Thus, the court held that the portion of Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-1-111 that allowed courts to enter an adoption decree based on the child's interests without a prior judicial termination of the parental rights pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 37-1-147 et seq. was constitutionally invalid. The appellate court erred in remanding the case for further proceedings. The father had established a fundamental right to a relationship with his child and was entitled to have his petition granted.


OUTCOME: The court granted the father's petition for legitimation and dismissed the parents' adoption petition. The court remanded the case to the trial court for the entry of an order whereby custody was to be transferred to the father.

State v. Chastain


No. 03-S-01-9308-CR-00051


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


871 S.W.2d 661; 1994 Tenn. LEXIS 26



February 14, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] BLOUNT COUNTY. CRIMINAL COURT. HON. D. KELLY THOMAS, JR., JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Blount County Court (Tennessee), which held that an act authorizing challenges of prior driving under the influence (DUI) convictions when being convicted of a third DUI was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested and charged with DUI. Because defendant had been convicted of two earlier DUI offenses, he was indicted for a third offense DUI, which provided for greater punishment than a first or second offense. Using Tenn. Code Ann. § 55-10-403(1) (Act) as authority, defendant filed a motion to strike his two earlier DUI convictions because of alleged constitutional deficiencies in those prior guilty pleas. The State countered by asking the trial court to declare the Act unconstitutional. The trial court agreed with the State and declared the Act unconstitutional. Defendant appealed and the court affirmed. The issue was that the Act was in direct conflict with the Post-Conviction Act. The court concluded that the state attorney general and district attorneys general had authority within circumscribed limits to challenge the constitutionality of a statute directly conflicting with or impliedly repealing another statute upon which the prosecution relied in the execution of its legal duties. Having so concluded, the court affirmed the trial court judgment holding that the Act violated the dictates of Tenn. Const. art. II, § 17.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which declared the Act unconstitutional.

State v. Cazes


No. 02-S-01-9103-CR-00005


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


875 S.W.2d 253; 1994 Tenn. LEXIS 28



February 14, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Rehearing Denied April 4, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Tenn. LEXIS 107.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] CRIMINAL COURT. SHELBY COUNTY. HON. JOSEPH B. McCARTIE, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Criminal Court, Shelby County (Tennessee), entered judgment, upon a jury verdict, convicting defendant of first-degree felony murder in the perpetration of a rape, aggravated rape, and first-degree burglary. After the sentencing hearing, the jury found that there were no mitigating circumstances outweighing the aggravating circumstances and sentenced defendant to death by electrocution. Appeal followed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant allegedly entered an elderly woman's home, beat her to death with a hammer, and sexually abused her. He argued that his conviction and sentence were invalid because the trial court committed errors at trial and at sentencing. The court disagreed and affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence. The medical examiner's testimony that the sexual penetration occurred at the time of death or shortly thereafter supported the finding of the elements of aggravated rape beyond a reasonable doubt. The circumstantial evidence, including defendant's fingerprints and his possession of a chipping hammer, unerringly pointed the finger of guilt at him alone. There was no indication that the trial court abused its discretion in denying individual, sequestered voir dire of prospective juror exposure to pretrial publicity. While the trial court did err in refusing to prohibit the state from cross-examining defendant on the circumstances of the offense during sentencing in violation of the self-incrimination privilege, the error was not prejudicial. Defendant was only questioned on cross-examination about matters that he reasonably raised during direct.


OUTCOME: The conviction and sentence were affirmed.

State v. Brimmer


No. 03S01-9108-CR-00080


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


876 S.W.2d 75; 1994 Tenn. LEXIS 15



February 7, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition to Rehear Denied May 2, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Tenn. LEXIS 136.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ANDERSON COUNTY. Hon. James B. Scott, Jr., Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the trial court (Tennessee) which, after a jury trial, convicted defendant of first degree premeditated homicide and sentenced defendant to death under the statutory aggravating circumstance of murder while committing a robbery. Defendant contended that the trial court erred in admitting defendant's admissions and that the instructions on mitigating circumstances were inadequate.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of first degree premeditated homicide and sentenced to death. Defendant contended that his statements introduced into evidence were unlawfully obtained and admitted in violation of his constitutional rights. Defendant also argued that there was insufficient evidence that the killing was intentional. Finally, defendant asserted that the jury was inadequately instructed on mitigating circumstances and that there was insufficient evidence to support the aggravating circumstance of murder in the perpetration of a robbery. The court affirmed defendant's conviction for first degree premeditated homicide, finding that applying the "totality of the circumstances" rule, defendant's statements were voluntary and that there was no violation of either federal or state constitutional rights in the admission of the statements. The court also determined that there was sufficient evidence of premeditation. The court further affirmed the imposition of the death penalty, concluding that the jury was adequately instructed on mitigating circumstances and that the evidence was sufficient to support the aggravating circumstance of murder while committing a robbery.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for first degree premeditated homicide and the trial court's imposition of the death penalty. The court concluded that defendant's written and oral admissions were properly admitted into evidence as voluntary and that the trial court adequately instructed the jury on the meaning and function of mitigating circumstances.

State v. Smith


No. 01S01-9103-CR-00010


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


868 S.W.2d 561; 1993 Tenn. LEXIS 410



November 18, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by State v. Smith, 1994 Tenn. LEXIS 2 (Tenn., Jan. 5, 1994)
Writ of certiorari denied Smith v. Tennessee, 513 U.S. 960, 115 S. Ct. 417, 130 L. Ed. 2d 333, 1994 U.S. LEXIS 7536 (1994)
Post-conviction relief denied at Smith v. State, 1998 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 680 (Tenn. Crim. App., June 30, 1998)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Dismissed by, Summary judgment granted by, Summary judgment denied by, Petition denied by, Request denied by Smith v. Bell, 2005 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 49361 (M.D. Tenn., Sept. 30, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] CRIMINAL COURT. DAVIDSON COUNTY. Hon. J. Randall Wyatt, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AFFIRMED. SENTENCES OF DEATH AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Criminal Court, Davidson County (Tennessee), entered judgment, upon a jury verdict, convicting defendant of three counts of first degree murder. The jury sentenced defendant to death on the murder counts as to all three victims. Appeal followed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of a triple murder. During the sentencing phase, the jury found the existence of certain aggravating circumstances and sentenced defendant to death. On appeal, the court affirmed the convictions and the sentence of death. The court held that (1) the evidence was sufficient to support the convictions, (2) defendant's statements were properly admitted into evidence as he was not in "custody" during the questioning, (3) evidence found as a result of the search of defendant's residence was admissible as the search warrant was validly obtained and executed, (4) evidence that defendant's wife was afraid of him was admissible, (5) photographic evidence was admissible as its probative value was not outweighed by its prejudicial effect, (6) the use of the alternate light source technique to identify defendant's palm print was reliable and admissible, (7) the audiotape recording of a 911 phone call was admissible as an excited utterance. The court also concluded that the jury's finding that the aggravating circumstances surrounding the murders were not outweighed by any substantial mitigating circumstances was proper and warranted the imposition of the death penalty.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the defendant's convictions for the triple murders, and affirmed the sentence of death finding that the sentence of death was not imposed in an arbitrary fashion, and that the evidence supported the jury's findings of the statutory aggravating circumstances.

 

95 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


State v. Howell


S/C No. 1


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


868 S.W.2d 238; 1993 Tenn. LEXIS 408



November 10, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] CRIMINAL COURT. SHELBY COUNTY. HON. JOSEPH B. McCARTIE, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Criminal Court of Shelby County (Tennessee) that convicted him of grand larceny and first-degree felony murder and sentenced him to death by electrocution. Defendant alleged numerous errors in both the guilt and sentencing phases of his trial. Defendant also argued that his ability to appreciate the wrongfulness of his acts and conform his conduct to the law was impaired by brain damage.


OVERVIEW: Defendant committed murder in Tennessee and in Oklahoma. The court held that: (1) restriction of voir dire was not error, as jurors exposed to pretrial publicity stated they could render an impartial verdict based solely on the evidence, and all peremptory challenges available to a death-eligible defendant were exercised; (2) admission of a codefendant's testimony about the Tennessee murder given in the Oklahoma proceedings did not violate defendant's constitutional right to confrontation, as Oklahoma counsel and trial counsel had the same motive to develop codefendant's testimony about the Tennessee murder; (3) codefendant's Oklahoma statements were admissible under the former testimony exception to the hearsay rule; (4) it was harmless error to exclude impeachment evidence of codefendant's recanted testimony, as overwhelming circumstantial evidence established defendant's guilt; (5) evidence of the Oklahoma murder was properly admitted to prove identity and flight; (6) the evidence supported the finding that no sufficiently substantial mitigating circumstance existed to outweigh the aggravating circumstances; and (7) the sentence was not excessive given the nature of the crime.


OUTCOME: Defendant's first-degree felony murder conviction was affirmed. Defendant's death sentence was also affirmed because it was neither arbitrarily imposed nor disproportionate to penalties assessed in similar cases given the nature of defendant's crime and his character.

 

96 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Davis-Kidd Booksellers v. McWherter


No. 01-S-01-9208-CH-00090


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


866 S.W.2d 520; 1993 Tenn. LEXIS 407; 22 Media L. Rep. 1225



November 8, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] CHANCERY COURT. DAVIDSON COUNTY. HON. IRVIN H. KILCREASE, JR., CHANCELLOR



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, booksellers, publishers, and associations, filed an action against defendant government officials under the Civil Rights Act of 1871, 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, and asserted that their First Amendment rights were violated by the display statute, Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-17-914(a) (1991). The Chancery Court of Davidson County (Tennessee) held that a portion of the statute was vague but upheld it in part. Both parties appealed.


OVERVIEW: The display statute criminalized the display or sale of a video or a written representation which contained material "harmful to minors" as defined under Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-17-901(6)(1991). The court noted that it had a duty to adopt a construction that would sustain the statute and avoid constitutional conflict. The court upheld the display statute under the First Amendment because it was susceptible to a narrowing construction that made it only applicable to materials that lacked serious literary, artistic, political, or scientific value for a reasonable 17-year-old minor. The nuisance statute, Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-3-10(a)(2)(1990), was upheld because it limited seizure of materials harmful to minors only if the materials were obscene and procedural safeguards accompanied the seizure. The term "excess violence" in the display statute, however, was found to be unconstitutionally vague and was eliminated under the doctrine of elision because it did not provide sufficient notice to potential violators. The statutes did not violate the Commerce Clause because the state regulation was evenhandedly applied to effectuate a legitimate local public interest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court that with a limiting construction applied, the display statute was not overbroad, that the nuisance statute allowed seizure of obscene materials harmful to minors, and that the term "excess violence" was void for vagueness and therefore, was eliminated from the statute under the doctrine of elision.

State v. Heck Van Tran


Shelby Law. No. 4


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT MEMPHIS


864 S.W.2d 465; 1993 Tenn. LEXIS 343



September 27, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition to Rehear Denied November 1, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Tenn. LEXIS 383.
Rehearing denied by State v. Heck Van Tran, 1993 Tenn. LEXIS 383 (Tenn., Nov. 1, 1993)
Writ of certiorari denied Heck Van Tran v. Tennessee, 511 U.S. 1046, 114 S. Ct. 1577, 128 L. Ed. 2d 220, 1994 U.S. LEXIS 3111 (1994)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at Heck Van Tran v. State, 1999 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 307 (Tenn. Crim. App., Apr. 1, 1999)
Related proceeding at State v. Bounnam, 1999 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 842 (Tenn. Crim. App., Aug. 16, 1999)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Motion granted by Heck Van Tran v. Bell, 145 F. Supp. 2d 939, 2001 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 8100 (W.D. Tenn., 2001)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Remanded by Van Tran v. State, 66 S.W.3d 790, 2001 Tenn. LEXIS 820 (Tenn., 2001)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] CRIMINAL COURT. SHELBY COUNTY. Hon. L. T. Lafferty, Judge. (Lower Court Nos. 88-01443, 88-01444, 88-01445, and 88-04384)



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AFFIRMED. SENTENCE AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED AND REMANDED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the Criminal Court of Shelby County (Tennessee), which convicted him of three counts of felony murder and sentenced him to death under Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-2-203 (1982) (recodified at Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-204 (1991)).


OVERVIEW: After defendant's motion to suppress certain statements was denied, a jury found defendant guilty of three counts of felony murder that occurred during the armed robbery of a family-run restaurant. Finding that the aggravating circumstances outweighed the mitigating ones under Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-2-203(g) (1982) (recodified at Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-204(g)(1991)), defendant was sentenced to death. On appeal, the court affirmed in part, holding, inter alia, that: (1) the evidence was more than sufficient to convict; (2) the trial court neither abused its discretion in appointing a relative to act as an interpreter for an eyewitness nor in admitting a video tape and color photographs of the crime scene; (3) defendant failed to establish a prima facie violation of U.S. Const. amend. VI on the ground that the jury fails to reflect a fair cross-section of the community; and (4) the Tennessee Death Penalty Statute was constitutional. While the court affirmed all three of the convictions of felony murder, it reversed his sentences as to two of them and remanded for resentencing. It affirmed the death penalty sentence imposed on the third felony murder conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed two of the convictions of felony murder but reversed the sentences and remanded for resentencing. The court then affirmed both defendant's conviction of felony murder and his sentence of death in the third count.

 

98 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Phillips v. State Bd. of Regents of State Univ. & Community College Sys.


No. 02-S-9206-CH-00039


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


863 S.W.2d 45; 1993 Tenn. LEXIS 337



September 20, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] CHANCERY COURT. SHELBY COUNTY. HON. D. J. ALISSANDRATOS, CHANCELLOR



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In her action against appellees, board of regents, college, chancellor, and president, appellant professor sought review of a judgment of the Chancery Court, Shelby County (Tennessee), which upheld her termination from the college on the ground of capricious disregard of accepted standards of professional conduct as set forth in Tenn. Code Ann. § 49-8-302(5)(1990). The professor claimed in part that her constitutional rights were violated.


OVERVIEW: The professor was terminated for capricious disregard of accepted standards of professional conduct pursuant to § 49-8-302(5). The trial court upheld the termination. On appeal, she claimed that appellees violated her constitutional rights. The court affirmed the judgment below, concluding that the charges were established by the requisite clear and convincing evidence under § 49-8-303(a)(4) (1990). The standard of capricious disregard of accepted standards of professional conduct was not unconstitutionally vague under the federal or state constitutions. Fairness was the basis of the void for vagueness doctrine and its purpose was only to give fair warning of prohibited conduct. The professor was warned about her conduct. By using her common sense and general knowledge of employer-employee relationships, the professor had fair notice that her conduct put her at risk for termination under the standard used. Her due process rights were not violated because she had notice of the allegations and a de novo hearing in the trial court. Her First Amendment rights were not violated because her complaints about her supervisor did not involve matters of public concern mandating open debate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court upholding the professor's dismissal.

 

99 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Wallen v. State


No. 03-S-01-9103-CR-00021


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


863 S.W.2d 34; 1993 Tenn. LEXIS 336



September 13, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Criminal Court. Sullivan County. Hon. George H. Garrett, Judge



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF TRIAL COURT AND COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the decision of the Court of Criminal Appeals (Tennessee), which affirmed the trial court's denial of a petition for post-conviction relief. Defendant had pleaded guilty to armed robberies and was sentenced as a persistent offender and as an especially aggravated offender, based on prior forgery convictions and his parole status. The trial court set aside the forgery convictions but did not change the robbery sentence.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the only issue raised by defendant was the use of his parole status to enhance the sentences imposed on his pleas of guilty to three charges of armed robbery after the earlier convictions underlying the parole were set aside. On this appeal, the court held that the validity of the prior forgery convictions was totally irrelevant to the later armed robbery sentences entered on defendant's pleas of guilty. The court found that the robbery court had advised defendant of his rights and the rights he would waive on a plea of guilty, so that he was not deceived nor misled, and that defendant admitted in the post-conviction hearing that the pleas were freely, voluntarily, and knowingly entered. The court found that defendant, with full knowledge of his rights and sentences, voluntarily took the benefits of a plea bargain and waived any irregularity or defect in the proceedings, including the possibility that the prior convictions used to enhance his punishment might be set aside. The court held that there was no requirement for a "knowing" and "voluntary" guilty plea that all the relevant facts actually be as a defendant apprehended them.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the Court of Criminal Appeals, which affirmed the trial court's denial of a petition for post-conviction relief from a sentence imposed on pleas of guilty to armed robberies.

State v. Maupin


S/C No. 03S01-9202-CR-00021


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


859 S.W.2d 313; 1993 Tenn. LEXIS 288



August 2, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] CRIMINAL COURT. WASHINGTON COUNTY. Hon. Lynn W. Brown, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS AFFIRMED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Criminal Court of Washington County (Tennessee), which reversed defendant's conviction based on insufficiency of evidence and remanded the case for trial on lesser included offenses.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted by a jury of aiding and abetting the first degree child abuse murder. The court of criminal appeals reversed the conviction based on insufficiency of evidence and remanded the case for trial on lesser included offenses. After the decision was released, a majority of the court declared unconstitutional the statute defendant was convicted of violating, Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-2-202(a)(2) (Supp. 1988). Defendant applied to the court to decide whether the double jeopardy clauses of the State or Federal Constitutions forbade retrial of lesser included offenses under the circumstances presented. Upon review, the court reversed the conviction. The court held that the prohibitions against double jeopardy did not preclude the State from trying defendant on the lesser included offenses. Once the conviction on the greater offense for insufficient evidence was reversed, the court stated that defendant could have been retried if the evidence was not insufficient to support a conviction on the lesser included offenses. Therefore, the court found that, based on the evidence at the first trial, a jury could have found defendant guilty of the lesser included offense.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction and remanded the case.

Wills v. State


No. 01-S-01-9201-CC-00010


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


859 S.W.2d 308; 1993 Tenn. LEXIS 292



August 2, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Montgomery County



DISPOSITION: COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS and TRIAL COURT REVERSED; CASE REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals (Tennessee), which affirmed a judgment of the trial court's denial of defendant's motion to set aside guilty pleas he entered into on the ground that he had not been advised of his constitutional rights prior to pleading guilty.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered into two guilty pleas. He then filed a motion to set aside the guilty pleas on the grounds that he was not properly advised of his constitutional rights prior to pleading guilty, and that he was not informed that the resulting convictions could have been used to enhance the punishment for subsequent convictions. The trial court denied his motion, and the appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment on a laches theory. Defendant challenged the judgments. On appeal, the court held that although there was no merit to defendant's claim of punishment enhancement, the record did not support a finding that defendant had been properly advised of his constitutional rights prior to pleading guilty. The court ruled that more than what transpired in the two hearings was necessary in order to comply with constitutional mandates. The court observed that no evidence suggested that the State discharged the burden placed on it, and explicitly rejected any notion that the doctrine of laches could have been invoked to deprive defendant of relief that was constitutionally mandated.


OUTCOME: The court reversed that judgment of the appellate court and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings, including, but not limited to, an order setting aside the guilty pleas challenged by defendant.

 

102 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


State v. Pearson


No. 03-S-01-9207-CR-00062


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


858 S.W.2d 879; 1993 Tenn. LEXIS 240



June 14, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Criminal Court. Knox County. HON. RANDALL E. NICHOLS, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Review was granted of a decision of the Court of Criminal Appeals (Tennessee), which affirmed the trial court's sentencing method when defendant pled guilty to crimes committed before the 1989 Criminal Sentencing Reform Act (1989 Act), but was sentenced after the 1989 Act went into effect. Defendant also challenged the appellate court's imposition of an enhancement. The state challenged the dismissal of a misdemeanor conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered a plea of guilty to 13 counts of first degree burglary, aggravated burglary, aggravated rape, assault, and theft. Two of the counts occurred before the 1989 Act went into effect. At sentencing, the trial court applied an enhancement factor that went into effect with the 1989 Act. The appellate court affirmed the sentence imposed by the trial court and added an additional enhancement factor for a history of criminal behavior. The court remanded the action for resentencing on the first degree burglary that occurred before the 1989 Act went into effect. The court held that when defendant was sentenced after the effective date of the 1989 Act for an offense that occurred before that time, the trial court should have calculated the applicable sentence under both sentencing statutes and imposed the lesser sentence of the two. On other issues, the court held that defendant did not make a knowing and voluntary waiver of his statute of limitations defense for a misdemeanor and should not have been prosecuted for the same. The court of appeals did not violate defendant's due process rights when it enhanced a sentence for prior criminal behavior.


OUTCOME: The case was remanded for re-sentencing on the first degree burglary charge based on the law when the crime occurred before the new sentencing statute went into effect. All other sentencing procedures imposed by the trial court and the appellate court were affirmed. Defendant was taxed with the costs of the appeal.

Hawk v. Hawk


No. 03S01-9201-CV-00013


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


855 S.W.2d 573; 1993 Tenn. LEXIS 202



June 1, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Hamilton County. The Hon. William L. Brown, Judge



DISPOSITION: TRIAL COURT AND COURT OF APPEALS REVERSED; REMANDED IN PART


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner grandparents brought an action under the Grandparents' Visitation Act (Act), Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-6-301, against respondents, a father and a mother, who had refused the grandparents the right to visit with their children. The Tennessee Court of Appeals affirmed the trial court's judgment that awarded grandparental visitation and held the father in contempt. The mother and father appealed.


OVERVIEW: The father and mother were married and refused to allow the grandparents to visit with their children. After the trial court awarded to the grandparents visitation under the Act, the father removed the children from the trial court's jurisdiction and was held in contempt for repeat offenses. The father and mother argued that the visitation order deprived them of their federal and state constitutional rights. The court, considering only Tenn. Const. art. I, § 8, held that the father and mother's constitutional rights to privacy were violated. Parents had a fundamental right to raise their children as they saw fit, and there was no finding that the mother or father was in any way threatening the children's welfare. The trial court inappropriately substituted its opinion as to the best interests of the children under the Act. The trial court erred in finding that the father committed repeat offenses of Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-9-102(3), which prohibited the willful disobedience of any party to a lawful order, as there was no evidence that the father was able to procure the children's return to the jurisdiction. Thus, he could only be sentenced for a single act of contempt.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that awarded the grandparents visitation rights and reversed the judgment holding the father in contempt for repeated offenses. The court remanded for resentencing for a single offense of contempt.

Allen v. State


S.C. No. 01S01-9201-CR-00006


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


854 S.W.2d 873; 1993 Tenn. LEXIS 204



June 1, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Criminal Court. Davidson County. Hon. Ann Lacy Johns, Judge



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF TRIAL COURT REVERSED; CASE REMANDED FOR APPOINTMENT OF COUNSEL AND FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate appealed the affirmation by the Court of Criminal Appeals of Tennessee of the dismissal, without the appointment of counsel or response by the State, of his pro se petition for post-conviction relief. He was convicted of first degree murder, which was affirmed on appeal. A prior petition for post-conviction relief was dismissed after an evidentiary hearing in which the inmate was represented by counsel.


OVERVIEW: After the dismissal, the inmate filed motions seeking the appointment of counsel, reconsideration of the dismissal, and permission to amend the petition, all of which were denied. Counsel was appointed in the appellate court, which found that the only issue not predetermined or waived by the prior petition was the trial court's jury charge in violation of Sandstrom, which was decided after the prior petition, that malice could be presumed from the use of a deadly weapon. However, the appellate court concluded that any error was harmless because the evidence overwhelmingly demonstrated malice. The court reversed, finding that under the Post-Conviction Procedures Act, Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-30-101 et seq., the trial court erred in failing to require the State to respond and to file the record of the two prior hearings, in failing to appoint counsel, and in failing to allow the inmate to amend his petition. Only after the petition had been amended by appointed counsel and after the State had complied with its statutory duty to adequately respond to the petition before the trial judge, would the case have been developed to the point where consideration of the merits was appropriate.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded for appointment of counsel and further proceedings.

State v. Branam


No. 03S01-9103-CR-00020


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


855 S.W.2d 563; 1993 Tenn. LEXIS 197



May 24, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at State v. Walker, 910 S.W.2d 381, 1995 Tenn. LEXIS 547 (Tenn., 1995)

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] KNOX COUNTY. Judge Randall E. Nichols



DISPOSITION: REVERSED IN PART AND REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the trial court (Tennessee), which convicted defendant of conspiracy to commit armed robbery, armed robbery, and first degree murder, and sentenced defendant to death on the murder conviction. In assessing the death penalty, the jury specifically found two aggravating circumstances in that the murder was committed to avoid arrest or prosecution and occurred during the commission of a robbery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of three crimes for his presence and role in a robbery and murder committed by another robber who was the triggerman and principal. Defendant was sentenced to death on the murder conviction. A year later, defendant discovered the existence of a witness statement that directly implicated another person in the crimes. On appeal, the court reversed in part and remanded. Capital punishment was precluded because there was insufficient evidence to show that the triggerman murdered the victim because she might have recognized defendant as a former employee, and because the remaining aggravating circumstance of participation in a robbery in which another robber was the triggerman could not be considered on remand. The court remanded the case for a hearing to determine if the alleged Brady violation suggested by post-judgment facts violated defendant's due process rights. The court affirmed the sufficiency of the evidence to establish defendant's guilt on the three indictments, upheld the trial court's rulings on counsel's motion to withdraw and the admission of defendant's jailhouse confession, and concluded that the remaining alleged errors were moot or waived.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's imposition of the death penalty against defendant and remanded the case to the trial court for resentencing and a hearing to determine the effect of post-judgment facts on the constitutional validity of defendant's convictions.

State v. Marshall


S/C No. 8


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON

DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE TRIAL COURT AND COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS AFFIRMED.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed the decision of the Court of Criminal Appeals (Tennessee), which affirmed the decision of the trial court, which found defendants guilty of violating Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-6-1104(a), possession with intent to distribute obscene material.

Defendants sought review alleging that §§ 39-6-1104(a), 39-6-1101(5) violated Tenn. Const. art. 1, § 19. The court held that that §§ 39-6-1104(a), 39-6-1101(5) did not violate the provisions of Tenn. Const. art. 1, § 19. The court affirmed the decision of the appellate court which affirmed defendants' convictions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of appellate court which affirmed the judgment of the trial court which found defendants guilty of possession of obscene material with intent to distribute.

Sparks v. State


No. 03S01-9212-CR-00105


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


1993 Tenn. LEXIS 187



May 10, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] As Corrected December 1, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Hamilton County. Hon. Douglas A. Meyer, Judge



DISPOSITION: REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a post-conviction action, petitioner inmate challenged the decision of the Hamilton County trial court (Tennessee), which convicted the inmate of armed robbery and felony-murder and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: The primary issue was whether the use of the felony-murder aggravating circumstance, Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-2-203(i)(7) (1982), to support the death penalty for felony-murder was harmless error. The inmate, in association with three other men, was involved in an armed robbery at a liquor store, during which the inmate shot and killed a delivery man. At the sentencing hearing, the prosecutor used two aggravating circumstances to support the death penalty. The court held that it was unconstitutional to use the felony-murder aggravating circumstance, §§ 39-2-203(i)(7) (1982), to support the death penalty upon conviction of felony-murder. Therefore the court concluded that only one aggravating circumstance remained. The court held that they were unable to speculate about what verdict the jury might have returned based on proof of a single aggravating circumstance. The court remanded for resentencing, holding that they could not say that in the absence of the felony-murder aggravating circumstance that there was proof beyond a reasonable doubt that the inmate should have been sentenced to execution.


OUTCOME: In the inmate's post-conviction action challenging his death sentence, after a conviction of armed robbery and felony-murder, the court remanded the action for resentencing.

Code Ann. § 55-10-403(1) had yet to be enacted which meant that there was nothing to reserve at trial. Absent explicit conformity with the procedures for preserving certified questions for review, the court concluded that the appeal was required to have been dismissed..


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal.

Kee v. Shelter Ins.


No. 02-S-01-9202-CV-00011


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


852 S.W.2d 226; 1993 Tenn. LEXIS 146



April 5, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] LAW COURT. SHELBY COUNTY. HON. JAMES E. SWEARENGEN, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff insured sought review of the order of the Law Court, Shelby County (Tennessee), which dismissed his complaint against defendant insurer for breach of their contract of insurance. Plaintiff alleged that his action was not time-barred under the provisions of Tenn. Code Ann. § 28-1-105(b) (Supp. 1992), which extended the time for filing the action.


OVERVIEW: The insured's house was destroyed by fire while he was covered by the insurer's homeowner's policy. His claim was denied, and he filed an action within the one-year contractual limitation. Later, he dismissed the action without prejudice and refiled after the one-year period. The trial court denied the insurer's motion to dismiss, upon its finding that § 28-1-105(b), which was enacted after the policy was issued permitted the insured to refile his action after the contractual time limitation had expired, so long as he had originally filed within the time limit. The appellate court reversed the trial court, and the court affirmed the reversal. Because the contract was already executed and the parties' contractual rights had already accrued prior to the effective date of § 28-1-105(b), the statute did not apply. The court held that the law that existed when the contract was executed controlled the rights and duties of the parties. The statute could not be applied retroactively to affect such contractual rights and duties. To do so would violate Tenn. Const. art. I, § 20, which provided that no retrospective law or law that impaired contractual rights could be made.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court.

State v. Hurley


S/C No. 34


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


876 S.W.2d 57; 1993 Tenn. LEXIS 150



April 5, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition to Rehear Granted August 30, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Tenn. LEXIS 315 
Rehearing granted by State v. Hurley, 876 S.W.2d 57, 1993 Tenn. LEXIS 315 (Tenn., 1993)
Writ of certiorari denied Hurley v. Tennessee, 513 U.S. 933, 130 L. Ed. 2d 287, 115 S. Ct. 328, 1994 U.S. LEXIS 7172 (1994)
Habeas corpus proceeding at Hurley v. Carlton, 2004 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 611 (Tenn. Crim. App., July 12, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] CRIMINAL COURT. COCKE COUNTY. Hon. J. Kenneth Porter, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AS MODIFIED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the Criminal Court of Cocke County (Tennessee) convicting him of premeditated first degree murder, felony murder, and armed robbery. The trial court sentenced defendant to death on each murder conviction and to a consecutive sentence of 12 years for the armed robbery conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant drove the victim to a secluded area where he shot and killed the victim and robbed him. Defendant was convicted and sentenced. On appeal, the court modified the order and affirmed. The court held that it was the jury's role to resolve the issue of the credibility of one of defendant's girlfriends, to whom defendant had confessed, and that the evidence against him was sufficient to support his conviction. The court also held that the weight of the evidence was sufficient to support the verdict because there was other evidence pointing to him as the person responsible for the victim's murder. The court held that defendant did not have the right to invoke the rule of spousal disqualification to prevent his wife, who was a willing witness, from testifying, that the trial judge committed no error resulting in the unjust disposition of the case, that defendant was not prejudiced by the trial court's denial of his motion for continuance, that the prospective jurors that were excused for cause were excused in compliance with the standards relating to death penalty cases, and that defendant's statements to a law enforcement officer were volunteered and thus admissible.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment convicting defendant of murder and armed robbery, as modified, and ordered the death sentence carried out unless stayed or modified.

State v. Bane


S/C No. 6


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


853 S.W.2d 483; 1993 Tenn. LEXIS 148



March 29, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion granted by Tennessee v. Bane, 510 U.S. 808, 114 S. Ct. 52, 126 L. Ed. 2d 23, 1993 U.S. LEXIS 4900 (1993)

Subsequent appeal at State v. Bane, 2000 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 56 (Tenn. Crim. App., Jan. 24, 2000)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] SHELBY COUNTY. (No. 89-01502 Below). Hon. William H. Williams Judge



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED, SENTENCE REVERSED, CAUSE REMANDED DROWOTA & O'BRIEN DISSENT FROM RESENTENCING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his conviction, by a trial court in Shelby County (Tennessee), for murder in the first degree in the perpetration of a robbery and from his sentence of death by electrocution.


OVERVIEW: Defendant asserted several trial errors and challenged the imposition of the death penalty. The court found that the evidence clearly established a planned, premeditated, and deliberate homicide committed by defendant, as found by the jury, in the perpetration of a robbery. The court determined that the trial court properly instructed the jury as to the elements of felony murder and the use and effect of circumstantial evidence. The court affirmed the judgment of conviction. With regard to imposition of the death penalty, the court determined that Tenn. Const. art. I, §§ 9 and 16 from imposing the death penalty in the manner provided by Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-202 et seq. The court found, however, that a recent decision of the court related to the felony murder statute required that the case be remanded to the trial court for the jury's reconsideration of the evidence and aggravating circumstances to determine if a sentence of death was appropriate.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment of conviction was affirmed but the case was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings and resentencing.

State v. Smith

857 S.W.2d 1; 1993 Tenn. LEXIS 149

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED & REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the Criminal Court, Hamblen County (Tennessee), in which he was convicted of first degree murder and sentenced to death by electrocution. This was defendant's second trial on this charge and he raised numerous errors pertaining to both his conviction and the sentence imposed on him.


OVERVIEW: In this, his second trial on the charge of first-degree murder, defendant was sentenced to death by electrocution. Tennessee Small Sch. Sys. v. McWherter


S.C. No. 01-S01-9209-CH-00101


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


851 S.W.2d 139; 1993 Tenn. LEXIS 114



March 22, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Costs and fees proceeding at Tennessee Small Sch. Sys. v. McWherter, 1993 Tenn. App. LEXIS 512 (Tenn. Ct. App., Aug. 4, 1993)
Appeal after remand at, Remanded by Tennessee Small Sch. Sys. v. McWherter, 894 S.W.2d 734, 1995 Tenn. LEXIS 45 (Tenn., 1995)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Chancery Court. Davidson County. Hon. C. Allen High, Chancellor
Tennessee Small School Systems v. McWherter, 1992 Tenn. App. LEXIS 486 (Tenn. Ct. App., June 5, 1992)



DISPOSITION: TRIAL COURT AFFIRMED; COURT OF APPEALS REVERSED; CASE REMANDED TO TRIAL COURT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant school systems sought review of a decision of the Court of Appeals (Tennessee), which reversed a trial court's decision that the statutory scheme of appellee state officials for funding the kindergarten-through-12th grade public school system violated the education clause and equal protection provisions of the Tennessee Constitution.


OVERVIEW: The school systems filed an action for a declaratory judgment that the statutory scheme of the state officials for funding the kindergarten-through-12th grade public school system violated the education and equal protection clauses of the state Constitution. The trial court ruled for the school systems, a decision that was reversed on appeal. The school systems sought review, and the court held that the statutory scheme violated the right to an adequate free education under Tenn. Const. art. XI, § 12, as well as the equal protection provisions of Tenn. Const. art. XI, § 8 and Tenn. Const. art. I, § 8. The plain language of Tenn. Const. art. XI, § 12 mandated a fundamental right to an adequate free education. The different classifications between large and small school systems did not have a reasonable relationship to a legitimate state interest. Local control of education was not a justification for disparity in opportunity. The proof failed to show a legitimate state interest justifying the grant to some citizens of the educational opportunities that were denied to other citizens similarly situated, and, thus, failed to satisfy the rational basis test.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision to dismiss the school systems' complaint for a declaratory judgment that the statutory scheme for funding public education in Tennessee violated the education and equal protection clause of the Tennessee Constitution.

Archer v. State


03S01-9206-CR-000057


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


851 S.W.2d 157; 1993 Tenn. LEXIS 143



March 22, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Criminal Court. Hamilton County. Hon. Joseph F. DiRisio, Judge.



DISPOSITION: TRIAL COURT AND COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Criminal Court, Hamilton County (Tennessee), which concluded that the validity of guilty pleas could not be challenged in a habeas corpus proceeding and that defendant's petition had been properly converted into one for post-conviction relief and dismissed as untimely.


OVERVIEW: Defendant filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus alleging that certain guilty pleas he entered were not knowing and voluntary. The trial court converted the petition into a petition for post-conviction relief and, because it was not filed within the required period, consideration of it was time-barred. On review, the court affirmed. The court found that the allegations in the petition in no way suggested that the challenged convictions were void due to the trial court's lack of jurisdiction over either the subject matter of the proceeding or over the person of defendant. The court also found that the petition did not indicate that the record of the proceedings showed that the trial court's actions were unauthorized or that defendant's sentence had expired and that defendant was being restrained illegally. The court determined that, because the petition did not properly allege grounds on which habeas corpus relief could be granted, defendant was not entitled to challenge the validity of his guilty pleas at any time during which he was incarcerated pursuant to those pleas.


OUTCOME: The conclusion that the validity of guilty pleas could not be challenged in a habeas corpus proceeding was affirmed.

State v. Sliger


No. 01-S-01-9203-CR-00032


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


846 S.W.2d 262; 1993 Tenn. LEXIS 19



January 19, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] CRIMINAL COURT. WILSON COUNTY. HON. J. O. BOND, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS REVERSED; TRIAL COURT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals (Tennessee) that reversed the quashing of an indictment against him under the flagrant nonsupport felony statute, Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-15-101.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was married and had two children. The family lived in another state until a divorce was granted to the wife in Tennessee. Defendant failed to pay child support and was indicted under the flagrant nonsupport felony statute. The trial court quashed the indictment, but the appellate court reversed. Defendant sought review, and the court reversed the appellate court. The court held that making nonsupport a felony against defendant would have amounted to increasing his punishment merely because he lived in another state. Such a construction would have violated defendant's Equal Protection right to travel under the Fourteenth Amendment. The court declined to so construe the statute because statutory constructions that resulted in a statute being unconstitutional were disfavored. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that quashed the indictment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the appellate court and affirmed the trial court's judgment that quashed the indictment against defendant.

Burford v. State


No. 01-S-01-9202-CR-00025


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


845 S.W.2d 204; 1992 Tenn. LEXIS 699



December 21, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Criminal Court. Trousdale County. HON. J. O. BOND, JUDGE.
Burford v. State, 1991 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 852 (Tenn. Crim. App., Oct. 17, 1991)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the Court of Criminal Appeals (Tennessee), which affirmed the trial court's dismissal of appellant's claim for post-conviction relief on the grounds that it was barred by the three-year statute of limitations contained in Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-30-102.


OVERVIEW: After appellant was convicted of robbery with a dangerous weapon, appellee state used five prior robbery convictions to have him sentenced as a persistent offender. The state supreme court denied appellant's application for permission to appeal. Four of the five prior convictions were subsequently found to be void and vacated. Appellant's claim for post-conviction relief was dismissed by the trial court, which ruled that the claim was barred by the statute of limitations contained in Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-30-102. The lower appellate court affirmed the dismissal. On appeal, the court reversed the lower appellate court's judgment and remanded the case to the trial court. The court held that although § 40-30-102 complied with due process and was constitutional on its face, the application of § 40-30-102 to bar consideration of appellant's claim deprived appellant of liberty without due process of law and was unconstitutional. The court found that the state interest represented by § 40-30-102 was not served by the application of the statute to appellant's claim. The court held that the claim for post-conviction relief was not barred by § 40-30-102.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the lower appellate court, which had affirmed the trial court's dismissal of appellant's claim for post-conviction relief. The court remanded the case to the trial court for an evidentiary hearing. The costs of the appeal were taxed to the state.

Bloomingdale's by Mail v. Huddleston


S/C No. 01S01-9106-CH-00047


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


848 S.W.2d 52; 1992 Tenn. LEXIS 703



December 21, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition to Rehear Denied February 22, 1993, Reported at 1993 Tenn. LEXIS 52.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Chancery Court. Davidson County. Hon. C. Allen High, Chancellor (Part II).



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of the decision of the Chancery Court of Davidson County (Tennessee), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellees, the Commissioner of Revenue of the State of Tennessee and the Attorney General of the State of Tennessee. The commissioner had made a tax assessment against the taxpayer. At issue was whether Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-1-1803(d), regarding attorneys' fees, was controlling.


OVERVIEW: The commissioner required the taxpayer to register as a dealer in the state and to collect use tax on its mail order sales. Because the parties later agreed as to the applicable law, the court vacated the summary judgment that had been granted by the trial court in favor of the commissioner and attorney general. The assessment was set aside. However, the court remanded the action to the trial court to determine the amount of attorneys' fees. The upper limit on the fees, set forth in § 67-1-1803(d), was not controlling because the taxpayer was properly before the trial court pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-1-1801 et seq. The trial court had subject matter jurisdiction and could not, therefore, deny the taxpayer its federal rights. Those rights include the entitlement to receive attorneys' fees under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988. To the extent that Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-1-1803(d) did not conflict with 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988, the Tennessee statute was applicable. Therefore, the taxpayer was entitled to attorneys' fees up to 20 percent of the amount assessed. The court could not use the state statute to limit the fees that were otherwise available under the federal statute.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and vacated the grant of summary judgment that had been in favor of the commissioner and the attorney general. The court remanded the action to the trial court for a determination of the amount of attorneys' fees awardable to the taxpayer. The trial court was directed to issue judgment in favor of the taxpayer and to declare that the assessment was invalid.

State v. Harris


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


844 S.W.2d 601; 1992 Tenn. LEXIS 723

Defendant was sentenced to 20 years, which was the minimum for aggravated sexual battery upon a child less than 13 years of age.

Buhl v. U.S. Sprint Communications Co.


# 03S01-9107-CH-00065


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


840 S.W.2d 904; 1992 Tenn. LEXIS 574



October 26, 1992, Decided  
October 26, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Smith v. Sprint Communs. Co., L.P., 2004 U.S. App. LEXIS 21642 (7th Cir. Ill., Oct. 19, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Chancery Court. Anderson County. Hon. Wm. E. Lantrip, Chancellor



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF COURT OF APPEALS AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant communications company appealed the decision from the Chancery Court, Anderson County (Tennessee) that, in eminent domain proceedings, found for plaintiff owners.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff owned three tracts of land upon which were located railroad tracks owned by a railroad company, successor in title to the right of way. Defendant communications company constructed a fiber optics telephone cable across plaintiffs' tracts of land, within the boundaries of the right of way. The cable was constructed pursuant to a non-exclusive "license agreement" between communications company and railroad company. Owners brought an action against communications company, claiming the construction of the cable constituted an unlawful taking for which they were entitled to compensation and damages. On appeal to the supreme court, the court affirmed but remanded to include the ancillary ownership claim involving the easement, which the court determined was given only for the use of a railroad right of way. The installation of the telephone cable without the consent of the owners of the fee constituted the taking of an interest in the property for which they were entitled to compensation.


OUTCOME: The appellate court judgment was affirmed but the case was remanded to provide relief to the owner who had granted an easement.

 

121 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Newport Housing Authority v. Ballard


S/C No. 30S01-9190-CV-00097


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


839 S.W.2d 86; 1992 Tenn. LEXIS 567



September 28, 1992, Decided  
September 28, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Law Court. Cocke County. Hon. Rex Henry Ogle, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landlord brought an unlawful detainer action against defendant tenant under Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-18-101 et seq. The general sessions court (Tennessee) denied the tenant's jury demand and awarded judgment to the landlord. On appeal, the circuit court awarded judgment to the landlord following a de novo jury trial. The tenant appealed, alleging the denial of a general sessions jury trial violated Tenn. Const. art. I, § 6.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed the judgment for the landlord. Tenn. Const. art. I, § 6 had never mandated the right to a jury trial in every civil cause. The right of trial by jury secured by this constitutional provision was the right of trial by jury as it existed at common law and was in force and use under the laws and Constitution of North Carolina at the time of the formation and adoption of Tennessee's Constitution. The unlawful detainer action was non-existent at the time of, or prior to, the adoption of the original Tennessee Constitution. Further, the legislature's intent, in creating the action of unlawful detainer, was to streamline the cumbersome and more formal common law action, such as ejectment, used to determine rightful possession of real property. Thus, as the law presently stood, there was no constitutional right, no common law right, or statutory right to a jury trial for either party in an unlawful detainer action heard in general sessions court. The appeal bond requirements of Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 29-18-128 through 29-18-130 did not impose any unreasonable or irrational burdens upon parties seeking to appeal an adverse decision from the general sessions court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment for the landlord.

State by South Carthage v. Barrett


No. 01-S-01-9003-CV-00025


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


840 S.W.2d 895; 1992 Tenn. LEXIS 570



September 28, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] CIRCUIT COURT. SMITH COUNTY. HON. BOBBY CAPERS, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff State appealed a judgment of the Smith Count Circuit Court (Tennessee), which held that Tenn. Code Ann. § 6-2-403 violated the separation of powers provision of the Tennessee Constitution and that the municipal court was without jurisdiction to convict defendant.


OVERVIEW: The State's appeal was taken on behalf of a town whose municipal court had convicted defendant of driving while intoxicated and driving without a license. Defendant appealed his conviction to the circuit court, which concluded that the municipal court was without jurisdiction to try his case. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court ruled that the town's ordinance, which granted the town's municipal court concurrent jurisdiction, rendered the municipal court an inferior state court. Thus, the judges of the municipal court had to be elected in compliance with Tenn. Const. art. VI, § 4. The town's municipal judge was not elected, so the municipal court was without jurisdiction to try defendant's criminal case. Because Tenn. Code Ann. § 6-2-403 gave the municipal court judge inferior court jurisdiction without requiring the judge to be elected, the statute violated Tenn. art. II, §§ 1 and 2. The presumption of constitutionality was rebutted. The statute was unconstitutional under separation of powers principles.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment against the State.

 

123 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


State v. Deuter


No. 3


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


839 S.W.2d 391; 1992 Tenn. LEXIS 550



September 14, 1992, Decided  
September 14, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected October 9, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Criminal Court. Weakley County. Hon. Phil B. Harris, Judge
State v. Deuter, 1989 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 772 (Tenn. Crim. App., Nov. 8, 1989)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF TRIAL COURT REVERSED; JUDGMENT OF COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS REVERSED; CASE REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals (Tennessee) affirming his conviction on five counts of aggravated sexual battery involving children.


OVERVIEW: The trial court admitted videotaped statements of the victims taken by police officers during their investigation. The record did not show when the statements were taken or whether the witnesses were under oath, and the only persons present were the victims and the police officers. The appellate court held that the admission of the tape was harmless error. The court held that the admission of the videotape violated defendant's constitutional right of confrontation and there was no showing of necessity that would warrant an exception. There was no judicial determination that appearing before defendant would traumatize the witnesses. Further, the victims' trial testimonies included no information as to when, where, or under what circumstances the acts occurred; what their relationship with defendant was; or how the acts were discovered. The videotaped testimony, elicited by leading questions, was more definite and included acts more numerous and serious than those mentioned in court. The admission of the tape was not harmless error beyond a reasonable doubt because there was no medical evidence of abuse and the victims' testimonies were not consistent with defendant's confession.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction and remanded for a new trial.

SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE
