Tenn. v. Johnson


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Tennessee


762 S.W.2d 110; 1988 Tenn. LEXIS 177



October 3, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied October 24, 1988; Rehearing Denied December 5, 1988.
Rehearing denied by State v. Johnson, 762 S.W.2d 110, 1988 Tenn. LEXIS 262 (Tenn., 1988)
Writ of certiorari denied Johnson v. Tennessee, 489 U.S. 1091, 109 S. Ct. 1559, 103 L. Ed. 2d 862, 1989 U.S. LEXIS 1559 (1989)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Remanded by Johnson v. State, 1999 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 828 (Tenn. Crim. App., Aug. 12, 1999)
Appeal after remand at, Remanded by Johnson v. State, 2009 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 830 (Tenn. Crim. App., Sept. 30, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] SHELBY CRIMINAL S/C No. 1, Hon. James C. Beasley, Judge by Designation



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Shelby Criminal Court (Tennessee), which convicted him of first degree murder and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first degree murder for shooting and killing the owner of a grocery store during an attempted robbery. Defendant contended that the evidence was insufficient to sustain his conviction and he was entitled to an acquittal at the close of the state's proof. The court rejected this contention, holding that a review of the record left no doubt that the evidence amply supported the verdict of the jury. The court held that an eyewitness identified defendant as the shooter, defendant's vehicle was linked to the attempted robbery, and a witness testified that defendant had admitted to the murder. Defendant contended that the trial court erred in allowing the admission of certain photographs of the victim on the basis that they only served to arouse and inflame the passions and emotions of the jury. The court held that to warrant admissibility a photograph must have been relevant to some issue at trial. The court affirmed the conviction, holding that the pictures admitted for the jury to see were relevant to show the location and nature of the victim's gunshot wounds and they were not particularly gruesome.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of first degree murder and the sentence of death.

 

173 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


WRG Enterprises, Inc. v. Crowell


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Tennessee at Nashville


758 S.W.2d 214; 1988 Tenn. LEXIS 176



September 26, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DAVIDSON EQUITY, Hon. Irvin H. Kilcrease, Jr., Chancellor, S/C No. 87-31-I.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED & REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff charitable solicitor appealed the decision of the Chancery Court for Davidson County (Tennessee), which upheld the constitutionality of two provisions of Tennessee's Solicitation of Charitable Funds Act, Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 48-3-513, 48-3-513(k), in the solicitor's petition for review that challenged the decision of defendants, secretary of state and attorney general, to deny a certificate to solicit charitable funds.


OVERVIEW: The solicitor had previously entered into solicitation contracts with two groups, charging a commission of 35 percent when it could only charge a total fee of 15 percent. The contract also provided that the solicitor would do telemarketing when it was prohibited to do so. The court reversed the chancery court's decision, finding that insofar as § 48-3-513(i) prohibited telephone solicitations by professional solicitors, it was unconstitutional and in violation of U.S. Const. amend. I and XIV, and Tenn. Const. art. I, §§ 8, 19. The court found that a statute was properly subject to facial attack where it imposed a direct restriction on protected First Amendment activity and where the defect in the statute was that the means chosen to accomplish the state's objectives were too imprecise, creating an unnecessary risk of chilling free speech. Likewise, the court found that Tenn. Code Ann. § 48-3-513(k) violated U.S. Const. amend. I and XIV, and Tenn. Const. art. I, §§ 8, 19. A percentage-based regulation upon the fees to be collected by professional solicitors was an unconstitutional invasion upon the First Amendment rights of charities and fundraisers alike.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the chancery court that was in favor of defendants and that upheld the constitutionality of the two challenged provisions of Tennessee's Solicitation of Charitable Funds Act.

 

174 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. O'Brien v. Massengill


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Tennessee at Jackson


756 S.W.2d 246; 1988 Tenn. LEXIS 165



August 22, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] BENTON EQUITY, S/C No. 1 (No. 6559 Below), Walton West, Chancellor



DISPOSITION:  REVERSED & REMANDED FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff citizen sought review of the decision of the Chancery Court of Benton County (Tennessee) that entered judgment in favor of defendants, Benton County (Tennessee) Election Commission and others, in the citizen's complaint for mandamus, charging that the Commission failed to abide by the requirements of Tenn. Code Ann. § 2-9-109 because it did not equip the County with voting machines for use in all elections.


OVERVIEW: The Commission argued that 1974 Tenn. Pub. Acts 641 amended Tenn. Code Ann. § 2-9-109 to exempt Benton County from the requirement that it provide voting machines and, as such, that the Commission was not required to equip the County with voting machines. The court reversed the judgment and remanded the cause, opining that 1974 Tenn. Pub. Acts 641 violated Tenn. Const. art. XI, § 8, which prohibited the legislature from passing any law granting to any individual an exemption from a law unless there was a reasonable basis for such discrimination. The Commission argued that the economic impact on the County, which would have resulted if it had purchased the voting machines, was a reasonable basis for excluding the County from the requirements of Tenn. Code Ann. § 2-9-109. The court disagreed, noting that testimony from several elected officials indicated that the cost to the County would not have been prohibitive. Additionally, the court noted that Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 2-9-112 through 2-9-114 include a provision permitting the State to finance the acquisition of the voting machines for a county.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the cause for further proceedings.

State v. Wright


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Tennessee at Nashville


756 S.W.2d 669; 1988 Tenn. LEXIS 154



August 8, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition to Rehear Denied August 29, 1988, Reported at: 756 S.W.2d 669 at 678.
Rehearing denied by State v. Wright, 756 S.W.2d 669, 1988 Tenn. LEXIS 167 (Tenn., 1988)
Writ of certiorari denied Wright v. Tennessee, 488 U.S. 1034, 109 S. Ct. 848, 102 L. Ed. 2d 979, 1989 U.S. LEXIS 362, 57 U.S.L.W. 3471 (1989)
Habeas corpus proceeding at Wright v. Bell, 2010 U.S. App. LEXIS 18139 (6th Cir.) (6th Cir. Tenn., 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Davidson Criminal, Hon. Walter C. Kurtz, Judge, S. Ct. No. 85-56-I



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the Davidson County Criminal Court (Tennessee) for premeditated murder in the first degree for killing two persons. For one murder defendant was sentenced to life imprisonment and for the second murder he was sentenced to death by electrocution.


OVERVIEW: The two victims and defendant were trafficking in illegal narcotics. The jury had found an aggravating circumstance under Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-203(i)(7) to the effect that the murder was committed while the accused was engaged in committing, attempting to commit, or fleeing after committing another first degree murder. The court affirmed the conviction and sentence, finding that although the trial court erred in admitting the medical examiner's opinion as to the sequence of events at the sentencing hearing, the error was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt because the jury had rejected the aggravating circumstance under Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-2-203(i)(6), which provided that the murder was committed for the purpose of avoiding a lawful arrest or prosecution of the accused. The court found that there was no merit to defendant's argument that the mitigating circumstances outweighed the aggravating circumstance because the jury found that defendant in cold blood shot the two victims. The court found that the death penalty was not disproportionate and did not result of any arbitrary or improper action by the jury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for premeditated murder in the first degree for killing two persons and his life imprisonment for one murder and his death sentence for the other murder.

 

176 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Thomasson v. Thomasson


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Tennessee


755 S.W.2d 779; 1988 Tenn. LEXIS 153



August 2, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Williamson Equity, Honorable Henry Denmark Bell, Judge, S. Ct. No. 87-59-I


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant husband challenged the judgment of the Court of Appeals (Tennessee), which affirmed the trial court's order granting appellee wife a divorce on the grounds of cruel and inhuman treatment and irreconcilable differences. The trial court had also dismissed the husband's divorce complaint.


OVERVIEW: The husband filed a complaint for divorce on grounds of adultery, cruel and inhuman treatment, and irreconcilable differences. The wife filed a divorce complaint on grounds of cruel and inhuman treatment and irreconcilable differences. Neither party filed an answer, and the trial court granted the wife a divorce. The trial court held that the wife's adultery was of no legal significance, and the appellate court affirmed that decision. On appeal, the court dismissed the complaints of both the husband and the wife and held that neither party was entitled to a divorce. The court found that the husband proved a cause of action for divorce to which the wife was without a valid defense and that the wife had proven a cause of action for divorce to which the husband was without a valid defense. Specifically, the wife sustained an action for cruel and inhuman treatment, and the husband proved an action for adultery. The statutory defense of justifiable cause, Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-4-120, required proof that the wife's adultery preceded and provided justifiable cause for the husband's cruel and inhuman treatment. The husband failed to meet that burden.


OUTCOME: The court ordered that the divorce complaints of both the husband and wife be dismissed.

Shelby County Election Com. v. Turner


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Tennessee


755 S.W.2d 774; 1988 Tenn. LEXIS 146



July 28, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] SHELBY EQUITY, HON. GEORGE T. LEWIS, CHANCELLOR, NUMBER



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county commission challenged the decision of the Shelby County Equity Court (Tennessee), which found in favor of appellee election commission in its declaratory judgment action and found that Tenn. Code Ann. § 37-1-211 was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff election committee (committee) filed a declaratory judgment action against defendant county commission to determine whether Tenn. Code Ann. § 37-1-211 was constitutional. The statute provided that the juvenile court judge would appoint the clerk of special juvenile courts. There was a person in the position of juvenile court clerk at the time who had been appointed by a judge. The trial court found that the statute was unconstitutional. On review, the court found that the juvenile court was an inferior court within the meaning of the constitution. Furthermore, Tenn. Const. art. VI, § 13 provided that clerks of the inferior courts were to be elected by the voters for a term of four years. Therefore, the trial court's decision was affirmed and the office of the clerk of the juvenile court was ordered on the ballot in the next general election.


OUTCOME: The trial court's decision that found in favor of the election committee in its declaratory judgment action was affirmed.

 

178 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Summers v. Thompson


No. 229


Supreme Court of Tennessee,


764 S.W.2d 182; 1988 Tenn. LEXIS 108



May 23, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Rehearing Overruled July 18, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] HAMILTON CHANCERY

Hon. R. Vann Owens, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION:  REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondents, mayor and members of the city board of commissioners, appealed from the Chancery Court of Hamilton County (Tennessee), which found that the at-will employment provisions of Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 6-21-501 and 16-18-102 violated the requirement of separation of powers under Tenn. Const. art. II, § 1, and issued a common law writ of certiorari, ordering petitioner municipal judge's reinstatement.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner municipal judge was terminated at a regularly scheduled public meeting of respondent board of commissioners after having served continuously in that position for 14 years. Municipal judge petitioned for a common law writ of certiorari and the trial court granted it, holding that the statute providing for the municipal judge to serve at the will of the board was a violation of state constitutional requirement for separation of powers. On appeal, the court reversed because this municipal judge was not cloaked with the powers of a judge of an inferior court within the meaning of Tenn. Const. art. VI, § 1. The court concluded that under the terms of the statutes and the provisions of the Constitution, the action of the board must be upheld because the limited jurisdiction of such courts over city ordinances, with their restricted fines and penalties, rather than over any State laws, did not entail an exercise of constitutional judicial power. Absent a showing of actual prejudice to a litigant before the city court because of the board's attempt to exercise improper influence over the city judge, the court declined to extend the reach of Article VI.


OUTCOME: The court concluded that the parties litigated the case on an incorrect reading of the statutes and held that the action of the board in removing the municipal judge was within their power under the applicable statutory provision in this case. Therefore, the court reversed the judgment below and dismissed the case.

Bates v. Alexander


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Tennessee


749 S.W.2d 742; 1988 Tenn. LEXIS 98



May 2, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] SHELBY EQUITY, D. J. ALISSANDRATOS, CHANCELLOR, NUMBER 2, No. 92386-3 R.D.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the County Register of Shelby County, and Shelby County, sought review of the decision of the Chancery Court of Shelby County (Tennessee), which declared an amendment to Tenn. Code Ann. § 8-21-1001, set forth in 1985 Tenn. Pub. Acts ch. 479 to be constitutional in the county register's action against appellee State Governor, State Attorney General, and Sheriff of Shelby County to declare the amendment unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The county register contended that the amendment to Tenn. Code Ann. § 8-21-1001 was unconstitutional because it violated Tenn. Const. art. 1, § 8 and the equal protection act of U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The amendment had increased the fees to be collected by the county registers for their services in all except the five most populous counties of the state. The county register of deeds was a constitutional office and had been supported by the fees authorized by the legislature for the registration of deeds and other instruments dealing with interests in real property. In establishing the compensation the legislature set fees based on population. When the fees were not sufficient to meet the minimum salary, it was paid out of the county's general funds. The amendment increased the fees in all counties except the five most populous counties. The court affirmed, finding that the test to be used in determining the validity of the population-based classification was the less stringent "rational basis" test. The court found that the five most populous counties were operating with a large surplus while over 30 percent of the other counties had operated at a loss.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment entered in favor of the governor, attorney general, and county sheriff in the county register's action that challenged the constitutionality of an amendment to the statute setting fees for services rendered.

State v. Barber


No. 6085


Supreme Court of Tennessee


753 S.W.2d 659; 1988 Tenn. LEXIS 36

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction and sentence rendered in the trial court (Tennessee) by a jury trial. Defendant was sentenced to 15 years, life imprisonment, and death by electrocution, respectively.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty and sentenced after it was established at trial that defendant and his brother broke into the home of a 75 year old woman, robbed her, and murdered her by hitting her repeatedly with a blunt instrument. At the sentencing hearing on the jury found two aggravating circumstances: the murder was especially heinous and the murder was committed while defendant was committing a felony. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction and the death sentence imposed by the trial court, after a jury trial, for first degree murder in perpetration of larceny. Costs were adjudged against defendant.

Hoyle v. Wilson


No. 87-17-I


Supreme Court of Tennessee


746 S.W.2d 665; 1988 Tenn. LEXIS 30



February 22, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at: 746 S.W.2d 665 at 675.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Opinion of January 19, 1988, Reported at: 746 S.W.2d 665.

 [**1] DAVIDSON LAW.

Hon. Muriel Robinson, Judge.



DISPOSITION:  Accordingly, the Petition to Rehear is denied. Costs are taxed to the State.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner State of Tennessee filed a petition for rehearing of a case involving enforcement of child support. The petition did not seek a reconsideration of the holding in the case, but asked the court to clarify some of the implications of the holding.


OVERVIEW: The State sought reconsideration of the court's statement that the duty to support was not and could not be established through a Uniform Reciprocal Enforcement of Support Act (URESA) action and that, at some point prior to the institution of a URESA action, some state must render an order establishing a duty to support. The court denied the State's petition for rehearing, rejecting the State's contention that the court's construction of URESA conflicted with prior case law. The court reaffirmed its position that URESA cannot substitute for the due process required to establish the duty of support in the first instance if that duty is not voluntarily undertaken by a respondent. The court also reaffirmed the existing law that no showing that arrearages would be used for the benefit of the children was ordinarily required because enforcement of arrearages constituted a form of reimbursement for the obligee's assumption of the entire duty of support during the period covered by arrearages.


OUTCOME: The court denied the State's petition for rehearing of a case involving enforcement of child support.

 

185 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Nance v. Westside Hospital


No. 87-21-I


Supreme Court of Tennessee


750 S.W.2d 740; 1988 Tenn. LEXIS 52



February 16, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied April 5, 1988, Reported at 1988 Tenn. LEXIS 305, Reported at: 750 S.W.2d 740 at 744.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Davidson Equity, Honorable Robert S. Brandt, Chancellor



DISPOSITION:  COURT OF APPEALS AFFIRMED; REMANDED FOR TRIAL ON THE MERITS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient and intervening plaintiff employer sought review of a judgment of the Court of Appeals (Tennessee) that worker's compensation benefits were not included in Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-26-119 and that the employer could enforce its statutory subrogation lien against any recovery the patient received from its medical malpractice action against defendants, hospital and physician.


OVERVIEW: The hospital and physician claimed § 29-26-119 eliminated as damages sums paid or payable to the employee under worker's compensation. The trial court held that § 29-26-119 applied to worker's compensation benefits, however, because that would deny the patient recovery to the extent of worker's compensation benefits paid, the employer could not assert its subrogation lien. The court affirmed the appellate court's holding that worker's compensation benefits were not of the same kind and character as the sources mentioned in § 29-26-119 but that the employer could assert its subrogation rights. The court held that worker's compensation benefits were not included within § 29-26-119, the patient's recovery against the hospital and physician could not be reduced by the sums received, but that the employer could enforce its subrogation rights. The statute required that benefits be paid and also indemnify the victim's losses. That phrase removed from the statute any collateral source that had subrogation rights. Where benefits carried a right of subrogation and a legal obligation on the employee's part to repay the collateral source, the employee's losses were not replaced or indemnified.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court that worker's compensation benefits were not collateral source benefits and that the employer could assert its subrogation rights was affirmed. The cause for remanded to the trial court for trial on the merits.

State v. Bell


No. 84


Supreme Court of Tennessee


745 S.W.2d 858; 1988 Tenn. LEXIS 24



January 25, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Hamilton Criminal.

Hon. Douglas A. Meyer.



DISPOSITION:  The case is remanded to the trial court for a further hearing in accordance with the directions set forth heretofore in this opinion. Upon the conclusion of that hearing the record will be returned to this Court for such further ruling as may be required in the case.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Hamilton Criminal Court (Tennessee), which, after a jury trial, entered convictions of felony murder, burglary, and felonious assault and sentenced defendant to death for the homicide, life imprisonment on each of the felonious assault counts, and 15 years' imprisonment for burglary. Defendant claimed that the trial court erroneously allowed the state to remove black persons from the petit jury.


OVERVIEW: After a jury trial, defendant was convicted of felony murder, felonious assault, and burglary. Defendant claimed that the state purposefully used its peremptory challenges to remove blacks from the petit jury solely because they were the same race as him. The court remanded the case for a hearing to determine whether there was a purposeful racial discrimination in the state's exercise of its challenges. The trial court incorrectly denied defendant the opportunity to establish a possible discriminatory practice in jury selection because defendant, the victims, and all the principal witnesses were black. Although this was a factor that may have been considered to discount any advantage that a discriminating prosecutor might have perceived in striking blacks from the jury, there were other considerations to be taken into account to determine whether the jury selection process violated the Equal Protection Clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The trial court failed to make any finding on the threshold issue of whether defendant was able to establish a prima facie case of purposeful discrimination. The court determined that the remainder of defendant's challenges were without merit.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the case for a hearing to determine whether there was a purposeful racial discrimination in the state's exercise of its peremptory challenges. The court modified the sentences to fix the burglary sentence to run concurrently with the other sentences. The court determined that the remainder of defendant's challenges were without merit.

State v. Porterfield


No. 2


Supreme Court of Tennessee


746 S.W.2d 441; 1988 Tenn. LEXIS 8



January 19, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition to Rehear Denied February 29, 1988, Reported at: 746 S.W.2d 441 at 452. Certiorari Denied May 16, 1988, Reported at: 486 U.S. 1017.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Shelby Criminal.

Honorable Joseph B. McCartie, Judge.



DISPOSITION:  All assignments of error are overruled. The judgment of conviction in each case and the sentence imposed pursuant thereto are affirmed. The sentences will be carried out as provided by law on April 15, 1988, unless otherwise stayed or modified by appropriate authority. Costs are taxed to appellants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed judgments of Shelby Criminal Court (Tennessee), which, after a jury trial, convicted one defendant of murder in the first degree and the other of accessory before the fact to murder in the first degree and sentenced both to death under the Tennessee Death Penalty Act, Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-2-203.


OVERVIEW: Over a period of months, defendant solicited several men to kill her husband. The other defendant was convicted of murder in the first degree after the victim was found beaten to death. The wife was convicted of accessory before the fact to murder in the first degree. Both were sentenced to death under the Tennessee Death Penalty Act, Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-2-203. The court affirmed the convictions and the sentences. Although the trial court erred in admitting codefendant's unredacted confession into evidence, the error was harmless in light of the overwhelming evidence against the wife. Joinder of the cases was permissible under Tenn. R. Crim. P. 8(c)(1) where each defendant was charged with accountability for each offense included. Evidence regarding one defendant's interest in accepting a plea bargain was not relevant to the issue of punishment or to any mitigating factor raised by defendant and was properly excluded. There was no prejudice to defendant by the trial court's failure to define "torture" where evidence supported the aggravating circumstance, Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-2-203(i)(5), as defendant repeatedly struck the victim with a tire iron, inflicting horrible wounds.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed one defendant's conviction for murder in the first degree and the other defendant's conviction for accessory before the fact to murder in the first degree. The court also affirmed the death sentence for both defendants.

Huskey v. State


No. 87-5-I


Supreme Court of Tennessee


743 S.W.2d 609; 1988 Tenn. LEXIS 4



January 11, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Coffee Law.

Hon. Gerald L. Ewell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Coffee County (Tennessee), which denied the attorney's claim that the limitations on fees paid to appointed counsel contained in the statutes and court rules were unconstitutional insofar as they did not allow "just compensation" or "fair market value" for services rendered by attorneys appointed to represent indigent persons accused in criminal cases.


OVERVIEW: The attorney argued that Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 40-14-201 to 210 and Tenn. Sup. Ct. R. 13, governing fees to counsel for indigents, violated the provisions of Tenn. Const. art. I, § 21 and U.S. Const. amend. V. The court held that the services of a licensed attorney were not the type of particular services referred to in the state constitution. There was no constitutional right to compensation in representing indigent defendants by appointment of the court. Therefore, the court determined that there was nothing unconstitutional either in the statutes that authorized compensation, in the limitations contained in those statutes, or in Tenn. Sup. Ct. R. 13. The license to practice law carried with it as a condition and an obligation the rendition of public service, including service by appointment for indigents.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of the attorney's claim and remanded the matter for collection of costs and for any other orders that may have been appropriate.

 

190 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


State v. Southern Fitness & Health, Inc.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Tennessee


743 S.W.2d 160; 1987 Tenn. LEXIS 1083



December 29, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] MADISON EQUITY.

HONORABLE JOE C. MORRIS, CHANCELLOR.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state challenged a judgment from the Madison County Chancery Court (Tennessee), which declared the Tennessee Health Club Bond Act (Act), Tenn. Code Ann. § 47-18-301 et seq., violative of both the federal and state constitutions after the state filed an action seeking to enjoin appellees, health club and president, from operating in violation of the Act, and to recover any consumer loss attributable to violations of the Act.


OVERVIEW: In response to the state's action, appellees filed a motion to dismiss, alleging that the Act created legislative classifications violating the Fourteenth Amendment's equal protection clause and Tenn. Const. art. XI, § 8; that the Act was retroactive, impairing contract obligations, Tenn. Const. art. I, § 20; and that the single bond amount was arbitrary and unconstitutional. On review, the court found no fundamental right or suspect class, so it asserted that the correct test was a rational basis. The court found that the requirement of a surety bond, certificate of deposit, or irrevocable letter of credit to assure that the clubs would follow through on their consumer agreements was a rational approach. The court did not find the Act's application only to for-profit corporations arbitrary as non-profit organizations were less prone to consumer fraud. The court found that the legislature balanced a consumer's potential loss with the health club industry's degree of regulation to arrive at policy decisions, including the exemption and the single bond amount. The court found no impairment of existing contract rights because the Act was only prospective. The judgment was reversed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment, which had held that the Tennessee Health Club Bond Act as unconstitutional and had dismissed an action brought by the state. The cause was remanded for trial.

First American Nat'l Bank v. Olsen


No. 270


Supreme Court of Tennessee


751 S.W.2d 417; 1987 Tenn. LEXIS 1076



November 23, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Knox Equity

Hon. Frederick D. McDonald, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff corporate taxpayer sought review of an order of the Chancery Court of Knox County (Tennessee), which entered judgment in favor of defendant Tennessee Commissioner of Revenue, and dismissed the corporate taxpayer's suit that sought a refund of corporate excise taxes paid under protest.


OVERVIEW: A corporate taxpayer commenced suit against the Tennessee Commissioner of Revenue, and sought a refund for corporate excise taxes paid under protest. The corporate taxpayer claimed that the amended excise tax, Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 67-4-801 et seq., violated 31 U.S.C.S. § 3124(a), and impaired the obligation of a contract. The trial court disagreed and dismissed the corporate taxpayer's petition. The corporate taxpayer sought review. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held: (1) the amended excise tax was enacted to include Tennessee obligations in the measure of the tax, and the legislative intent must be upheld absent a constitutional barrier; (2) the amended excess tax did not impair the obligation of a contract because it was enacted to include Tennessee obligations; and (3) the amended excise tax did not violate 31 U.S.C.S. § 3124(a) the amended excise tax was a nondiscriminatory tax imposed on discrete property interests, even though the interest could be measured by the underlying assets, thus the tax fell within the exception to 31 U.S.C.S. § 3214(a).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court that dismissed the corporate taxpayer's suit, which sought a refund for corporate excise taxes paid under protest.

 

192 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Haywood County v. Hudson


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Tennessee, at Jackson


740 S.W.2d 718; 1987 Tenn. LEXIS 1015



November 17, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Haywood Criminal No. 1

No. 1262, Hon. Dick Jerman, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, having been charged with murder in the first degree, appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Haywood County (Tennessee), which ordered that a sample of blood be withdrawn from him for the purpose of testing to determine whether he was infected by a virus indicating the presence of AIDS.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested on charges of murder in the first degree. Upon his arrest, defendant stated to an officer that he suffered from AIDS. Defendant objected to the drawing of a sample of blood upon religious grounds, and an evidentiary hearing was held on the matter. The trial court ordered that a sample of blood be withdrawn from defendant for the purpose of testing to determine whether he was infected by a virus indicating the presence of AIDS pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 41-4-138(a). The court affirmed and remanded for further proceedings. Defendant denied that he had AIDS and testified that he represented that he had AIDS in order to threaten or frighten the agent. The testimony clearly showed that the sheriff and public health officials had reasonable cause to carry out the blood test. The operation of the jail itself, the safety of the sheriff and his staff, and the safety and welfare of other persons incarcerated in the jail are involved, and any alleged religious belief or conviction of defendant yielded to concerns for the public safety and welfare that were clearly established by the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that ordered that a blood sample be withdrawn from defendant for the purpose of testing to determine whether he was infected by a virus indicating the presence of AIDS, and the matter was remanded for further proceedings.

 

193 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Tennessee Conservation League v. Cody


No. 86-60-I


Supreme Court of Tennessee


745 S.W.2d 854; 1987 Tenn. LEXIS 974



September 21, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Reported at: 745 S.W.2d 854 at 857.


PRIOR HISTORY: DAVIDSON COUNTY

Hon. Irvin H. Kilcrease, Jr., Chancellor.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff conservation league appealed from a judgment of a Chancery Court of Davidson County (Tennessee), which declared constitutional two statutes enacted by the legislature regulating the hunting and taking of raccoons and the training of coon dogs. The league contended that the statutes were not rationally related to the constitutional purpose of preserving and protecting wildlife.


OVERVIEW: The statutes challenged by the league provided different regulations for different counties on the hunting and taking of raccoons. The court agreed with the chancellor that the provisions did not violate the constitutional prohibition on special legislation. Different regulations in different counties were justified by the different conditions prevailing in the counties. The league argued that the statutes did not protect or preserve wildlife as provided in Tenn. Const. art. XI, § 13, the constitution provision authorizing the legislature to enact legislation for the preservation and protection of game and fish. The court held that although the legislature did not choose the best means possible, the statutes were valid because they were rationally related to the constitutional purpose of protecting wildlife. The court had to leave the protection of raccoons and training of coon dogs in the hands of the Legislature so long as there was a viable causal connection between the legislative action and a constitutional purpose.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court.

 

194 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


State v. Claybrook


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Tennessee, at Jackson


736 S.W.2d 95; 1987 Tenn. LEXIS 972



September 8, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Criminal Court for Crockett County, No. 1873 Below, No. 1.

Hon. Dick Jerman, Jr., Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction by the Criminal Court for Crockett County (Tennessee) for murder in the first degree and his sentence to death by electrocution.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sentenced because he had been previously convicted of a violent felony, the murder was committed during the course of a felony, and the murder was heinous, atrocious, and cruel, all of which were aggravating circumstances in Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-2-203(i)(2), (5), (7). The court reversed, holding that the trial court improperly denied defense counsel the opportunity to separately and individually voir dire prospective jurors, out of the presence of other jurors, concerning their knowledge of defendant's prior criminal record and their pretrial knowledge of the details of the murder they would be sitting on. The trial court failed to follow the dictates of Tenn. R. Crim. P. 24(a). The court held that the trial court should have permitted the individual voir dire of the jurors once it became aware that 80 percent of the first group of prospective jurors had information regarding defendant's case. This error was not harmless but was prejudicial as set forth in Tenn. R. App. P. 36(b). The court denied defendant's claim of errors as to the trial court's refusal to suppress evidence, the admission of defendant's statement to the police, and the validity of the death penalty.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for murder in the first degree and his sentence to death by electrocution.

Swift v. Kirby


No. 86-71-I


Supreme Court of Tennessee


737 S.W.2d 271; 1987 Tenn. LEXIS 958



August 31, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Davidson Equity

Honorable Robert S. Brandt, Chancellor



DISPOSITION:  We reverse the judgment of the Court of Appeals and dismiss this lawsuit. Costs are adjudged against plaintiff Swift.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant purchasers sought review of the decision of the Court of Appeals (Tennessee), which entered judgment for plaintiff defaulter and determined that the phrase "equity of redemption" did not waive the defaulter's statutory right to redeem property sold at foreclosure under Tenn. Code Ann. § 6-8-101 et seq.


OVERVIEW: The defaulter executed a deed of trust conveying real property to secure payment on a note. He defaulted and the property was sold to the purchasers. The defaulter filed suit seeking to redeem the property in reliance upon § 66-8-101 et seq. The appellate court affirmed the trial court's decision that the defaulter had not waived the statutory right of redemption and that 1984 Tenn. Pub. Acts 774 was unconstitutional. The court reversed the appellate court's decision. The court held that the phrase "equity of redemption" embraced the statutory right of redemption.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's decision and dismissed the lawsuit.

 

196 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Dep't of Social Services v. Wright


No. 29


Supreme Court of Tennessee


736 S.W.2d 84; 1987 Tenn. LEXIS 962



August 31, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Roane Circuit.

Honorable Don T. McMurray Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner State challenged a judgment of the Roane County Circuit Court (Tennessee), which dismissed the State's petition against respondent putative father to establish his paternity under the Uniform Reciprocal Enforcement Support Act (URESA), Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-5-201, et seq. The trial court found that the application of § 36-5-219(b) to the issue of paternity contravened the putative father's right to equal protection.


OVERVIEW: The Department of Social Services for the County of St. Clair, Michigan filed, on behalf of a minor child, a "Complaint to Adjudicate Paternity Under the Uniform Reciprocal Enforcement of Support Act" against the putative father. The State of Tennessee proceeded with the action in the Tennessee trial court. The court affirmed in part and held as follows: (1) applying Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-5-219(b), which stated that a duly certified URESA petition created a presumption of the truthfulness of the facts alleged therein and prima facie evidence of the liability of the respondent and shifted the burden of proof to such respondent, to a paternity action under URESA denied URESA respondents equal protection under the law; and (2) the application of § 36-5-219(b) created an impermissible classification because Tennessee law required in-state petitioners seeking to establish paternity to carry the burden of proof while the URESA provision shifted the burden to the respondent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision to the extent that it held it unconstitutional to apply the burden shifting provision in an adjudication of paternity under URESA. The trial court's dismissal of the URESA petition was improper. This cause was remanded for further proceedings.

 

197 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Whitley v. Portland


No. 87-13-I


Supreme Court of Tennessee


1987 Tenn. LEXIS 956



August 10, 1987, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] NOT DESIGNATED FOR PUBLICATION


PRIOR HISTORY: Sumner Equity.

Hon. Tom E. Gray, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners challenged an order of the Equity Court of Sumner County (Tennessee), which held that the property owners' action challenging three ordinances of annexation was not timely filed.


OVERVIEW: The property owners filed an action challenging three annexation ordinances. The trial court held that the action was not timely filed within the meaning of Tenn. Code Ann. § 6-51-102. The court affirmed and remanded the case for the collection of costs. The property owners claimed that under the provisions of Tenn. Code Ann. § 6-51-102(b) they were entitled to bring an action within one year and thirty days after the effective date of the third ordinance. The court rejected said argument. The court found that the only grounds upon which actions could be filed by aggrieved property owners challenging the annexation were those contained in Tenn. Code Ann. § 6-51-103. Further, the court held that said actions had to be filed within thirty days after final passage of the ordinance being challenged.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order that held that the property owners' action challenging three ordinances of annexation was not timely filed. The court remanded the case for the collection of costs.

 

198 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


South Cent. Bell Tel. Co. v. Celauro


No. 86-72-I


Supreme Court of Tennessee


735 S.W.2d 228; 1987 Tenn. LEXIS 1069



August 10, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Davidson County

Hon. C. Allen High, Chancellor



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; AND REVERSED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent, Commissioner of Revenue (commissioner) and State of Tennessee (state), sought review of the decision of the trial court of Davidson County (Tennessee), which ordered payment to petitioner telephone company of a refund of the gross receipts tax and of the sales tax, holding that the end user charge was derived from interstate commerce which the legislature had exempted from both taxes.


OVERVIEW: Under protest, the telephone company paid the taxes on "end user" charges paid by local telephone customers as part of the costs of interstate long distance service. The chancellor ordered reimbursement for the telephone company, holding that the end user charge was derived from interstate commerce, which the legislature had exempted from the sales tax and the gross receipt tax. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment of the court below ordering a refund of the gross receipt tax and reversed the judgment ordering a refund of the sales tax. The court held that the income had been generated from interstate commerce because the Federal Communications Commission (FCC) ordered the charges as a means of making all customers share in the costs of interstate service. The court held that the state could collect the sales tax on the end user charges because local subscribers had paid the end user charges for the use of the local telephone system in interstate commerce. Therefore the taxed activity had a substantial nexus to the state, was apportioned to the state by the FCC, did not discriminate against interstate commerce, and related to services provided within the state.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the court below ordering respondents to pay to the telephone company a refund of the gross receipts tax and reversed the judgment ordering a refund of the sales tax.

 

199 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


McFaddin v. Jackson


No. 73


Supreme Court of Tennessee


738 S.W.2d 176; 1987 Tenn. LEXIS 933



July 27, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition to Rehear Denied October 12, 1987, Reported at: 738 S.W.2d 176 at 182.


PRIOR HISTORY: Sullivan Equity.

Honorable Richard E. Ladd Chancellor.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Commissioner of Revenue, State of Tennessee, sought review of the decision of the trial court (Tennessee), which held that plaintiff taxpayer did not owe certain estate taxes paid under protest in her suit to recover those monies paid pursuant to 1978 Tenn. Pub. Acts ch. 731 from the commissioner.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer filed suit to recover estate taxes paid on certain accounts in her spouse's estate pursuant to 1978 Tenn. Pub. Acts ch. 731, which provided that the account balances in question would not be subject to state tax if they were exempt from federal estate tax. At the time ch. 731 was enacted, the spouse's accounts were not subject to federal estate tax; however at the time of the her spouse's death, they were subject to federal taxation pursuant to an amendment to I.R.C. § 2039. In finding that the taxpayer did not owe the tax, the trial court held that the legislature did not intend to incorporate future amendments to the Internal Revenue Code into the statute, and that such an intent would constitute an improper delegation of legislative power. The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, interpreting the term "may be or become effective" in the statute as an express intent to include future amendments into the body of the statute. The court held that there had been no unconstitutional delegation of legislative power, because the contingency that would trigger the tax was one enacted by the sovereign power, rather than the will of the voters.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, dismissed the taxpayer's suit, and adjudged costs against the estate of the taxpayer's spouse.

 

200 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Bemis Pentecostal Church v. State


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Tennessee


731 S.W.2d 897; 1987 Tenn. LEXIS 1064



May 26, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] MADISON EQUITY No. 8.

Hon. Joe C. Morris, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION:  Judgment of Court of Appeals Reversed; Judgment of Trial Court Reinstated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff churches filed an action challenging the constitutionality of the Campaign Financial Disclosure Act of 1980 (Act), Tenn. Code Ann. § 2-10-101 et seq. Defendants, a state and its officials, sought review of the judgment of the Tennessee Court of Appeals that reversed the trial court's judgment and held that the Act burdened free speech and, absent any compelling state interest, was thus unconstitutional as applied to referenda elections.


OVERVIEW: The churches had participated in a campaign opposing the adoption of on-premises liquor consumption in a referendum measure but failed to file disclosure statements regarding their contributions as required by the terms of the Act. The churches alleged that the Act violated their First and Fourteenth Amendment rights under the Constitution of the United States. The trial court found that the Act was constitutional, and the court agreed, reversing the judgment of the appeals court. The court held that the Act was subject to a strict scrutiny standard of review and that, as enacted, it did not control the quality or content of speech or limit contributions or expenditures made during a campaign. The Act was neutral in all respects with regard to the groups to whom it applied and the types of activities at which it was specifically aimed. The court determined that the Act served a number of legitimate and compelling state interests, including the maintenance of free, open, and fair elections, the dissemination of campaign information to voters, and the prevention of corruption and fraud. The court concluded that the organizational burdens imposed by the Act were minimal.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the appeals court that held that the Act was unconstitutional and reinstated the judgment of the trial court. The costs were divided equally among the parties.
